4\. [Predestination]{.class_s35U}---[never a reference to a lost man. ]{.class_s35U}Although a lost sinner's destination is the Lake of Fire, he can change it at any time by receiving Jesus Christ. [No saint is predestinated to go to Heaven until he gets saved]{.class_s35U} (Rom. 8:28--30 and comments in that Commentary).

5\. [Reprobation]{.class_s35U}---no reference at all to any "eternal decree" of damnation. The reprobation that took place in Romans 1, took place [in time]{.class_s35U}, not eternity. The word [reprobate]{.class_s35U} in the New Testament may refer to the lost condition of a man (2 Cor. 13:5--7), but there is never any hint whatsoever that that condition is [irreversible]{.class_s35U}.

In fact, the term [reprobation]{.class_s35U} means that a person or group of people is being placed on probation [again]{.class_s35U}. That is, God gave them an opportunity under one system of salvation; they failed under [that ]{.class_s35U}system, so God gave them another chance under [another ]{.class_s35U}system.

["But was manifest in these last times for you."]{.class_s35V} The words ["last times"]{.class_s35V} in verse 20 throw all the Fundamentalists for a loop. All of the Fundamental and Conservative Bible teachers will tell you that the ["last days"]{.class_s35V} or the ["last times"]{.class_s35V} began with the birth of Jesus Christ and last for 2,000 plus years until the Second Advent. They get that from verse 20 and Hebrews 1:2.

Both Peter and Paul make it perfectly clear that ["the last days"]{.class_s35V} were [future prophecy ]{.class_s35U}(2 Tim. 3:1; 2 Pet. 3:3). Peter places ["the last days"]{.class_s35V} as immediately preceding the return of Jesus Christ and ending with the dissolution of the earth (2 Pet. 3:3--10). Well, if that's so, what do you do with a verse like 1 Peter 1:20?

Now, I have discussed this matter in detail in my comments on Hebrews 1:2. The fact of the matter is that from Christ's baptism to Stephen's martyrdom in Acts 7, everything is set up by God so that [both]{.class_s35U} advents could have taken place. That is why Christ speaks to His disciples after His resurrection about ["the kingdom of God"]{.class_s35V} in regards to the restoration of the earthly Davidic kingdom (Acts 1:3--6). That is why Peter quotes Joel 2 in Acts 2. That's why he talks about Israel's sins being blotted out at the Second Advent (Acts 3:19). That is why the Body of Christ is not revealed and ["the gospel of the grace of God"]{.class_s35V} (Acts 20:24; 1 Cor. 15:1--4; Gal. 1:6--9) is not preached until after Acts 7 (see comments in that Commentary).

["The last days"]{.class_s35V} are right there in Acts 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7. The Lord gives Israel one more chance to receive Jesus as the Christ. When the Jews [reject ]{.class_s35U}the message of Stephen, God puts off Daniel's Seventieth Week for nearly[ 2,000 years.]{.class_s35U}

So what you have in 1 Peter 1:20 is another of those places where there is a [double application]{.class_s35U} to the verse. If you make the ["last times"]{.class_s35V} the crucifixion of Christ (see the context), then you have the resurrection chronologically in verse 21, followed by the ascension (["and gave him glory"]{.class_s35V}).

Hebrews 1:3 says, speaking of Christ, ["Who being the brightness of his glory\...when he had by himself purged our sins, sat down on the right hand of the Majesty on high."]{.class_s35V}

Paul said in 1 Timothy 3:16 that Christ was ["received up into glory."]{.class_s35V} In that verse, ["glory"]{.class_s35V} is more than a reference to Heaven; it is the state of being in which God dwells. John 17:24 (Jesus speaking):[ "Father, I will that they also, whom thou hast given me, be with me where I am"]{.class_s35V} (there's Glory as a place: Heaven) ["that they may behold my glory, which thou hast given me"]{.class_s35V} (and there's the attribute of God).

But the ["last times"]{.class_s35V} could just as well refer to the times before, and including, the Second Advent. Look at 2 Thessalonians 1:7--10. In verse 8, you have the death, burial, and resurrection just like 1 Peter 1:21 (["the GOSPEL of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class_s35V}), and in verses 9--10 you have the glory given to Jesus Christ at His Advent.

In fact, throughout 1 Peter, the glory of Christ is directly associated with the Advent. First Peter 4:13, ["But rejoice, inasmuch as ye are partakers of Christ's sufferings; that, when his glory SHALL []{#c16C.xhtml_page_234}BE REVEALED." ]{.class_s35V}That's future; that's the Second Coming. First Peter 5:1, ["the glory that SHALL BE REVEALED."]{.class_s35V} First Peter 5:4, ["When the chief Shepherd shall appear, ye shall receive a crown of GLORY."]{.class_s35V} In 2 Peter 1:17, you have a reference to the glory given to Christ on the mount of Transfiguration, which was a picture of the Second Coming (2 Pet. 1:19). The Second Advent is connected with the glory given to Christ all throughout 1 and 2 Peter.

Notice in verse 21 that belief in God is not enough. [Mohammed doesn't win, place, or show. ]{.class_s35U}The belief of Mohammed in "monotheism" is the belief of a [devil ]{.class_s35U}(James 2:19). It is the belief in God ["by him"]{.class_s35V}; i.e., [by Jesus]{.class_s35U} Christ. John 14:6, ["Jesus saith unto him, I am the way, the truth, and the life: NO MAN COMETH UNTO THE FATHER, BUT BY ME."]{.class_s35V}

Moreover, it is belief in the God ["that raised him]{.class_s35V} \[Jesus\][ up from the dead."]{.class_s35V} Romans 10:9, ["That if thou shalt confess with thy mouth the Lord Jesus, and shalt believe in thine heart that ]{.class_s35V}[God hath raised him from the dead]{.class_s363-0}[, thou shalt be saved."]{.class_s35V}

Mohammed didn't even believe that Jesus [died ]{.class_s35U}on the cross, much less rose [from the dead.]{.class_s35U}

Verses 22 is one of those verses that Campbellites use to prove you're washed from your sins in the baptismal pool. They would say that ["the truth"]{.class_s35V} that you obey to purify your soul is getting baptized.

There's no water within twenty-one verses, either way, of verse 22. In fact, 1 Peter 1 is so dry that the grass is withering in verse 24.

["Obeying the truth"]{.class_s35V} to purify your soul is believing (faith---vs. 21) what the Scriptures say (vs. 23) about []{#c16C.xhtml_page_235 .class-1}["the precious blood of Christ"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 19). Paul calls it ["obedience to the FAITH"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 1:5, 16:26 and comments on those verses in that Commentary), [not]{.class_s35U} obedience to water baptism.

If you don't exercise faith and belief in the blood atonement, you don't [obey]{.class_s35U}, no matter what you do. You can repent, confess, believe, and be baptized; and you will go straight to Hell. You can [repent ]{.class_s35U}and [confess ]{.class_s35U}Christ like Judas Iscariot. You can [believe ]{.class_s35U}and get baptized like Simon the Sorcerer. Both were unsaved and ended up in Hell.

There is only one thing that you[ can't do]{.class_s35U} and go to Hell. [You can't put your personal faith in the shed blood of Jesus Christ to save your soul and go to Hell. ]{.class_s35U}You can't do it. That's ["obeying the truth."]{.class_s35V} Anything short of the blood atonement is [not]{.class_s35U} obedience.

You can pray, you can be baptized to have original sin removed, you can speak in tongues as the initial evidence of the baptism of the Holyghost, you can join the church Christ founded, you can study the Bible until your eyeballs fall out. But until you place your trust only in the [blood of Jesus]{.class_s35U} shed on Calvary, you are a [child of disobedience]{.class_s35U} (Eph. 2:2) and under the wrath of God (Eph. 2:3).

One more time with feeling: ["see that ye love one another with a pure heart fervently."]{.class_s35V} How do you get ["a pure heart,"]{.class_s35V} Peter? Acts 15:9, spoken by the man who wrote 1 Peter 1:22, ["And put no difference between us and them, purifying their hearts BY FAITH."]{.class_s35V} He went on to say in Acts 15:11, ["But we believe that ]{.class_s35V}[through the grace of the Lord Jesus Christ]{.class_s363-0}[ we shall be saved, even as they."]{.class_s35V}

That's Ephesians 2:8--9. It's ["grace\...through faith."]{.class_s35V} Water baptism had nothing to do with it.

["Unto unfeigned love of the brethren, see that ye love one another."]{.class_s35V} That word ["unfeigned"]{.class_s35V} means that you're not [pretending ]{.class_s35U}to love someone: your love is real. In other words, if you have obeyed the truth, and if you have purified your soul, you will [sincerely ]{.class_s35U}love your brothers and sisters in Christ.

That is one of the evidences of the New Birth (vs. 23). John says, ["We know that we have passed from death unto life, because we love the brethren"]{.class_s35V} (1 John 3:14).

One of the ways that you can destroy your assurance of salvation is to gossip and complain about the brethren, always find fault with them, never forgive them, never pray for them, grow bitter toward them, etc. That's not [loving ]{.class_s35U}the brethren, and it will make you doubt your salvation.

Now, nobody knows better about the faults of the saints than I do. I have seen the saints commit nearly every sin a person can commit, outside of a sex murder. I have been hurt by the saints, I have been lied to by the saints, I have been divorced by the saints, I have been threatened and sued by the saints.

But as God as my witness, I would rather hang around a bunch of Christians than [any ]{.class_s35U}of my old buddies from the unsaved days. Knowing what Christians are like hasn't changed [that]{.class_s35U}. The saints have been a blessing to me, and I thank God for them. I can't say that I like [every one]{.class_s35U} of them or that I can have fellowship with every one of them. But I do love them, and you should too.

People think that because I "skin the brethren alive" when I preach, that I'm "not showing any love." []{#c16C.xhtml_page_237}That's because they've been brainwashed by the "glass toilet" (the TV), and they respond to the tone of my voice much as my German Shepherd would. But I do love the brethren. If I didn't, I wouldn't preach against their sins. I would preach on "coping and sharing" and "family values" and let them hit a bonfire at the Judgment Seat of Christ.

I don't hate people like Gary Hudson and Curtis Hutson and Fred Afman and Bob Jones Jr. and Bob Jones III and John R. Rice. I'll call their hand on their [lying ]{.class_s35U}and [disbelief ]{.class_s35U}in the word of God, but I don't [hate]{.class_s35U} them. I pray for them, and I pray that God will use them. I sure do. [I hope God uses every one of them. ]{.class_s35U}And if the Lord uses [them ]{.class_s35U}more than he uses me, I think that's just great. I have nothing personal against any of them. I just can't take how they treat the Book; that's all.

I used to get on Jack Hyles, when John R. Rice was alive, about Hyles-Anderson College's stand on the Bible. Their faculty and staff corrected the [AV]{.class_s35U} just like the faculties at BJU and Tennessee Temple. But a few years after Rice died, Hyles came out and made a public stand for the [KJV]{.class_s35U} and straightened out the teachers at his college.

When he did that, I made a public retraction in the [Bible Believers' Bulletin]{.class_s35U} of everything I had ever said about him. After all, my "beef" wasn't with Hyles [personally]{.class_s35U}.

A few years later, he got into some hot water over a secretary, and Bobbie Scumner published a bunch of foul-mouthed gossip about him in his rag [The Biblical Evangelist. ]{.class_s35U}I kept my mouth shut about it. If you love someone, you don't [believe ]{.class_s35U}the worst about him. If the []{#c16C.xhtml_page_238}worst [is ]{.class_s35U}true, you don't try to smear his reputation across the entire countryside.

I wrote Hyles a letter and gave him some verses that had helped me when I was "under the gun." A graduate of PBI and an associate of Hyles, Jack Patterson, even tried to get the two of us together.

You say, "Would you have met with him?" Sure I would. I would have sat down with him and tried to encourage him in the Lord. [He was my brother in Christ.]{.class_s35U}

You see, I have a lot more grace when it comes to the brethren than the brethren have toward [me]{.class_s35U}. The Lord has been too good to me for me to go around holding a grudge against [anyone]{.class_s35U}.

And now, some great verses on the word of God.

23 Being born again, not of corruptible seed, but of incorruptible, by the word of God, which liveth and abideth for ever.

24 For all flesh is as grass, and all the glory of man as the flower of grass. The grass withereth, and the flower thereof falleth away:

25 But the word of the Lord endureth for ever. And this is the word which by the gospel is preached unto you.

Your ["seed"]{.class_s35V} is ["corruptible."]{.class_s35V} It will bring death to your children someday, if the Lord tarries. You will die because your [daddy's seed]{.class_s35U} was corruptible. Your daddy died (or will die) because [his daddy's seed]{.class_s35U} was corruptible. It goes all the way back to Adam.

But when you are ["born again,"]{.class_s35V} you are born of something that will never die, rot, or grow old (["of incorruptible"]{.class_s35V}). What is it? [It's the Book!]{.class_s35U}[ ]{.class_s36E}["By the word of God, which liveth and abideth for ever."]{.class_s35V}

Somebody says, "Well, that's the incarnate Word. It's the Lord Jesus Christ. The [King James]{.class_s35U} should have capitalized the[ w.]{.class_s35U}"

No, it's not! Look at verse 25. It is ["the word which by the gospel is preached unto you."]{.class_s35V} Those are [spoken words]{.class_s35U} which are read (or quoted) from a Book.

James 1:21 says, ["Receive with meekness the engrafted word, which is able to save your souls."]{.class_s35V} Then it's [not ]{.class_s35U}Christ. A Christian is baptized [into]{.class_s35U} Christ's Body (1 Cor. 12:13); [Christ is not grafted onto him. ]{.class_s35U}The Holy Spirit takes possession of the body (1 Cor. 6:19--20); He's not an addendum to it.

In verse 23, the word of God is incorruptible ["seed."]{.class_s35V} In the context, that seed is like the "seed" of a man. But when Peter first heard the analogy, the seed was like the seed of a plant. In Luke 8, the Lord told the parable of the sower. In Luke 8:11, He said, ["The seed is the word of God."]{.class_s35V} So when you get down to verse 24 of 1 Peter 1, you run into ["grass."]{.class_s35V}

So not only is the word of God likened to the [seed ]{.class_s35U}of God that brings about a new birth, it is likened to the seed that is sown by the Lord that causes a barren field (the human heart) to bring forth life and fruitfulness to God.

Now, all of that means this: you can't receive Jesus Christ as your Saviour and put your faith in the blood atonement apart from [the Scriptures. ]{.class_s35U}They are inseparably connected with each other. Paul said, ["So then faith cometh by hearing, and hearing by the word of God. ]{.class_s35V}(Rom. 10:17).

You have got to accept what the Bible [says ]{.class_s35U}about Jesus Christ and the blood atonement to be saved.

That is what is wrong with the Catholics, the Jehovah's Witnesses, the Mormons, the Charismatics, and every professing "Christian" who is trying to work his way to Heaven. [Every one of them depart from what the Scriptures say about either Jesus Christ or salvation or both.]{.class_s35U}

Groups like the Jehovah's Witnesses and the Mormons believe on Jesus Christ. Sure they do; if you don't believe me, just ask one of them. THEY JUST DON'T BELIEVE WHAT THE BIBLE [SAYS ]{.class_s35U}ABOUT JESUS CHRIST.

You take Catholics. They believe that Jesus is God and the Son of God, but when it comes to receiving Christ as Saviour, they don't do it the way the Bible says to do it. They think swallowing a [starchy wafer ]{.class_s35U}and drinking a chalice of [hootch ]{.class_s35U}is receiving Christ. THAT'S [NOT ]{.class_s35U}HOW YOU DO IT (John 1:12).

Notice once again how Peter completely screws up the neat dispensational compartments of the "Dry Cleaners." ["Being born again."]{.class_s35V} That's present tense. [It's not the future rebirth of Israel. ]{.class_s35U}Furthermore, ["the gospel"]{.class_s35V} of verse 25 is [not ]{.class_s35U}the ["gospel of the kingdom."]{.class_s35V} It's ["the gospel"]{.class_s35V} of Christ's blood atonement (vs. 19) and resurrection (vs. 21).

["By the word of God, which LIVETH."]{.class_s35V} The Scriptures are alive. Hebrews 4:12 says, ["For the word of God is quick."]{.class_s35V} That word ["quick"]{.class_s35V} is another word for [living.]{.class_s35U}

When Paul was in prison in Rome, he wrote Timothy and said, ["Wherein I suffer trouble, as an evil doer, even unto bonds; but the word of God is not bound"]{.class_s35V} (2 Tim. 2:9). Paul couldn't unlock his stocks and []{#c16C.xhtml_page_241}walk out of that cell, but the word of God could. Why? [Because it was alive; it was living.]{.class_s35U}

I have read the account of a prison chaplain from South Carolina named Jack Orr. Jack Orr walked "the last mile" to the death chair with thirty-one men. According to the testimony of Jack Orr, a small, black Bible appeared, without exception, in the cell of each one of the dead men, either under the mattress or on the floor under his bunk immediately [after ]{.class_s35U}his execution. [Before ]{.class_s35U}the execution, that same Bible was taken to the office of the prison chaplain and [locked in a drawer. ]{.class_s35U}It always disappeared and was always found after the doomed man died, in his cell.

Now, I don't know how that happened. I wouldn't even hazard a guess. But naturally (providentially through men) or supernaturally, that Bible went from a locked drawer to the locked cell of a condemned prisoner. And though I have no idea how it got there, I do know this: [the Bible is a living Book.]{.class_s35U}

Of course, it doesn't [look ]{.class_s35U}that way. It looks like it's only ink on paper, [just like any other book. ]{.class_s35U}But the Bible has a Spirit in it that other books don't have. The Spirit that lives in that Book is the same Spirit that lives in the body of a Christian, and it's the same Spirit that pricks the conscience of the unsaved man and convicts him of his sins. It's the [Holy Spirit]{.class_s35U}, the Spirit of Christ. When a man picks up that Bible, whether it's a saved man being led by the Spirit or an unsaved man under the conviction of the Spirit,[ the Spirit in that Book bears witness to the Holy Spirit who is working in that man. ]{.class_s35U}That is why that Book "has your number," and it speaks to you [personally]{.class_s35U}.

I found that out before I got saved. When I was twenty-seven years old, I was sitting in a bar in []{#c16C.xhtml_page_242}Pensacola, and I was at the end of my rope. I had all of my life I could stand, and I was ready to "check out." I made up my mind to get a gun and blow my brains out. I wasn't going to leave any note saying, "Good-bye cruel world," or anything that dramatic. I was just going to stick the muzzle in my mouth and pull the trigger.

As I got up to pay my check, I heard a voice tell me, "YOU NEED TO GET A BIBLE." There was no one behind me, and the fellow in front of me hadn't said anything. I thought I had too many beers and attributed it to "hearing things." [Then I heard it again.]{.class_s35U}

Well, I grew up in a family where you did what you were told. If I was told to get a Bible, I would get a Bible. I broke into a flop house where some drunk was passed out, and I stole me a Bible.

When I got it back to my room, I said to myself, "Now, if this Book is more than any other kind of a book, wherever I open it, it will speak to me [personally]{.class_s35U}." Boy, was [that]{.class_s35U} ever an understatement. I opened it up and put my finger down (Bible roulette!). There was Ezekiel 28:1--10. ["Behold, thou art wiser than Daniel; there is no secret that they can hide from thee\...but thou shalt be a man, and no God, in the hand of him that slayeth thee."]{.class_s35V}

I slammed that Bible and threw it across the room, where it landed under the dresser. When I recovered from my shock, I said to myself, "You crazy nut, what are you getting upset about? It's just a[ book!]{.class_s35U} It's just [ink on paper."]{.class_s35U} But every time I would pick it up and read it, it would slam [me]{.class_s35U}, it would slam my life, it would slam my [thoughts]{.class_s35U}, it would slam my [habits]{.class_s35U}, it would slam my[ self-righteousness. ]{.class_s35U}That Book had me so on edge that I lost twenty pounds in four weeks.

That Book was [alive]{.class_s35U}, and it had a hold on me like a pit bull mauling a kitten. But that's what I needed at the time, see. I needed to be told that I was completely helpless and hopeless before the Lord could send Hugh Pyle to lead me to Christ. That's what that Bible did: it stripped me of everything I held dear (even to the point of my clothes and eyeglasses) and let me know in no uncertain terms that I was headed for Hell. That Book was [alive]{.class_s35U}, and it knew me better than I knew myself.

The Bible is not only alive, it ["abideth for ever."]{.class_s35V} Verse 25 says, ["But the word of the Lord endureth for ever."]{.class_s35V}

The Psalmist said, ["For ever, O LORD, thy word is settled in heaven"]{.class_s35V} (Psa. 119:89). Jesus said, ["Heaven and earth shall pass away, but my words shall not pass away"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 24:35).

If you hold a Bible in your hand, you are holding something that will be around after ["the elements shall melt with fervent heat"]{.class_s35V} (2 Pet. 3:10). That Bible says, ["For, behold, I create new heavens and a new earth: and the former shall not be remembered, nor come into mind"]{.class_s35V} (Isa. 65:17). All traces of this present creation will be gone and forgotten, except one. The only thing that will be in Heaven that will even recall the world as it is now will be [the Book.]{.class_s35U}

Verses 24--25 are a quote from Isaiah 40:6--8. The ["grass"]{.class_s35V} is a reference to all plant life.

He says, ["all flesh is as grass."]{.class_s35V} If there is any doubt about what he is talking about there, the original quote from Isaiah 40:7 clears it up: ["Surely THE PEOPLE is grass."]{.class_s35V}

So men are like [grass]{.class_s35U}. You can get a good sermon out of that. Look up the characteristics of the different kinds []{#c16C.xhtml_page_244}of grasses (Augustine, Johnson, Zoysia, etc.), and you will see the different kinds of men.

He adds, ["and all the glory of man as the flower of grass."]{.class_s35V} All the things that man builds (the pyramids, Stonehenge, the Eiffel Tower, the Great Wall of China, the Empire State Building, the Taj Mahal) and everything that man creates (music, art, science, etc.) are like the flowers.

Now, in what way is man like the grass and his glory like the flowers? Well, it isn't in their [splendor]{.class_s35U}. Christ says, ["Consider the lilies of the field, how they grow; they toil not, neither do they spin: And yet I say unto you, That even Solomon in all his glory was not arrayed like one of these"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 6:28--29).

Nothing [man ]{.class_s35U}does is comparable with anything [God ]{.class_s35U}does. No camera on earth can compete with the human eye; no computer built by anybody comes anywhere close to the human brain. Man can only [imitate ]{.class_s35U}what God does; he can't [duplicate ]{.class_s35U}it. Clones came from something God did.

There are 900 theme and amusement parks in this country, and they bring in 161 million visitors every year. [That's the glory of man]{.class_s35U}. But there are only 388 national parks, most of them featuring natural wonders and beauty, and they have 360 million visitors each year. That's a testimony; did you know that? That's a testimony to the fact that more people would rather see something [God ]{.class_s35U}made than something [man ]{.class_s35U}put together.

The way that man is like the grass is in the brevity of his life. David said, ["As for man, his days are as grass: as a flower of the field, so he flourisheth. For the wind passeth over it, and it is gone; and the place thereof shall know it no more"]{.class_s35V} (Psa. []{#c16C.xhtml_page_245}103:15--16). Isaiah 51:12 says, ["Who art thou, that thou shouldest be afraid of a man that shall die, and of the son of man which shall be made as grass."]{.class_s35V}

When Christ compares men to grass, He says, ["If God so clothe the grass of the field, which to day is, and to morrow is CAST INTO THE OVEN"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 6:30). [That's a reference to Hell]{.class_s35U} (Matt. 13:42). When James applies the allusion to the wicked rich in the Tribulation, he says they will burn at the Second Advent of Christ (James 1:10--11 cf. 2 Pet. 1:19; 2 Thess. 1:8).

Now, a flower's life is brief. All around the Gulf Coast, people have azalea bushes. Most people plant them like a hedge around their fences or houses. They aren't really much to look at, except in the Spring. Sometime around the beginning of March, buds will pop out on those things. About two weeks later, every branch on that bush will be in bloom. The thing is just covered with blossoms.

But they don't last long; [they hardly last two weeks. ]{.class_s35U}Then every flower on that bush wilts and falls off and makes a mushy, ugly mess around the bottom of that plant.

You people from up North see a similar thing with your trees every year. Every Spring, new leaves come out on those trees, and from April to September those things are just as green as can be. But around the middle of October, the leaves change from green to bright yellow, red, and orange. Then they get all dried and brown and fall off until that tree is so barren that you think it is dead.

When I was in school, we memorized a poem where every stanza ended with "And where are the snows of []{#c16C.xhtml_page_246}yesteryear?" They're gone; they're melted away. They ain't comin' back!

A man enters this world and flourishes and blossoms in his own glory for a while; then he dies and goes to Hell. That's how man is like [the grass.]{.class_s35U}

[A saved man's case is different. ]{.class_s35U}He has come to the eternal word and has believed the Gospel (vs. 25). He has done the will of God in regards to getting eternal life, and he will live forever (1 John 2:17; 2 Pet. 3:9; 1 Tim. 2:4). Therefore he is like[ a tree of life]{.class_s35U} planted by God next to [the water of life]{.class_s35U}, and ["his leaf also shall not wither"]{.class_s35V} (Psa. 1:3).

[]{#c1MX.xhtml}

## Chapter 2 {.heading_s3A-1}

2:1 Wherefore laying aside all malice, and all guile, and hypocrisies, and envies, and all evil speakings,

2 As newborn babes, desire the sincere milk of the word, that ye may grow thereby:

3 If so be ye have tasted that the Lord is gracious.

["Wherefore"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 1). That is, in light of the fact that you have something that is ["incorruptible,"]{.class_s35V} that won't wither or fall away, and that is permanent (1 Pet. 1:23--25), then you should do the following:

The first thing is ["Laying aside all malice, and all guile, and hypocrisies, and envies, and all evil speakings."]{.class_s35V} So the first thing you need to do is get rid of some things.

Notice, once again, that you are in "Pauline territory." The Apostle Paul told his converts to put off the old nature and to put away certain works (Eph. 4). He said, ["Let all bitterness, and wrath, and anger, and clamour, and evil speakin, be put away from you, with all malice"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 4:31). He said in Colossians 3:8--9, ["But now ye also put off all these; anger, wrath, malice, blashemy, filthy communication out of your mouth. Lie not one to another, seeing that ye have put off the old man with his deeds."]{.class_s35V}

Now, Peter says to lay aside ["malice."]{.class_s35V} Malice is ill will toward another person. You do something just for the purpose of messing someone up. It's akin to hatred.

["Guile."]{.class_s35V} Guile is double-talk, double-dealing, manipulating, politicking, trickery. [Politicians ]{.class_s35U}are the []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_248}best example of it. A politician will go to one group and tell them what they want to hear in order to get their votes. Then he'll go to another group and tell them something exactly the opposite to what he told the other group, but he'll say it in such a way that it doesn't sound like he contradicted himself. He is "equivocating" just to get elected.

It's like the politician who was questioned on a particular issue and replied, "Well, some of my friends are for it, and some of my friends are against it, and I always stand [with my friends."]{.class_s35U} What did he actually say about the subject? He didn't say anything! That's [guile.]{.class_s35U}

["Hypocrisies."]{.class_s35V} That's pretending to be something that you are not. Most people associate it with [profession]{.class_s35U}. They identify a hypocrite as one who doesn't live up to his [profession]{.class_s35U}. But by that definition everyone in the world is a hypocrite to some extent. There is nobody who completely lives up to what he professes to believe, especially in matters of morals and ethics, and right and wrong; unless he has the moral standards of an alley cat.

Hypocrisy goes beyond [profession]{.class_s35U}. It has to do with [why]{.class_s35U} you do [what]{.class_s35U} you do: your motive. A hypocrite will study the Bible to find an alibi to do what he wants; [not to learn the Book. ]{.class_s35U}He will come to prayer meeting just to "make contacts." To a hypocrite, church is a social club, not a place where you expose yourself to the teaching and preaching of the word of God.

A hypocrite is one who is not sincere in his [motivation]{.class_s35U}. A person may be a devil in the way he lives and yet not be a hypocrite. He may not live up to what he professes and yet not be a hypocrite. If he is sincere and straight forward and consistent, he is not a hypocrite.

[Hitler]{.class_s35U}, for instance, was not a hypocrite. He was a demon-possessed egomaniac, but he was [not ]{.class_s35U}a hypocrite. You knew exactly where he was coming from and exactly what he wanted to do and why. That is why the German people voted him [down ]{.class_s35U}twice.

It took a real hypocrite to set up the Third Reich, and it wasn't Hitler. [It was Franz Von Papen. ]{.class_s35U}He was connected with the [papal authority of Rome,]{.class_s35U} and under [Vatican orders,]{.class_s35U} he dissolved the [Catholic Center Party. ]{.class_s35U}This allowed the Nazi party, with Hitler as its head, to come to power in Germany (see the chapter on "Hellish Mother Whore" in [The History of the New Testament Church,]{.class_s35U} Vol. 2, Bible Baptist Bookstore, 1984). But through political maneuvering and subterfuge, Von Papen managed to "get off the hook" after the war. While other Nazi leaders were hung or imprisoned for their "honesty," [Von Papen was released on a few technicalities. ]{.class_s35U}That's what you call a ["cheap opportunist": a hypocrite.]{.class_s35U}

["Envies."]{.class_s35V} Normally we equate envy with jealousy, but it is a little bit different. It is possible to have ["godly jealousy"]{.class_s35V} (2 Cor. 11:2). In fact, one of the names of God, in the Scriptures, is ["Jealous"]{.class_s35V} (Exod. 34:14). But [envy ]{.class_s35U}is never spoken of in a good light; it is always bad. That is because envy is a malicious, covetous form of [jealousy]{.class_s35U}. Paul lists it as one of ["the works of the flesh"]{.class_s35V} which will cause you to lose your inheritance in the Millennial kingdom (Gal. 5:19--21).

["And all evil speakings."]{.class_s35V} That would include lies (Eph. 4:25). It would include ["blasphemy"]{.class_s35V} and ["filthy communications"]{.class_s35V} (Col. 3:8). It would include false teachers who speak ["perverse things, to draw away disciples after them"]{.class_s35V} (Acts 20:30). It is []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_250}associated with loud, angry arguments (Eph. 4:31). It is also ["foolish talking"]{.class_s35V} and ["jesting, which are not convenient"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 5:4). And of course, it would include gossip, ladies (1 Tim. 5:13).

The second thing you should do, after laying aside those sins, is ["as newborn babes, desire the sincere milk of the word"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 2). When you get saved, you become a son of God (John 1:12). You are made a son of God by [two operations. ]{.class_s35U}The first is the [New Birth,]{.class_s35U} and the second is [adoption]{.class_s35U}. When you are born again, the Holy Spirit comes into you and brings new life (regeneration) to the dead spirit with which you were born. So spiritually (i.e., in your new nature), you are like a new baby, and you are to ["grow in grace, and in the knowledge of our Lord and Saviour Jesus Christ"]{.class_s35V} (2 Pet. 3:18). You are not to stay a baby all of your Christian life (1 Cor. 3:1--3; Heb. 5:12--14).

But when you are saved, you are also [adopted ]{.class_s35U}(Gal. 4:4--5). When the Lord adopts you as a son, He legally owns you as His child, and He gives you the privileges of a grown son. Though you may be a baby [spiritually]{.class_s35U}, you can still come into God's throne room and speak to Him personally (Heb. 4:16). Well, a baby can't do that. All he can do is cry and hope you guess right as to what he wants. But you are not merely a spirit, you are also a body and soul. That soul contains the will and intellect, and they have developed much further than a baby by the time you get saved. That is why you get the privileges of an adult through [adoption]{.class_s35U}.

But [spiritually]{.class_s35U}, you need to grow, and if a baby is to grow, he needs [milk]{.class_s35U}. The Bible is the Christian's spiritual food; it's a complete diet. It's like [bread]{.class_s35U} (Matt. 4:4); it's like [apples]{.class_s35U} (Prov. 25:11); it's like [honey]{.class_s35U} (Psa. 19:10); []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_251}it's like [meat]{.class_s35U} (Heb. 5:12); and here, it's like [milk. ]{.class_s35U}That's everything you need to be healthy and strong, spiritually. Those foods represent carbohydrates for energy, protein for strength, and vitamins and minerals for maintenance.

The only thing a baby needs to do is [grow]{.class_s35U}. He doesn't need to worry about his bank account or his car or his house payment or his job. He just needs to [grow]{.class_s35U}. And to grow properly, that child needs to eat, and he needs to sleep. That's all a baby does: [eat and sleep.]{.class_s35U}

So a baby Christian should do two things: he should get into the word and [learn ]{.class_s35U}the very basic things from the Scriptures, and he should [rest ]{.class_s35U}in the promises of God. And if you don't do those two things, you won't [grow]{.class_s35U}. If you are always worried and upset about your salvation and whether you have lost it, you aren't resting in the promises of God as you should, and you haven't grown properly in your Christian life.

Likewise, the main reason that a lot of Christians don't grow is that they don't get[ into the word of God. ]{.class_s35U}If you do any personal work at all, you know that there are Christians who are saved and know it and are faithful in church and serving God. Those are the ones who, early in their Christian lives, got into the Scriptures and [grew]{.class_s35U}. Then there a lot of Christians (and in the United States it is the majority of Christians) who got saved, but they never darken the door of a church except around Christmas and Easter (if that often). They will talk to you with their beer in hand, smoking their cigarette, with the TV or radio (playing rock or country music) blaring in the background. Occasionally they will put a "hell" or a "damn" in the conversation.

A lot of my preacher brethren will look at those people and swear they weren't [saved]{.class_s35U}. But I don't believe that. I []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_252}think there will be all kinds of people in Heaven. I think a lot of those people are as saved as I am. But along the way, they never got into the Book, so [they never grew.]{.class_s35U}

About the time that I got saved, there was a fellow in Pensacola named Hal Kennedy who got saved. Hal Kennedy played guitar in a hillbilly band and sang country music in bars and dives all around Pensacola. But Hal Kennedy never got into the Scriptures, so he ended right back in the country music bands singing in the same places.

I thank God for the influences in my early Christian life that got me into the word and got me in quick and got me in [deep]{.class_s35U}. Within a week of when I got saved, my mother-in-law sent me a [Scofield Reference Bible. ]{.class_s35U}I began reading that Bible [four hours a day. ]{.class_s35U}Within a year, I had read through it[ twenty-four times.]{.class_s35U}

Not long after I was saved I was exposed to real [Bible teaching]{.class_s35U} and real [Bible preaching. ]{.class_s35U}When I went to paint a baptistry in Dixon Mills, Alabama, I got to hear Roy Kemp, J. Frank Norris' Bible teacher, lecture on the book of Revelation.

Then a little Scottish preacher named James McGinley came to preach a revival at Brent Baptist. He was the only survivor of a rifle company in World War I. He hadn't entered a church until he was twenty-seven years old. Well, I was an infantryman in the army, and I wasn't saved until I was[ twenty-seven]{.class_s35U} years old, so he had my undivided attention. I made it to every night of that meeting, even though I had to catch a bus to church and hitchhike back downtown every night for [two weeks.]{.class_s35U}

Then my brother-in-law, who had gone off to Bible school to train for the ministry, came back to Alabama to get back into farming. He gave me the only textbook []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_253}he had kept. It was a copy of Clarence Larkin's [Dispensational Truth. ]{.class_s35U}I read through that book[ five times in three months.]{.class_s35U}

Meanwhile, Hugh Pyle got me doing little things to serve the Lord. He knew that I could draw, so he gave me a book of cartoons by a man named E. J. Pace. Pace was a cartoonist for the [Sunday School Times]{.class_s35U} for almost fifty years. Bro. Pyle used a lot of wisdom with me. He just dropped that book off at work where I would be sure to find it. I got to looking through that book, and the first thing I thought was "I can do better than that." Old Hugh Pyle got me! That's exactly what he intended to happen.

He had me in to draw for Brent's Vacation Bible School. That first chalk talk was pretty rough. I drew the three Hebrew children in the fiery furnace, and I [implied ]{.class_s35U}(rather strongly) that if those kids didn't act right, they might have to burn in Purgatory for a while (I hadn't gotten all my doctrine straight yet). But Bro. Pyle was very gracious and "covered" for me.

From there I painted a baptistry. Then I travelled to Delaware and apologized to my parents, and I tried to lead them to Christ. Eventually I ended up at Bob Jones University to find a way to use my radio training for the Lord.

Now, I didn't tell you all of that to [brag]{.class_s35U}. That is how God took a young, cussing, beer-soaked, fornicating dance band drummer and infantryman and turned him into a [Bible teacher]{.class_s35U} and [preacher]{.class_s35U}. The Lord may not have the same plans for [you ]{.class_s35U}that He had for me, but He never intends for you to remain just as you were before you were saved. You passed from death to life, and the Lord wants you to ["grow up into him in all things, which is the head, even Christ"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 4:15). One thing is for []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_254}sure: you will never accomplish the purpose God has for you if you do not [grow]{.class_s35U}.

Notice that Peter admonishes the new Christian to ["desire the SINCERE milk of the word."]{.class_s35V} The word ["sincere"]{.class_s35V} means "without hypocrisy." The Bible is always straight. It always "tells it like it is." It won't "butter you up" or flatter you.

But more than that, the word ["sincere"]{.class_s35V} is a reference to the[ purity of the Scripture. ]{.class_s35U}Peter wants the new Christian to get the pure, [unadulterated word of God;]{.class_s35U} not the corruptions that were making their way through the churches (2 Cor. 2:17). Never has there be a time where that verse was more applicable than today. There are plenty of "Bible studies" going on all around America. Yet America has never been more Biblically illiterate than it is today. How can that be?

The problem is in the [milk]{.class_s35U}. The babes in Christ aren't getting ["the sincere milk of the word,"]{.class_s35V} the [Authorized Version. ]{.class_s35U}They are getting watered-down, polluted [skim milk ]{.class_s35U}devoid of the vitamins and minerals essential to growth. They are getting the [NIV]{.class_s35U} with 64,000 words removed from the text; the [NASV,]{.class_s35U} with 36,000 words removed from the text; the [NKJV,]{.class_s35U} shot through with readings from the liberal [RSV]{.class_s35U} of the National Council of Churches. They are getting every Alexandrian corruption that is on the market shoved at them. BUT THEY ARE NOT GETTING ["THE SINCERE MILK OF THE WORD."]{.class_s35V}

For instance, here in 1 Peter 2:2, the [RSV]{.class_s35U} reads, "Like newborn babes, long for the pure spiritual milk, that by it you may grow up to salvation." [That's works salvation. ]{.class_s35U}If you get saved, you get saved instantaneously, the moment []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_255}you trust Christ as your Saviour. [No one "grows up to salvation."]{.class_s35U}

The [NASV]{.class_s35U} and [NIV]{.class_s35U} have tried to cover up the heresy of the text from which they translated (Nestle's). The [NASV]{.class_s35U} says, "grow [in respect ]{.class_s35U}to salvation." The [NIV]{.class_s35U} says, "grow up in your salvation." But those [aren't]{.class_s35U} translations. Those are [paraphrases ]{.class_s35U}to make you think that the Westcott-Hort text of Sinaiticus and Vaticanus is an orthodox text.

The Nestle's text, which contains the Alexandrian reading, says, "eijõ swthrivan" ([eis soterian]{.class_s35U}). The "formal correspondence" (i.e., word-for-word) translation is "into" (or "unto") "salvation." A little problem with "the original text" there, eh what?

Anything to get rid of the [King James]{.class_s36G} text!

["If so be ye have tasted that the Lord is gracious"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 3). Verse 3 is a continuation of verse 2. Peter is saying that if you have come to the Lord and if you have tasted of His graciousness, then keep coming back to the Book flowing with milk (vs. 2) and honey (Psa. 19:10).

David said, ["O taste and see that the ]{.class_s35V}[Lord ]{.class_s360}[is good"]{.class_s35V} (Psa. 34:8). He said in Psalm 119:103, ["How sweet are thy words unto my taste! yea, sweeter than honey to my mouth!"]{.class_s35V}

One time an atheist was having a public debate with a Christian. After a couple of rounds, the Christian could see he wasn't making any headway arguing with the atheist on inductive reasoning and deductive reason, subjective facts and objective facts; so he decided he was going to try a different approach. The next time his turn came to speak, he simply got up and began peeling an orange. He only had ten minutes for his turn and he took []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_256}about three of them just peeling that orange; he never said a word.

Then section by section, he began to [eat ]{.class_s35U}that orange. Of course the audience thought that was a real "hoot." They laughed at him; then they booed and hissed him. Then they were muttering to themselves and finally grew silent. With only one minute left, the Christian turned to the atheist and asked, "Now, how did that orange taste?"

Of course the atheist wasn't about to be outwitted. With a smirk he said, "I don't know; [I didn't eat it."]{.class_s35U}

Then the Christian replied, "Then how can you know what I am talking about? You have never tasted and seen ['that the ]{.class_s35V}[Lord ]{.class_s360}[is good.']{.class_s35V}" And he went over and sat down, [and that ended the debate.]{.class_s35U}

Until you come to the Lord and [try Him out,]{.class_s35U} you can't possibly know anything about what He says.

4 To whom coming, as unto a living stone, disallowed indeed of men, but chosen of God, and precious,

5 Ye also, as lively stones, are built up a spiritual house, an holy priesthood, to offer up spiritual sacrifices, acceptable to God by Jesus Christ.

6 Wherefore also it is contained in the scripture, Behold, I lay in Sion a [chief corner stone]{.class_s363-1}, elect, precious: and he that believeth on him shall not be confounded.

7 Unto you therefore which believe he is precious: but unto them which be disobedient, [the stone which the builders disallowed]{.class_s363-1}, the same is made the head of the corner,

8 And a [stone of stumbling]{.class_s363-1}, and a [rock of offence]{.class_s363-1}, even to them which stumble at the word, being disobedient: whereunto also they were appointed.

In verse 4, Peter compares the Lord (the ["whom"]{.class_s35V} in vs. 4 refers back to ["the Lord"]{.class_s35V} in vs. 3) to ["a living stone."]{.class_s35V} He then says to the believers to whom he is writing: ["Ye also, as lively stones."]{.class_s35V} So the Christian, like his Lord, is a[ living stone.]{.class_s35U}

What is ["a living stone"]{.class_s35V}? Well, there is only one stone mentioned in the Bible that is the product of a living organism, and not merely an inorganic mineral. It is a [pearl ]{.class_s35U}(see comments on Matt. 13:46 in that Commentary). As a body of people, the Church is a [living organism]{.class_s35U} (the Body of Christ) that is likened to two stone structures in a building (["the pillar and ground"]{.class_s35V} \[foundation\][ "of the truth"]{.class_s35V} (1 Tim. 3:15).

Now, while that pearl is a perfect picture of the Church, the Body of Christ, when it comes to Jesus Christ, He is a different ["living stone." "A living stone"]{.class_s35V} is any stone that is actively growing and forming. In the human body, gall stones and kidney stones are like that. The pearl grows and forms in the oyster. But active formations, such as stalactites and stalagmites, are also referred to as "living stone" because they are growing all the time.

Outside of the pearl, there is only one other stone in the Bible that "grows." In Daniel 2, Nebuchadnezzar has a dream in which ["a stone\...cut out without hands"]{.class_s35V} destroys the image of the world empires. When it does, the stone [grows ]{.class_s35U}into ["a great mountain, and filled []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_258}the whole earth"]{.class_s35V} (Dan. 2:35). So that stone is living, [and it is a picture of Jesus Christ at the Second Coming.]{.class_s35U}

Notice in verse 7, that Christ is called ["the head of the corner."]{.class_s35V} There is only one structure in which a [corner ]{.class_s35U}stone is the [head]{.class_s35U}. It is a [pyramid]{.class_s35U}. There are five corners on a pyramid, and the top corner is where the "cap" stone sits; thus the capstone is ["the head of the corner."]{.class_s35V} So on the back of your dollar bill is a pyramid with the headstone having an [eye ]{.class_s35U}in it (Zech. 3:9), indicating that the headstone is [alive. So in Zechariah 3:9, you have a stone with seven eyes in it.]{.class_s35U}

Notice in verse 4 that the stone that was Jesus Christ was ["disallowed indeed of men."]{.class_s35V} Again, the Lord Jesus is described in verse 7 as ["the stone which the builders disallowed."]{.class_s35V} That is why that pyramid on the back of your dollar bill has a [detached ]{.class_s35U}headstone. The first time He came the builders [rejected ]{.class_s35U}Him.

What you have in these verses is the story of how God replaced Israel [spiritually]{.class_s35U}, in this age, as His house and His priests with the Church because of the Jews' rejection of Christ.

Verse 6 is a quote from Isaiah 28:16. The cornerstone is laid ["in Zion,"]{.class_s35V} not in [the nations]{.class_s35U}. And Zion in Isaiah 28:16 is [not]{.class_s35U} the heavenly Sion of Hebrews 12:22. [It is earthly Jerusalem]{.class_s35U} (Isa. 28:14).

So the building of Isaiah 28:16 [is the earthly kingdom of Israel]{.class_s35U}, with the seat of authority, Zion, representing the whole kingdom. Christ insinuates as much when He gives the parable of the vineyard in Matthew 21:33--45. The Lord Jesus Christ is the ["chief corner stone,"]{.class_s35V} the first stone laid in God's earthly kingdom. He is ["the head of the corner,"]{.class_s35V} the [cap stone]{.class_s35U}, which is the last []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_259 .class-1}[corner stone]{.class_s35U} laid on a pyramid. He is the ["Alpha and Omega, the first and the last"]{.class_s35V} (Rev. 1:11).

And that's not all, Isaiah 28:16 says that He is the entire foundation. [He is all five corners.]{.class_s35U}

"Five bleeding wounds He bares, received on Calvary!" [The nation of Israel is directly connected with Christ's blood atonement]{.class_s35U}. So the [Rock ]{.class_s35U}from which the Israelites drank in the wilderness (1 Cor. 10:4) had to be smitten first (Exod. 17:6). Though we can certainly apply Isaiah 53 to Christ dying for all sinners (and I do), the fact is that the prophecy was written [directly ]{.class_s35U}to the nation of Israel. He was named ["Jesus"]{.class_s35V} because He would ["save HIS people]{.class_s35V} \[the Jews\][ from their sins"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 1:21). And before the kingdom can be reestablished, with the King reigning, the Jews as a nation have to accept and repent of their role in the crucifixion of their Messiah (Acts 3:12--21, 4:8--12; Zech. 12:10).

The very idea of all these people getting upset with Mel Gibson's movie [The Passion of the Christ]{.class_s35U} because it made the Jews appear to be guilty of the murder of Jesus Christ. Sure they were guilty! They stood right before Pilate and said, ["His blood be on us, and on our children"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 27:25). (Mel gave in to public opinion on that scene and had it removed from the film.) The Lord gave them at least [six chances]{.class_s35U} in the book of Acts (three in Jerusalem and three in the Dispersion) to make a national repentance of the crucifixion of Christ, while the memory was still fresh in their minds and the facts were still well known through eyewitnesses. When they wouldn't do it, the Lord turned to the Gentiles.

Now, we have discussed this matter in detail in our comments on Romans 11 (see that Commentary), so we []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_260}will not spend a great deal of space here going over it again. But right now, in the Church Age, what was true of Israel [physically]{.class_s35U} is true of the Church, the Body of Christ, [spiritually.]{.class_s35U}

Israel was a [physical ]{.class_s35U}household with a physical [house ]{.class_s35U}(the temple) in which to worship. Peter says, ["Ye\...are built up a spiritual house"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 5). The Church is a [spiritual ]{.class_s35U}household with ["Jesus Christ himself being the chief corner stone"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 2:20). The Church [individually ]{.class_s35U}(1 Cor. 6:19--20) and corporately (Eph. 2:21) is the temple of God today.

The nation of Israel was called to be a nation of [physical ]{.class_s35U}priests (Exod. 19:6). Peter says that we are ["an holy priesthood."]{.class_s35V} That's not written to a bunch of elite, celibate, black-robed cannibals getting drunk on communion wine and[ molesting young boys. ]{.class_s35U}It is written to every Christian (vs. 10). Every Christian (man and woman, boy and girl) is a priest of God in this age. That doctrine is called[ The Priesthood of the Believer,]{.class_s35U} and it is one of the major tenets of [the Reformation.]{.class_s35U}

The nation of Israel offered up physical sacrifices of lambs, sheep, bulls, and goats at a physical altar. They burned physical incense when they prayed. The Christian, though, is ["to offer up ]{.class_s35V}[spiritual sacrifices]{.class_s363-0}[, acceptable to God by Jesus Christ"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 5).

And that one little statement completely destroys the Roman Catholic "Mass." As any Roman Catholic knows (or is supposed to know), the Mass is a [literal ]{.class_s35U}(not spiritual) [sacrifice ]{.class_s35U}of the blood and body of Jesus Christ. Of course the Catholic Church these days may give you all kinds of gas about the elements being offered up in an unbloody manner, but the teaching is that you actually []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_261}eat the [real ]{.class_s35U}body, you drink the [real ]{.class_s35U}blood of Jesus Christ.

That's [not]{.class_s35U} the type of sacrifices which a Christian offers. His sacrifices are sacrifices like ["the sacrifice of praise to God continually"]{.class_s35V} (Heb. 13:15). A spiritual sacrifice is ["giving thanks to his name"]{.class_s35V} (Heb. 13:15). Doing good and giving (["to communicate"]{.class_s35V}: see comments on Gal. 6:6; Phil. 4:14; and 1 Tim. 6:18 in those Commentaries) are spiritual sacrifices. Paul called the gifts which the Philippians sent to him ["a sacrifice acceptable, wellpleasing to God"]{.class_s35V} (Phil. 4:18). Every Christian is to offer up his body as ["a living sacrifice, holy, acceptable unto God, which is your reasonable service"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 12:1). Paul even called the faith of a Christian a sacrifice (Phil. 2:17).

Now, a "sacrifice" is a [sacrifice ]{.class_s35U}(and not merely a gift) when it costs the giver something dear or valuable to him. And if you look at those spiritual sacrifices in that light, you will see that there are times in your life when everyone of those items will be a real [sacrifice ]{.class_s35U}on your part.

You take that first one, for instance: ["praise to God continually."]{.class_s35V} It is not always easy to praise God, did you know that? When you lose a wife or a husband or a little child to death, praising God is hard to do; that's when it's a [sacrifice]{.class_s35U}. But I have been to many a Christian funeral where, though the saints are weeping, they are still singing and praising God, and every once in a while they will get shouting.

Job was able to do it. Job lost all his wealth and all of his children, and he still managed to worship God and say, ["Blessed be the name of the ]{.class_s35V}[Lord]{.class_s360}["]{.class_s35V} (Job 1:19--[]{#c1MX.xhtml_page_262}21). I guarantee you that that meant more to God than all the [burnt offerings]{.class_s35U} Job had ever made (Job 1:5).

I have been through some situations for which, honest to God, I didn't see how I could possibly thank God. The trick when that happens is, if you just can't bring yourself to thank God for the "bad hand" He dealt you, then make a sacrifice on your part and find something for which you [can]{.class_s35U} thank Him. Then later on, after the Lord has worked that bad situation for your good (Rom. 8:28), you can thank Him in retrospect for putting you through it.

We have had students come through PBI who had to make a sacrifice to do right. Their mammas and daddies promised them that if they would go to [some other school, ]{.class_s35U}then they would pay all their school bills, but if they came to [PBI ]{.class_s35U}then they were completely on their own. You might have to sacrifice mamma and daddy or your friends to ["do good."]{.class_s35V}

Paul said of the giving of the churches of Macedonia: ["their deep poverty abounded unto the riches of their liberality"]{.class_s35V} (2 Cor. 8:1--2). Those Christians knew [how]{.class_s35U} to sacrificially give.

And of course when you lay your body and faith on the altar you are sacrificing your will and self-reliance so that God will use you.

Notice that three times in these verses that Jesus Christ is called ["precious."]{.class_s35V} We have already discussed how precious Jesus Christ is to the Christian, and that's in verse 7. Do you think I would trust [anything else?]{.class_s35U} I am betting the most valuable thing I have, my soul, on Him.

The Bible says, ["For what shall it profit a man, if he shall gain the whole world, and lose his own soul?"]{.class_s35V} (Mark 8:36). Well, I am betting my soul that Jesus Christ is right! You say, "What if He's wrong?" []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_263 .class-1}[Then I lose everything. ]{.class_s35U}I am depending completely on [Him ]{.class_s35U}and no one (and nothing) else. ["Unto you therefore which believe he is precious."]{.class_s35V}

But did you notice, that is [not]{.class_s35U} how the word is used in verse 4 and verse 6. Verses 4 and 6 are not a reference to Jesus Christ being precious to the Christian. They are speaking of the Lord being precious to the One who chose Him: God the Father.

When God the Father chose Jesus Christ to be our Saviour, He selected the best that He had to offer. Jesus is God's ["beloved Son"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 3:17, 17:5). He is God's ["dear Son"]{.class_s35V} (Col. 1:13). The Father loved the Son ["before the foundation of the world"]{.class_s35V} (John 17:24).

That is why God puts the emphasis on the Second Coming of Christ that He does in the Scriptures. [There are ten times as many prophecies about the Second Advent as there are about the First. ]{.class_s35U}That is because God the Father is interested in the exaltation of His Son (Phil. 2:9--11).

Brethren, the Lord is not interested in the day that wicked men killed His Son. That's what [we ]{.class_s35U}are interested in. That is why He is precious to [us]{.class_s35U}. God is interested in the day [that His Son takes the throne of the earth and brings everything into subjection to Himself.]{.class_s35U}

God gave the most precious thing He had to save man, and men mocked Him and harassed Him and tried to murder Him. They took Him and slapped Him and spat on Him and beat Him until He was unrecognizable as a man and finally nailed Him to a cross. So one day God is going to return everything that men did to His Son back to them "in spades."

Verse 8 is a quote from Isaiah 8:14. At Christ's first coming, He was ["a stone of stumbling, and a rock []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_264}of offense."]{.class_s35V} Men come across this Stone, and they won't believe and obey what God says about it. So God appoints them to [stumble ]{.class_s35U}over that Stone. The unsaved man rejects Jesus Christ and stumbles right into Hell. Christ said, ["And whosoever shall fall on this stone shall be broken"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 21:44), and that is a quote from Isaiah 8:15.

At the Second Coming, though, the disobedient don't fall on the Stone; [the Stone falls on them]{.class_s35U}. Matthew 21:44, ["But on whomsoever it shall fall, it will grind him to powder."]{.class_s35V} Second Thessalonians 1:7--8, ["When the Lord Jesus shall be revealed from heaven with his mighty angels, In flaming fire taking vengeance on them that know not God, and OBEY NOT the gospel of our Lord Jesus Christ."]{.class_s35V}

9 But ye are a chosen generation, a royal priesthood, an holy nation, a peculiar people; that ye should shew forth the praises of him who hath called you out of darkness into his marvellous light:

10 Which in time past were not a people, but are now the people of God: which had not obtained mercy, but now have obtained mercy.

Verse 9 gives [four views]{.class_s35U} of the Body of Christ. Many of these are similar to the description of Israel in the Old Testament. But note that the Body of Christ has a [spiritual ]{.class_s35U}status, not a physical one like Israel. When it comes to the [physical ]{.class_s35U}promises made to Israel, Romans 11 makes it very clear that the nation is only [temporarily set aside. ]{.class_s35U}The Lord will one day save the whole nation and restore her to all ["the gifts and calling of God"]{.class_s35V} (see Rom. 11:29 and comments).

The Church is first of all ["a chosen generation."]{.class_s35V} Sometimes the word [generation]{.class_s35U} is used of the descendants of a individual or nation and the time period in which they live (Matt. 1). When used to describe a period of time, it is measured from the birth to the death of a particular person. But that is not how the word is used here.

Psalm 22:30 says, ["A seed shall serve him; it shall be accounted to the Lord for a generation."]{.class_s35V} Christians are a seed that God has [generated]{.class_s35U}. He gave life to our dead spirits (Eph. 2:1) through the Holy Spirit.

But we are more than just ["the offspring of God"]{.class_s35V} (Acts 17:29). Paul compares us to Isaac who was the son of Abraham chosen by God to be Abraham's heir (Gen. 17:19--21 cf. Gal. 4:28).

Every Christian is the generation[ of God]{.class_s35U} through the New Birth and chosen by God through ["the adoption of sons"]{.class_s35V} (Gal. 4:5--6 cf. Rom. 8:14--16) and election (see comments on Rom. 8:29; Eph. 1:4; and 1 Pet. 1:2 in those Commentaries).

["A royal priesthood."]{.class_s35V} Back in verse 5, Peter called them ["an holy priesthood."]{.class_s35V} THERE IS NO SUCH THING AS A [CATHOLIC]{.class_s35U} PRIESTHOOD IN EITHER TESTAMENT.

[Every Christian ]{.class_s35U}is called out to be a priest of ["the blessed and only Potentate, the King of kings, and Lord of lords"]{.class_s35V} (1 Tim.  6:15). Also, some day, the Lord will make you ["kings and priests unto God and his Father"]{.class_s35V} (Rev. 1:6).

In the Old Testament, the Jews were called out by God to be ["a ]{.class_s35V}[kingdom of priests]{.class_s363-0}[, and an holy nation"]{.class_s35V} (Exod. 19:6). That Bible says of the nation of Israel: ["the people shall dwell alone, and shall not []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_266}be reckoned among the nations"]{.class_s35V} (Num. 23:9). So Israel was a nation set apart by God for His service, which is what the word ["holy"]{.class_s35V} means in this instance.

In the New Testament, the Body of Christ, the Church, is ["an holy nation."]{.class_s35V} [Every Christian ]{.class_s35U}has been separated, spiritually, from this world, when the Holy Spirit baptized you into the Body of Christ. The word ["ecclesia"]{.class_s35U} means a [called-out ]{.class_s35U}assembly. A Christian is to live in such a way that his [State]{.class_s35U} matches his [Standing.]{.class_s35U}

Paul says, ["I beseech you therefore, brethren, by the mercies of God, that ye present your bodies a living sacrifice, HOLY, acceptable unto God, which is your reasonable SERVICE. AND BE NOT CONFORMED TO THIS WORLD"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 12:1--2).

Now, not only are you separated from the world, but your [allegiance ]{.class_s35U}has changed. Your physical citizenship means nothing to God one way or another. The Bible says of us who are saved, ["For our conversation is in heaven"]{.class_s35V} (Phil. 3:20). We are ["fellowcitizens with the saints"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 2:19). We have been ["translated\...into the kingdom of his dear Son"]{.class_s35V} (Col. 1:13).

I don't know how many of you reading this Commentary are nationalistic or patriotic. I was raised by my father to believe that the greatest thing any man could do was to die in the service of his country. I am, now, nowhere near as patriotic as I used to be, and it gets less and less every year. The reason is that I [switched homelands.]{.class_s35U}

You see, my leader isn't Bush (father or son), Clinton, Reagan, Carter, or JFK. It's King Jesus. My capitol isn't Washington, D.C. Hebrews 13:14, ["For here have we no continuing city, but we seek one to come."]{.class_s35V} [My capitol is the New Jerusalem.]{.class_s35U}

My [Constitution ]{.class_s35U}is the Bible. I'm in a different [army ]{.class_s35U}than the one in which I served during World War II: I'm in the Lord's army. (I suppose that if you're in the Church of Christ that you are in the Lord's [navy;]{.class_s35U} specifically, [the submarine corps]{.class_s35U}.)

Now, that doesn't negate my responsibilities as a citizen of the United States here on earth, as we are about to learn in verses 13--17. But I am a Christian first and foremost,[ and after that, ]{.class_s35U}I am an American. And my allegiance to Jesus Christ and His people transcends national loyalties and geographic boundaries. I may be against the Hindu government of India, but I have Christian brothers and sisters there whom I love and pray for and support, regardless of the[ type of government]{.class_s35U} under which they live.

The [Bible Baptist Church]{.class_s35U} supports a missionary in Vietnam named Mike Roberts. Mike Roberts was an Army Ranger who fought [against ]{.class_s35U}the Communists during the Vietnam War. Today, he serves in Vietnam as a [missionary]{.class_s35U}, with the cooperation of the communist Vietnamese government.

Bro. Roberts is no Communist by any stretch of the imagination. But he made up his mind before he went that he was not going there to spread Americanism, democracy, or our republican form of government.

He was going there to win the lost to Jesus Christ and strengthen believers.

To accomplish this, he made friends of several government officials. As a result, he has been able to get into every [public school ]{.class_s35U}in Ho Chi Minh City (formerly, Saigon) to give out [school supplies]{.class_s35U}, and this gives him an open door into the homes of the parents where he is able to give the Gospel out. The government has even allowed []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_268}his converts to build a church in downtown Saigon, with no government control over the services. That fellow has been a success in a communist nation because[ he represented Jesus Christ]{.class_s35U} (2 Cor. 5:20), [not America.]{.class_s35U}

Finally, the church is called ["a peculiar people."]{.class_s35V} Israel was called ["a peculiar treasure"]{.class_s35V} (Exod. 19:5; Psa. 135:4), ["a peculiar people unto himself ]{.class_s35V}\[God\]["]{.class_s35V} (Deut. 14:2), and ["his]{.class_s35V} \[God's\] [peculiar people"]{.class_s35V} (Deut. 26:18).

Back when the KJV was translated, the word ["peculiar"]{.class_s35U} meant private property; something was [peculiar]{.class_s35U} (the private property) to an individual, nation, assembly, thing, etc. Then the word was used of marks or characteristics distinctive of a person, group, or thing. Today, the word is used to describe things or people that are odd or different in a strange way.

Now, [all ]{.class_s35U}of those definitions are good descriptions of a Christian. A Christian is God's private property (1 Cor. 6:19--20). His life should be marked by characteristics that demonstrate he is a Christian (Eph. 4, 5). And to the world, a Christian who is living for Jesus Christ will always be an[ odd ball ]{.class_s35U}and a fanatical [nut]{.class_s35U}. Peter said, ["Wherein they ]{.class_s35V}\[the folks with whom you used to run around\][ ]{.class_s35V}[think it strange]{.class_s363-0}[ that ye run not with them to the same excess of riot"]{.class_s35V} (1 Pet. 4:3--4).

["That ye should shew forth the praises of him."]{.class_s35V} In other words, the purpose of God making you part of ["a chosen generation, a royal priesthood, an holy nation, a ]{.class_s35V}[peculiar people]{.class_s363-0}["]{.class_s35V} is so that you will give Him praise. And notice that that praise is a public thing. Praising God isn't limited to a Christian's "prayer closet." God wants us to ["shew forth the praises of him."]{.class_s35V} We []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_269}should praise God before other people and let them know [why]{.class_s35U} He is worthy of praise.

"Who hath called you out of darkness into his marvelous light."

Now, I have showed you in this verse how similar Israel and the Church are. Those descriptions of saved, Christian Gentiles are so close to how God describes those Jews in the Old Testament that the Hyperdispensationalists will tell you the verse is referring to the Jews in the Tribulation. But when you get down to that last phrase, that interpretation won't work. That passing from darkness to light is a [Pauline expression.]{.class_s35U}

Acts 26:17--18, ["Delivering thee from the people, and from]{.class_s35V}[ the Gentiles]{.class_s363-0}[, unto whom now I send thee. To open their eyes, and to ]{.class_s35V}[turn them from darkness]{.class_s363-0}[ to light."]{.class_s35V} Ephesians 5:8, ["For ye were sometimes darkness, but now are ye light in the Lord."]{.class_s35V} Colossians 1:12--13, ["Giving thanks unto the Father, which hath made us meet to be partakers of the inheritance of the saints in light: ]{.class_s35V}[Who hath delivered us from the power of darkness]{.class_s363-0}[, and hath translated us into the kingdom of his dear Son."]{.class_s35V}

Verse 10:[ "Which in time past were not a people, but are now the people of God."]{.class_s35V} Then Peter can't be talking about the Jews. In the Old Testament, the Jews [were]{.class_s35U} ["a people,"]{.class_s35V} and they [were]{.class_s35U}[ "the people of God."]{.class_s35V} The Lord told Pharaoh, ["Let MY people go"]{.class_s35V} (Exod. 5:1, and He told Solomon, ["If MY people, which are called by my name, etc."]{.class_s35V} (2 Chron. 7:14).

But there was a time when God [did]{.class_s35U} disown the Jews and then promised their [restoration]{.class_s35U}. It was Hosea 1:10 []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_270}and 2:23. Those are the verses that Peter is quoting in verse 10. When Paul quotes those verses in Romans 9:25--26, he doesn't apply them to the Jews at all. [He applies them to Gentiles believing the Gospel of Jesus Christ. ]{.class_s35U}That is what Peter is doing here.

How do you know that is what Peter is doing? Because right now (the Church Age), the Jews are [not]{.class_s35U} God's people. They are in the state described in Hosea 1:10. Romans 11 says they are [cast away]{.class_s35U} in verse 15, that they are branches [broken off ]{.class_s35U}the olive tree in verse 17, that God is not sparing them at this time in verse 21, that they are in [unbelief ]{.class_s35U}in verse 23, and that they are mostly blind in verse 25. [Of course, that will change in the Tribulation and at the Second Advent ]{.class_s35U}(Rom. 11:25--27).

So the Jews [were ]{.class_s35U}God's people in the Old Testament, but they are not [now ]{.class_s35U}because of their rejection of the Messiah. But they [will be]{.class_s35U} when their Messiah shows up again (Zech. 12:10). In the meantime, they are still ["beloved for the fathers' sakes"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 11:28).

The Gentiles, on the other hand, were not God's people in the Old Testament. When God [turned from ]{.class_s35U}the Jews in the book of Acts, He [turned to]{.class_s35U} the Gentiles. They have been grafted ["into a good olive tree"]{.class_s35V} though it was contrary to their ["nature"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 11:24). They have obtained the mercy which Peter mentions in the last half of verse 10 (Rom. 11:30). As a result, the Church is made up mostly of saved Gentiles.

They are now ["called to be saints"]{.class_s35V} (1 Cor. 1:2). They are ["one new man"]{.class_s35V} in Christ (Eph. 2:15). They are part ["of the household of God"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 2:19). They are ["the children of God\...and joint-heirs with Christ"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 8:16--17).

You are living in the day when ["the times of the Gentiles"]{.class_s35V} (Luke 21:24) is beginning to come to an end. (See the [Bible Believer's Commentary on Esther.]{.class_s35U})

11 Dearly beloved, I beseech you as strangers and pilgrims, abstain from fleshly lusts, which war against the soul;

12 Having your conversation honest among the Gentiles: that, whereas they speak against you as evildoers, they may by your good works, which they shall behold, glorify God in the day of visitation.

While verse 9 gives titles for the Body of Christ, corporately, verse 11 gives two titles to Christians as [individuals]{.class_s35U}. They are ["strangers and pilgrims."]{.class_s35V} Before a Gentile is saved he is called a "stranger" and a "foreigner" (Eph. 2:19), but he is a stranger ["from the covenants of promise, having no hope, and without God in the world"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 2:12). Like Cain in the Old Testament, he is ["a fugitive and a vagabond in the earth"]{.class_s35V} (Gen. 4:14).

The difference between ["strangers and pilgrims"]{.class_s35V} and ["a fugitive and a vagabond"]{.class_s35V} is this: ["a fugitive"]{.class_s35V} is someone "on the run" from the law. ["A vagabond,"]{.class_s35V} like a pilgrim, is travelling all of the time, but his travels are an [aimless wandering without purpose]{.class_s35U}. The unsaved man is [running ]{.class_s35U}from God's Law and His justice; he has no idea of where he is going or how to get there or what to do on the journey.

The Christian, however, though he may be a stranger, is not a stranger[ to God. ]{.class_s35U}HE has been ["accepted in the beloved"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 1:6). The Christian is a stranger to [this world. ]{.class_s35U}He does not belong or fit in; it is not []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_272}his homeland. Like the song says, "This world is not my home; I'm just a passing through." The Christian is taking a journey: [he is a pilgrim]{.class_s35U}. But unlike the vagabond, the Christian knows where he is [headed]{.class_s35U}, and he has a [purpose ]{.class_s35U}along the way. The Christian is merely passing through this world to [his permanent home.]{.class_s35U}

That is one of the hardest things to get across to God's people: HOME IS NOT [HERE!]{.class_s35U} I preach about Heaven at some churches, and the whole congregation just sits there and blinks at me like a tree full of owls. But I will keep talking about it until I drop in my tracks. I will do all I can to raise a stink about this world in the nostrils of Christians so they will desire the sweet roses of Paradise.

The most pitiful thing in the world is to watch a Christian get settled in and comfortable down [here]{.class_s35U}, and God just leaves him alone. Brethren, the best thing the Lord can do for you, in a situation like that, is to send something your way to stir you up and make this world bitter to you and Heaven sweet.

I have seen God reach down and take a little boy or girl home to Heaven and break the heart of some Christian couple. But I have seen that same couple "light up" when I got to preaching about Heaven. They have something over there, now, to look forward to. And if the Lord can't get you to ["set your affection on things above" ]{.class_s35V}with what Jesus Christ did for you and with the promises in His word, then He'll take something you love down [here ]{.class_s35U}and put it up [there ]{.class_s35U}so you will want to go see it again.

Now, notice in verse 11, that Peter is begging them (["I beseech you"]{.class_s35V}) to do something on the basis that they have no permanent home down on earth. Since they []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_273}are ["strangers and pilgrims"]{.class_s35V} to this world, He wants them to ["abstain from fleshly lusts."]{.class_s35V}

In the New Testament, the Christian is to abstain from eating or drinking blood (no Mass; Acts 15:20,29), he is to ["abstain from all appearance of evil"]{.class_s35V} (changed in all the new "Bibles" so you [can appear]{.class_s35U} to do evil as long as you don't really do it---1 Thess. 5:22), he is to ["abstain from fornication"]{.class_s35V} (1 Thess. 4:3), and he is to ["abstain from fleshly lusts"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 11).

Peter tells you that ["fleshly lusts\...war against the soul."]{.class_s35V} The [NIV, ]{.class_s35U}one of the most corrupt translations you can get, changes ["fleshly lusts"]{.class_s35V} to "sinful desires" so you won't identify the enemy HQ in your war. This time not even the [NASV]{.class_s35U} or the [RSV]{.class_s35U} were that stupid.

Now, the Christian has [three great enemies: the world, the flesh, and the Devil]{.class_s35U} (James 3:14--16). You win the war with the world by presenting your body to God as ["a living sacrifice"]{.class_s35V} and letting the Holy Spirit transform you ["by the renewing of your mind"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 12:1--2). You win the war with the Devil by putting ["on the whole armour of God"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 6:10--18) and resisting Him (James 4:7). Paul says, ["(For the weapons of our warfare are not carnal, but mighty through God to the pulling down of strong holds;) Casting down imaginations, and every high thing that exalteth itself against the knowledge of God, and bringing into captivity every thought to the obedience of Christ]{.class_s35V} (2 Cor. 10:4--5).

The flesh, though, is different. The Devil and the world are outside you, storming the walls, trying to get in and conquer. But the flesh is a "fifth column" that lives with you, fighting you from [the inside. ]{.class_s35U}Before you were saved, your soul was connected to your flesh and []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_274}acted with your flesh and was corrupted by your flesh. But when you got saved, the Holy Spirit performed an ["operation"]{.class_s35V} (that's what it's called in Col. 2:12) and circumcised (cut) ["the body of the sins of the flesh"]{.class_s35V} away from your soul (Col. 2:11). So now your soul is no longer connected to your flesh.

But you have to be wary in regards to that relationship. Although the soul is not connected to the flesh, it remembers when it was and has a propensity to give in to the[ desires of the flesh. ]{.class_s35U}That's why Paul said, ["Flee also youthful lusts"]{.class_s35V} (2 Tim. 2:22). When Joseph was tempted by Potiphar's wife to commit adultery, he ran (Gen. 39:13). Lester Roloff used to say, "Joseph [lost his coat,]{.class_s35U} but he [kept his character."]{.class_s35U}

The best way to treat ["the lust of the flesh"]{.class_s35V} (1 John 2:16) is get as far away from it as possible. ["Flee"]{.class_s35V} from it. ["Abstain"]{.class_s35V} from it. Don't see how close you can get to it without sinning.

Verse 12, ["Having your conversation honest among the Gentiles."]{.class_s35V} That verse sounds like Peter could be addressing Jews. Of course, ["the Gentiles"]{.class_s35V} is not a reference to any saved Gentile at all. Those are unsaved Gentiles who are speaking against saved people (it could be Jew or Gentile) ["as evildoers."]{.class_s35V}

The Hyperdispensationalists should never forget that there are [three groups of humanity]{.class_s35U} in the Pauline epistles: the Jews, the Gentiles, and ["the church of God"]{.class_s35V} (1 Cor. 10:32). Peter just got through describing believers as a nation separate from the other nations (vs. 9) and ["strangers and pilgrims"]{.class_s35V} in the world (vs. 11). So it would not be anything odd for Peter to speak of ["the Gentiles"]{.class_s35V} in distinction from all believers, whether those believers were Gentiles or Jews.

Peter is talking to believers in the Body of Christ, and he is talking to Christians against whom the unsaved Gentiles were speaking as if they were criminals---["evildoers."]{.class_s35V} In the book of Acts, Paul and his converts were accused by the Gentiles of disturbing the peace (Acts 16:20, 17:6), sedition (Acts 16:21, 17:7), "hate crimes" (according to modern New Age Globalists---Acts 19:26--27), and murder (Acts 28:4).
