["They may by your good works, which they shall behold, glorify God."]{.class_s35V} This is similar to what Christ said in Matthew 5:16 (see comments in that Commentary). It is also one of the excuses that lazy Christians use for not witnessing.

"Well, Dr. Ruckman, I don't believe in talking it; I believe in livin' it. I just try to let my little light shine, you know."

That's the speech of a Christian who is afraid to open their [yap]{.class_s35U} for Jesus Christ. They will sit and talk your ear off about hunting, fishing, football, the neighbors, the folks at church, the relatives, the weather, etc.; but when it comes to the subjects of Jesus Christ, salvation, and the Bible they, all of a sudden, experience "lockjaw."

Now, do you [really]{.class_s35U} want people to ["see your good works"]{.class_s35V}? [Just speak up for Jesus Christ!]{.class_s35U} They will watch you like a hawk. They will examine [every move you make]{.class_s35U} as if you were under a microscope.

The problem modern Christians have is that [they don't want folks to watch them too closely. ]{.class_s35U}Their [actions ]{.class_s35U}don't always match their [profession]{.class_s35U}, and they don't want to change the way they are living.

If you are a Christian, you not only have a responsibility to "walk it," you should "talk it" as well. Don't you worry; if you [talk]{.class_s35U} about Jesus Christ, the lost []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_276}will look at your daily [walk. That's]{.class_s35U} when they will see the difference and ask you more about the Jesus Christ you talked about. But if you never talk about [why]{.class_s35U} you live differently, they will just assume that you are another self-righteous sinner, like [them]{.class_s35U}, trying to work your way to Heaven.

["The day of visitation."]{.class_s35V} This is another of those places in 1 Peter that could have a[ double application:]{.class_s35U} one now for the Church and a future application for saints in the Tribulation.

In the Old Testament, ["the day of visitation"]{.class_s35V} is a reference to God visiting in judgment, specifically the judgment that accompanies Jesus Christ at the Second Advent (Isa. 10:3; Jer. 8:12, 10:15, 23:12, 46:21, 51:18; Hosea 9:7; Micah 7:4). But in the New Testament, ["visitation"]{.class_s35V} is Jesus Christ coming and offering salvation, first to the Jews and then to the Gentiles.

Luke 1:68, ["Blessed be the Lord God of Israel; for]{.class_s35R}[ he hath visited and redeemed his people]{.class_s35W-0}[."]{.class_s35R}

Luke 1:76--79, ["And thou, child, shalt be called the prophet of the Highest: for thou shalt go before the face of the Lord to prepare his ways; To give knowledge of salvation unto his people by the remission of their sins, Through the tender mercy of our God; ]{.class_s35R}[whereby the dayspring from on high hath visited us]{.class_s35W-0}[, To give light to them that sit in darkness and in the shadow of death, to guide our feet into the way of peace."]{.class_s35R}

Luke 7:16, ["And there came a fear on all: and they glorified God, saying, That a great prophet is risen up among us; and, ]{.class_s35R}[That God hath visited his people."]{.class_s35W-0}

Acts 15:14, ["Simeon hath declared how ]{.class_s35R}[God at the first did visit the Gentiles]{.class_s35W-0}[, to take out of them a people for his name."]{.class_s35R}

Every one of those New Testament references is Jesus Christ showing up at [His first coming]{.class_s35S}. But everyone of them is in a [Second Advent context]{.class_s35S}. Like I have showed you before, when Christ came the first time, [the Lord had things set up so that both advents could have been fulfilled before A.D. 70.]{.class_s35S}

When Peter talks about ["the day of visitation" ]{.class_s35R}here in verse 12, it could be a reference to the Gospel coming to the Gentiles of verse 12. In other words, here are bunch of Gentiles speaking evil of a group of Christians. Despite the ridicule, those Christians live a life of good works that matches their profession. Then one day some of those Gentiles get saved, and they glorify God for some Christians who lived what they preached and were a good testimony to them.

That's one way of looking at it. Another is God visiting [judgment ]{.class_s35S}on those same Gentiles. When they die and stand before God, they would have to give Him the glory because the Lord sent them a witness through believers whom the Gentiles could not legitimately accuse of wrongdoing. Not only was the preaching of the Christians a testimony [against]{.class_s35S} those Gentiles, but their lives were as well.

And then, a third and final way of looking at it is the reference is to Jews who have believed on Christ and are keeping the commandments in the Tribulation (Rev. 12:17, 14:12). The fact that they were able to make it through the Tribulation clean will be a testimony against their Gentile [enemies ]{.class_s35S}when Christ comes to judge the nations at His Second Advent (Matt. 25).

13 Submit yourselves to every ordinance of man for the Lord's sake: whether it be to the king, as supreme;

14 Or unto governors, as unto them that are sent by him for the punishment of evildoers, and for the praise of them that do well.

15 For so is the will of God, that with well doing ye may put to silence the ignorance of foolish men:

16 As free, and not using your liberty for a cloke of maliciousness, but as the servants of God.

17 Honour all men. Love the brotherhood. Fear God. Honour the king.

18 Servants, be subject to your masters with all fear; not only to the good and gentle, but also to the froward.

Verse 13 is one of those "hard" verses in the Scripture. It isn't hard to [understand;]{.class_s35U} it's hard to [obey. ]{.class_s35U}You are told to ["submit yourselves to EVERY ordinance of man,"]{.class_s35V} and you are told to do it ["FOR THE LORD'S SAKE."]{.class_s35V}

Since I have gone into this matter thoroughly in Romans 13 (see that Commentary), I will only make a few brief comments here. Are there exceptions to the word ["every"]{.class_s35V}? Yes, there are (Acts 4:19--20, 5:29). Is the Constitution one of them? No, it isn't.

I know that will upset some of you, but that's just the way it is. One of my preacher friends up in Indianapolis decided he wasn't going to pay the taxes of his employees the way the government asked him to do it. He ended up with only a handful of people left and the federal marshals coming in and shutting down the work and confiscating the property.

He tried twisting the Bible so that he only had to obey the Constitution and not ["every ordinance of man."]{.class_s35V} It didn't work.

You might as well face it, brethren. [The Constitution is a joke and has been since 1861. ]{.class_s35U}Abraham Lincoln decided for the [whole country, ]{.class_s35U}back in 1861, that the Constitution could be ignored at any time [if it was for the good of the federal government.]{.class_s35U}

Woodrow Wilson put through an [unconstitutional income tax ]{.class_s35U}that has never been repealed. Why? Because it keeps a bunch of [federal bureaucrats employed. ]{.class_s35U}The country's economy is [unconstitutionally controlled ]{.class_s35U}by a private corporation called the Federal Reserve Bank. It's good because it relieves Senators and Congressmen of their responsibility in that regard. They can blame a bad economy on the president---even though Constitutionally it is [not]{.class_s35U} his responsibility.

[The president can now go to war without any declaration passed by the Congress ]{.class_s35U}(Korea, Vietnam, Grenada, Bosnia, Kuwait, Afghanistan, Iraq, etc.). That's a direct violation of the checks and balances set up in the Constitution. Do you know what will be done about it? [Not one cotton-pickin' thing on the face of this earth.]{.class_s35U}

Recently, the big stir is over federally appointed judges making rulings that [establish]{.class_s35U} law rather than [interpret]{.class_s35U} law. Moreover, instead of going back to English common law and legal precedents set by previous courts, judges now make their decision on the opinions of [foreign governments]{.class_s35U} and their [own political agendas. ]{.class_s35U}Are these judges being removed by the President and Congress for violating the Constitution? Of course not! That would be the pot calling the kettle black.

You can scream and yell about the Constitution all you want. You will find out what Judge Roy Moore, the Chief Justice of the Alabama Supreme Court, found out when he set up a monument of the Ten Commandments in a government building. [Nobody in the federal government gives a "flip" what the Constitution says.]{.class_s35U}

If you don't follow ["every ordinance of man"]{.class_s35V} the way you are told, you will lose your [job ]{.class_s35U}(Roy Moore), you will lose your [property ]{.class_s35U}(Greg Dixon), and you could even lose your [life ]{.class_s35U}(David Koresh).

There are two reasons why I pay my taxes. Neither of those reasons have to do with the Constitution, patriotism, "God Bless America," or anything like that. [I pay my taxes so I won't get my head blown off by an FBI sharpshooter]{.class_s35U} (vs. 14, Rom. 13:4), and I do it [because God told me to do it]{.class_s35U} (vs. 13, Rom. 13:5--7).

Now, Peter says, ["Submit yourselves to every ordinance of man."]{.class_s35V} Then he lists the men to whom he is referring.

["To the king, as supreme"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 13). At the time, ["the king"]{.class_s35V} was a [demented madman]{.class_s35U} named Nero who was a faggot (queer, fairy, fruit loop, etc.), committed fornication with his own mother, murdered his own subjects, and burned his capitol city to the ground. If Peter could subject himself to someone like [that]{.class_s35U}, then you can subject yourself to people like George Bush (father or son), "Slick Willie" Clinton, Jimmy Carter, or JFK.

Now, in the Bible, the Lord recognizes two forms of government: [a Theocracy and a Monarchy]{.class_s35U}. A Theocracy is when [God ]{.class_s35U}runs the government. A [Monarchy ]{.class_s35U}is when a [king ]{.class_s35U}runs the government. [There is no Democracy or Republic anywhere in the Bible.]{.class_s35U}

Our republican form of government was set up by a group of Christians and God-fearing men who were sick and tired of living under Roman Catholic and Anglican monarchs who tried to control the way they [worshipped]{.class_s35U}. They wanted to worship God the way they believed the Bible dictated, not the way some man told them. So the cry of the Revolutionary War was "No king, but King Jesus," and the [Bible ]{.class_s35U}was the basis for all our laws, including [The Constitution]{.class_s35U}.

The fact is that [The ]{.class_s35U}Constitution was set up to govern a Bible-reading, commandment-observing, [Christ-professing people. ]{.class_s35U}It was never made to control a bunch of sex-obsessed, media-controlled, intemperate, hedonistic [monkey men ]{.class_s35U}that constitute the present population of the United States.

You say, "Who believes that besides you, Ruckman?" [Every "Founding Father" of the United States believed that. ]{.class_s35U}If you don't believe me, get a book from the Bookstore called [America's God and Country Encyclopedia of Quotations]{.class_s35U} by William Federer and read what the men who set up this country said about "government of, by, and for the people." Every one of them taught that if a people weren't ruled by God on the inside, no government of [man ]{.class_s35U}could adequately rule them on the outside.

So God's form of government is a society ruled directly by [Him ]{.class_s35U}and His [words]{.class_s35U}. And when He sets up a [king]{.class_s35U}, that king is to be in subjection to the Lord and His words. And if God allowed America to break away from her king and set up a Democratic Republic, He only blessed it as long as its leaders were in subjection to [Him ]{.class_s35U}and His [words]{.class_s35U}.

When America removed[ Bible reading ]{.class_s35U}and [prayer ]{.class_s35U}from its schools and public offices, the Lord "blessed" her with [moral filth]{.class_s35U} pouring out of every media outlet, a skyrocketing [VD rate]{.class_s35U}, almost a 1,000 percent rise in violent crimes, an uncontrollable [drug problem]{.class_s35U}, a [prison population]{.class_s35U} so large that we now have to rely on private corporations to house them all, a 50 percent [divorce rate]{.class_s35U}, faggots trying to marry other faggots, children [killing each other]{.class_s35U} in public schools, an [abortion ]{.class_s35U}rate so alarming that it is actually threatening the expected population growth and future economy of the country, pornography, child molestation, [and an influx of Moslems ]{.class_s35U}who will (eventually), by force, require you to submit to [their ]{.class_s35U}god and [their ]{.class_s35U}Koranic laws.

And some of you actually think that a return to the Constitution would cure all of that! If you honestly believe that, please come see me. I have some "prime, Florida, waterfront property" (swampland) that I would love to sell you.

["Or unto governors"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 14). In the New Testament, those were people like Pilate, Felix, Festus, and Gallio.

["As unto them that are sent by him for the punishment of evildoers, and for the praise of them that do well."]{.class_s35V} And again, all of that is Pauline doctrine from Romans 13:1--5. It is written to Christians in the Church Age.

And then an important verse: ["FOR SO IS THE WILL OF GOD"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 15). Good Christians are always concerned about [the will of God]{.class_s35U} for their lives. A Christian teenager, who is trying to do right and serve God, always wonders what [the will of God]{.class_s35U} is. Should he []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_283}be a preacher? Should she marry a preacher and be a pastor's wife? Should he or she go to the mission field?

There are a lot of circumstances in life where it takes prayer, counsel, and the Holy Spirit's guidance to figure out what the will of God actually is supposed to be. But for the Christian, there are three clearly revealed things in the New Testament that are ["the will of God."]{.class_s35V}

1\) ["For this is the will of God, EVEN YOUR SANCTIFICATION, that he should ABSTAIN FROM FORNICATION']{.class_s35V} (1 Thess. 4:3).

2\) ["IN EVERYTHING GIVE THANKS: for this is the will of God in Christ Jesus concerning you"]{.class_s35V} (1 Thess. 5:18).

3\) ["For so is the will of God, THAT WITH WELL DOING YE MAY PUT TO SILENCE THE IGNORANCE OF FOOLISH MEN"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 15).

What is the ["well doing" ]{.class_s35V}of verse 15? It is the submission to the ordinances of men in the context of verses 13 and 14.

If you want to shut a bunch of stupid bureaucrats up, then do what they tell you to do. You don't have to [like ]{.class_s35U}the rules and recommend the rules or even agree with the rules. But it is God's will that you obey them so unsaved people can't point to you and legitimately say, "He's a criminal; she's a law breaker."

Verse 16:[ "As free."]{.class_s35V} The Christian is free. Paul said, ["Stand fast therefore in the liberty wherewith Christ hath made us free" ]{.class_s35V}(Gal. 5:1). That freedom extends to every part of life. [Four times ]{.class_s35U}in the book of 1 Corinthians, Paul says, ["All things are lawful for me"]{.class_s35V} (1 Cor. 6:12, 10:23). When it comes to this matter of paying taxes and obeying the government, Christ Himself said, ["Then are the children free"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 17:26).

But you have to watch yourself concerning your liberty in Christ. Just because you [can]{.class_s35U} do a thing, doesn't mean you [should]{.class_s35U} do a thing. And just because something is [legal,]{.class_s35U} it doesn't make it [right.]{.class_s35U}

You don't do everything you have liberty to do because there are more considerations than [your freedom ]{.class_s35U}in Christ that are at stake. You don't want to offend unsaved people for no reason (Matt. 17:27). You don't want to do anything that is not [expedient ]{.class_s35U}or will gain control of you (1 Cor. 6:12) or that won't build you up in Christ (1 Cor. 10:23).

In 1 Peter 1:16, you are not to use your freedom to be hateful, spiteful, or vengeful (["not using your liberty for a cloke of maliciousness"]{.class_s35V}). The Lord didn't give you your Christian liberty for that reason. Paul says, ["Ye have been called unto liberty; only use not liberty for an occasion to the flesh"]{.class_s35V} (Gal. 5:13).

["But as the servants of God."]{.class_s35V} You are free, but you are not free from [righteousness]{.class_s35U}. In 1 Corinthians 7:22, Paul says, ["For he that is called in the Lord, being a servant, is the Lord's freeman: likewise also he that is called, being free, is Christ's servant."]{.class_s35V} You are a slave, knocked down on the block and sold to Jesus Christ. That Book says, ["For ye are bought with a price"]{.class_s35V} (1 Cor. 6:20).

The Christian is [free in]{.class_s35U} Jesus Christ, and yet he is a [slave to]{.class_s35U} Jesus Christ. That's one of those paradoxes of the Christian life.

["Being then made free from sin, ye became the servants of righteousness\....for as ye have yielded your members servants to uncleanness and to iniquity unto iniquity; even so now yield your members servants to righteousness unto holiness. []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_285}For when ye were the servants of sin, ye were free from righteousness\....But now being made free from sin, and become servants to God, ye have your fruit unto holiness, and the end everlasting life"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 6:18--22).

When it comes to this matter of [liberty]{.class_s35U}, the Christian needs to understand this: there is a difference between [liberty]{.class_s35U} and [license. Liberty]{.class_s35U} is the freedom to do right. In America, you have liberty, but you don't have the liberty to do anything [you want]{.class_s35U}. True liberty is always regulated by law so you don't violate the liberties of others. The patriotic song says, "thy liberty IN LAW."

[License,]{.class_s35U} however, is doing something that you don't have a right to do. In the moral realm, it is going beyond the bounds of liberty and doing something you [should not do. ]{.class_s35U}Hence, the word [licentious,]{.class_s35U} meaning "characterized by EXCESSIVE ASSUMPTION of liberty; disregarding commonly accepted rules; deviating freely from that which is correct."

An old time divine once said that [true liberty ]{.class_s35U}lies within the bounds of God's rules and regulations for your life. He will allow you to do anything that is [right]{.class_s35U} and [legal]{.class_s35U} (according to His law), and outside of those two boundaries is [slavery]{.class_s35U}. You will come under the dominion of the world, the flesh, or the Devil.

You can become ["entangled again with the yoke of bondage"]{.class_s35V} (Gal. 5:1). You can ["fall into reproach and the snare of the devil"]{.class_s35V} (1 Tim. 3:7) and be ["taken captive by him"]{.class_s35V} (2 Tim. 2:26).

And then there are a series of short commands in verse 17.

1\) ["Honour all men."]{.class_s35V} There is a certain amount of respect, courtesy, and kindness you should give to any []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_286}man. Of course not all men deserve the same [amount ]{.class_s35U}of honor. I wouldn't treat a bum like Elvis Presley with the same respect I would pay to a man like Harlan Popov or Richard Wurmbrand. Paul says, ["honour to whom honour"]{.class_s35V} is due (Rom. 13:7).

You are commanded to honor your father and mother (Eph. 6:2). You are to treat the brethren ["in honour preferring one another"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 12:10). A husband is to give ["honour unto the wife, as unto the weaker vessel"]{.class_s35V} (1 Pet. 3:7). The church is to ["honour widows that are widows indeed"]{.class_s35V} (1 Tim. 5:3). Paul tells slaves to ["count their own masters worthy of all honour"]{.class_s35V} (1 Tim. 6:1). And in the church, ["let the elders that rule well be counted worthy of double honour"]{.class_s35V} (1 Tim. 5:17).

2\) ["Love the brotherhood."]{.class_s35V} You are to love other Christians as your brothers and sisters in Christ. Notice again that 1 Peter can't be written exclusively to Jews, either in the Church Age or the Tribulation. ["Brotherly love"]{.class_s35V} is a Pauline commandment to the church (Rom. 12:10; 1 Thess. 4:9; Heb. 13:1).

3\) ["Fear God."]{.class_s35V} Good advice to [anyone ]{.class_s35U}(saved or lost) at any time (Church Age or Tribulation). And when the Bible says ["fear God,"]{.class_s35V} it means [fear,]{.class_s35U} as in being SCARED. It doesn't mean "respect" or "godly reverence" (see comments on Heb. 11:7 and Prov. 1:7 in those Commentaries).

4\) ["Honour the king."]{.class_s35V} The individual isn't always [worthy ]{.class_s35U}of the honor that comes with the [position]{.class_s35U}. When that's the case (as it certainly was in the case of Nero, and more recently in the case of "Slick Willie" Clinton), then you have to show the honor [due to that position. ]{.class_s35U}In []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_287}the army, we called it saluting the [uniform ]{.class_s35U}instead of [the officer.]{.class_s35U}

Verse 18: ["Servants"]{.class_s35V} (he's talking to slaves, not to employees) ["be subject to your masters with all fear."]{.class_s35V} There is nothing in the entire Bible, anywhere from Genesis to Revelation, that advocates the abolition of slavery.

Having said that, I can hear the cry go up, "Bigot! White Supremacist! KKK!"

Oh, shut your mouth! I preach to more black folk (and [bad]{.class_s35U} black folk at that; I mean, some of them have come home drunk and slammed the baby's head against the wall) in a month than some of my white preacher brethren have done in a year. And I hug them too. Even if they might have contracted AIDS.

The truth is (regardless of what you think), that in the New Testament, [the slave is commanded to obey his maste]{.class_s35U}r (Eph. 6:5; Col. 3:22) and please him well (Titus 2:9). He is to show him honor and[ serve him ]{.class_s35U}(1 Tim. 6:1--2) and [subject himself to him]{.class_s35U} (vs. 18).

That goes for [unbelieving masters]{.class_s35U} (1 Tim. 6:1) as well as believing ones (1 Tim. 6:2). It applies to ["the good and gentle"]{.class_s35V} as well as to the Simon Legrees (["The froward,"]{.class_s35V} vs. 18).

19 For this is thankworthy, if a man for conscience toward God endure grief, suffering wrongfully.

20 For what glory is it, if, when ye be buffeted for your faults, ye shall take it patiently? but if, when ye do well, and suffer for it, ye take it patiently, this is acceptable with God.

Now, Peter takes that last word in verse 18 (["froward"]{.class_s35V}), and he expands it to include all Christians, not merely the slaves whom he was addressing.

The idea is if someone is mistreating you as a forward master would mistreat his slave, and he is doing it because you are following God and your conscience, then [that ]{.class_s35U}is something for which it is worth thanking God (["thankworthy"]{.class_s35V}).

But the catch is you are ["suffering wrongfully"]{.class_s35V}: that is, you have done nothing to [deserve ]{.class_s35U}the grief and suffering you are getting. You have to be careful as to the reason [why]{.class_s35U} you are getting it "in the neck."

If you are "taking a lickin'" for [your own stupidity and your own faults]{.class_s35U}, then that's no good (vs. 20). ["What glory is it?"]{.class_s35V} Absolutely none. [You are getting what you had coming.]{.class_s35U}

When John R. Rice was embroiled in the Billy Graham controversy back in the 1950s, he fell down some cellar stairs and almost killed himself. When he wrote about the incident in the [Sword of the Lord,]{.class_s35U} he said the Devil pushed him.

Oh, come on! Get off it! Don't blame the Devil because you are clumsy. That's not suffering for [well-doing.]{.class_s35U}

If something bad happens to you, the first thing you need to ask yourself is, "Did I do anything to deserve this?" I know that goes against this modern self-esteem movement, but the fact is that most of the trouble that comes our way is [our own fault]{.class_s35U}. We should make some attempt to remedy our faults.

James says, ["Confess your faults one to another"]{.class_s35V} (James 5:16 and comments in that Commentary). David asked the Lord to cleanse him []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_289 .class-1}["from secret faults"]{.class_s35V} (Psa. 19:12). You have faults that you know and faults of which you aren't aware.

You need to take a good hard look at yourself and [identify those faults]{.class_s35U} in your nature. When they cause problems between you and others, confess those faults to the offended party. Let them know that you realize the problem is because of [you]{.class_s35U}, and you seek to make amends. Ask the Lord to take care of those faults you aren't aware of.

When trouble comes to you because of [those faults,]{.class_s35U} don't whine and cry because you're getting what you deserve. Just pray to God that you don't get any greater punishment than you got.

Somebody came to Bob Jones Sr. one time, complaining about everything on the campus: the food, the hours, etc. After letting them blow off a little steam, Bob Jones replied, ["It beats going to Hell, doesn't it?"]{.class_s35U}

Yeah, it sure does.

Now, whatever trouble comes your way, you should take it patiently. Paul said, ["Tribulation worketh patience"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 5:3). But realize that patient endurance of an affliction brought about by your [own faults ]{.class_s35U}is profitless. You get nothing for it at the Judgment Seat of Christ.

If you want ["glory"]{.class_s35V} from God for suffering, here is what you have to do. You have to ["do well."]{.class_s35V} But that's not enough. You have to ["suffer for it."]{.class_s35V} Then you have to ["take it patiently." "This is acceptable with God."]{.class_s35V}

God rewards you when you suffer for doing right and being patient as you go through it. Paul adds giving thanks to God, as well (Eph. 5:20; 1 Thess. 5:18). When you do that, you will be rewarded.

21 For even hereunto were ye called: because Christ also suffered for us, leaving us an example, that ye should follow his steps:

22 Who did no sin, neither was guile found in his mouth:

23 Who, when he was reviled, reviled not again; when he suffered, he threatened not; but committed himself to him that judgeth righteously:

24 Who his own self bare our sins in his own body on the tree, that we, being dead to sins, should live unto righteousness: by whose stripes ye were healed.

25 For ye were as sheep going astray; but are now returned unto the Shepherd and Bishop of your souls.

Notice, in verse 21, that part of the Christian's calling is to suffer for Jesus Christ. That's what the ["hereunto"]{.class_s35V} refers back to in verse 20.

Christians are ["called to be saints"]{.class_s35V} (1 Cor. 1:2). They are ["called unto the fellowship of his Son Jesus Christ"]{.class_s35V} (1 Cor. 1:9). They are ["called\...into the grace of Christ"]{.class_s35V} (Gal. 1:6) and ["called unto liberty"]{.class_s35V} (Gal. 5:13). They are called to render ["blessing"]{.class_s35V} (1 Pet. 3:9), and they are called ["to glory and virtue"]{.class_s35V} (2 Pet. 1:3). They are called to ["eternal life"]{.class_s35V} (1 Tim. 6:12). And the ultimate Christian calling is to be ["conformed to the image"]{.class_s35V} of Jesus Christ (Rom. 8:29--30).

Now, the same God who called the Christian to all of [those things ]{.class_s35U}called the Christian to suffer patiently for well-doing. You don't hear many messages on that, but []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_291}it is the case. When Saul of Taursus got saved, the Lord said, ["For I will shew him how great things he must SUFFER for my name's sake"]{.class_s35V} (Acts 9:16).

["Because Christ also suffered for us."]{.class_s35V} You are called to suffer for Christ because the Lord suffered for you. Hebrews 5:8 says, ["Though he were a Son, yet learned he obedience by the things which he suffered."]{.class_s35V}

["Leaving us an example, that ye should follow his steps."]{.class_s35V} There  are two times in the Scriptures that Christ is said to be our example. One is here in verse 21; [He is our example of suffering.]{.class_s35U}

The other is given by Christ Himself in John 13:15. ["For I have given you an example, that ye should do as I have done."]{.class_s35V} The Lord had just finished washing the disciples' feet. He was giving them an example of how to minister to each other using the "word."

Galatians 6:1, ["Brethren, if a man be overtaken in a fault, ye which are spiritual, restore such an one in the spirit of meekness."]{.class_s35V}

Both those examples are Pauline, so both those examples are for the New Testament Christian. According to the Scriptures, if you are saved, you should follow Christ's example of [humility ]{.class_s35U}and [forgiveness ]{.class_s35U}and His example of [suffering for doing right]{.class_s35U}. But both of those examples are set for discipleship, not salvation.

The Liberal teaching is that Christ suffered to set a "moral example" for mankind. In other words, the sufferings of Christ should cause us to be sorry for our wicked lives and to "turn over a new leaf," and this is what gains us access into Heaven.

[REFORMATION ]{.class_s35U}IS NOT [SALVATION]{.class_s35U}.

The best example of this view is a book by a Congregational minister named Charles Sheldon. Sheldon wrote a book called [In His Steps,]{.class_s35U} and it is considered a Christian "classic." It's recommended by almost every church, Christian bookstore, and Bible school.

It is one of the biggest piece of Liberal junk that has ever been written and placed on the market.

At the end of that book, the author is pontificating, and he says, "It is time we gave a [new definition]{.class_s35U} of a Christian."

It is? You mean the definition given in Acts 11:26, Acts 26:28, and 1 Peter 4:16 isn't good enough anymore?

"What is a Christian?" continues Sheldon. "He is one who would do what Jesus would do if [He were here."]{.class_s35U}

Hence, the recent marketing fad (\$\$\$) among "Christians": "WWJD?" ["What would Jesus do?"]{.class_s35U} That may be good for conning a stupid, Laodicean Christian out of a few bucks, but that has nothing to do with [becoming]{.class_s35U} a Christian or [living]{.class_s35U} the Christian life.

One time, a Christian walked into a Christian bookstore looking for a T-shirt with a Gospel message on it. The clerk showed him to a rack with T-shirts all bearing the [WWJD?]{.class_s35U} logo on them. Each one was marked \$25.00.

Curious, the Christian asked the clerk, "What does this [WWJD?]{.class_s35U} thing mean?"

"Well," replied the clerk, "it stands for 'What Would Jesus Do?' Every time you get in a questionable situation you should ask yourself 'What would Jesus do if He were here?'"

"I see," said the Christian, and with that he turned and began to walk out of the store.

"Wait a second!" cried the clerk. "I thought you wanted to buy a T-shirt."

"I did," said the Christian, "but then I asked myself 'What would Jesus do?' And [I don't think He would spend \$25.00 for one of those T-shirts."]{.class_s35U}

You say, "Now there you go again, Dr. Ruckman: ranting and raving because you think you're right and everyone else is wrong." [You better believe it, brother. ]{.class_s35U}In this case, I am absolutely right, and any other opinion about the matter is sheer [religious nonsense.]{.class_s35U}

For example?

For example---you have to repent of your sin and accept a sinless sacrifice even to become a Christian (Acts 20:21, 26:20; 1 Cor. 15:1--4). [Did Jesus have to do that? ]{.class_s35U}Of course not!

Hebrews 7:26--27, ["For such an high priest became us, who is holy, harmless, undefiled, separate from sinners, and made higher than the heavens; WHO NEEDETH NOT daily, as those high priests, TO OFFER UP SACRIFICE, FIRST FOR HIS OWN SINS."]{.class_s35V}

"What would Jesus do?" Well, He sure wouldn't repent of any sin since[ He never committed any. ]{.class_s35U}And you think following [WWJD]{.class_s35U}? is going to make you a Christian? You have another "think" comin'.

"But Dr. Ruckman, you [know]{.class_s35U} that isn't what he meant. He was talking to people who were already saved."

You think so, huh? Well, let's just test his thesis on the life of a saved sinner to see if it makes him a "Christian."

Matthew 15:22, 26, ["And, behold, a woman of Canaan came out of the same coasts, and cried unto him, saying, Have mercy on me, O Lord, thou []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_294}son of David; my daughter is grievously vexed with a devil\...But he answered and said, It is not meet to take the children's bread, and to cast it to the dogs."]{.class_s35V}

Here is some poor Gentile woman begging the Lord for mercy and deliverance for her daughter, and Jesus calls them both ["dogs."]{.class_s35V} Do you know what the name of a [female dog ]{.class_s35U}is, in modern parlance? [Just try that the next time you go on door-to-door visitation and see how far you get with the "prospect"!]{.class_s35U}

What would Jesus do? He would call a corrupt government official a ["fox"]{.class_s35V} (Luke 13:32). He would call the leaders of another religion hypocrites, fools, blind guides, ["whited sepulchres,"]{.class_s35V} serpents, a ["generation of vipers,"]{.class_s35V} and children of Hell (Matt. 23). He would call one of His own church members ["Satan"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 16:23).

Question: Do you know anyone, who subscribes to Sheldon's philosophy, that talks like [that?]{.class_s35U} Do you even know anyone, outside of that arch-heretic Peter S. Ruckman, who talks like [that?]{.class_s35U}

Why not? THAT IS WHAT [JESUS ]{.class_s35U}DID!

You see, when these goody-little-two-shoes talk about what would Jesus [do]{.class_s35U}, they do not mean [what Jesus did according to the Scriptures. ]{.class_s35U}They actually mean "What do I [think]{.class_s35U} that Jesus would do?" They then fashion a Jesus out of John 3:16, the Sermon on the Mount, Psalm 23, and 1 Corinthians 13.

Their "Jesus" is kind of like the Jesus of Stewart Custer (BJU), who said, "There is never a particle of bitterness or unkindness in the words of the Lord Jesus Christ" (Ruckman, [Custer's Last Stand,]{.class_s35U} Bible Baptist Bookstore, 1986, ppg. 51--52; citing pg. 30 of Stewart []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_295}Custer's [The Truth About the King James Version Controversy]{.class_s35U}).

These sanctimonious sissies have forgotten that the [Jesus ]{.class_s35U}of the New Testament is the [Jehovah ]{.class_s35U}of the Old Testament (1 John 5:20). He is the same God of whom Moses wrote, ["And it shall come to pass, that as the ]{.class_s35V}[Lord ]{.class_s360}[rejoiced over you to do you good\...so the ]{.class_s35V}[Lord ]{.class_s360}[will rejoice over you TO DESTROY you, and TO BRING YOU TO NOUGHT"]{.class_s35V} (Deut. 28:63). He said, ["I will heap mischiefs upon them; I will spend mine arrows upon them. They shall be burnt with hunger, and devoured with burning heat, and with bitter destruction: I will also send the teeth of beasts upon them, with the poison of serpents of the dust. The sword without, and terror within, shall destroy both the young man and the virgin, the suckling with the man of gray hairs"]{.class_s35V} (Deut. 32:23--25).

[He's the same God who drowned the entire population of the earth in the days of Noah. ]{.class_s35U}He's the same God who burnt Sodom and Gomorrah to the ground. In both instances, [He killed the innocent babies along with the perverted adults.]{.class_s35U}

Just because that was not part of His commission at the first coming (Luke 9:55--56) doesn't mean He won't do it again. The unsaved, during the Tribulation, say of Him, ["And said to the mountains and rocks, Fall on us, and hide us from the face of him that sitteth on the throne, and from the WRATH OF THE LAMB"]{.class_s35V} (Rev. 6:16).

That's ["the Lamb of God, which taketh away the sin of the world"]{.class_s35V} (John 1:29) about whom they are []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_296}talking. It's "gentle Jesus meek and mild," "the lowly Galilean."

He's the One Who comes ["]{.class_s35V}[in flaming fire taking vengeance]{.class_s363-0}[ on them that know not God, and that obey not the gospel of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class_s35V} (2 Thess. 1:8) Someday He will declare, ["]{.class_s35V}[Depart from me, ye cursed, into everlasting fire]{.class_s363-0}[, prepared for the devil and his angels"]{.class_s35V} (Matt. 25:41).

That is the Jesus of [the Book:]{.class_s35U} the entire Book, not just the parts you like. He's the same Jesus who said, ["Suffer the little children to come unto me, and forbid them not: for of such is the kingdom of God"]{.class_s35V} (Mark 10:14).

If you are going to ask "What Would Jesus Do," you have to consider [that]{.class_s35U}. If you don't, you're not honest; you're nothing but a self-righteous Liberal.

Now, the fact of the matter is that there are [some ]{.class_s35U}points of Christ's earthly life you can follow and there are some points that you [can't. ]{.class_s35U}How do you know which are which? You follow the example that the Holy Spirit set for the New Testament Christian: the Apostle Paul.

First Corinthians 11:1, ["]{.class_s35V}[Be ye followers of me,]{.class_s363-0}[ even as I also am of Christ."]{.class_s35V}

First Timothy 1:16, ["Howbeit for this cause I obtained mercy, ]{.class_s35V}[that in me first Jesus Christ might shew forth all longsuffering, for a pattern]{.class_s363-0}[ to them which should hereafter believe on him to life everlasting."]{.class_s35V}

When Paul followed Jesus Christ and was made a pattern of Jesus Christ, he did not stop at His ascension. For as anyone knows, Christ was a pork-abstaining, []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_297}sabbath-observing, temple-worshipping Jew who never preached ["the gospel of the grace of God"]{.class_s35V} (Acts 20:24) to Gentiles one time between Luke 2:7 and Acts 1:9 (see Matt. 4:23 and 10:5--7 and comments in that Commentary).

When Paul followed Jesus Christ, he followed not only His [example]{.class_s35U}, but His [revelation ]{.class_s35U}as well (Gal. 1:11--12). That revelation contained many things that ["Christ after the flesh"]{.class_s35V} (2 Cor. 5:16) would never do, because, in the flesh, [Jesus Christ was an Old Testament Jew. ]{.class_s35U}You are a New Testament Christian!

So don't follow Charles Sheldon down a path that, logically, leads to Seventh-day Adventism, Roman Catholicism, and Hell, I might add.

Now, how did Christ set His example for us?

1\) ["Who did no sin"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 22). [That's]{.class_s35U} a good example for a Christian to follow. [You shouldn't sin. ]{.class_s35U}There's nothing wrong with that. You will never reach sinless perfection down here, like Jesus Christ did, but you can sure go longer [without sinning ]{.class_s35U}than you can sinning.

I timed myself once. I made an effort to go as long as I could without committing one sin, and I timed myself by the clock. Try it yourself sometime. Try it for five minutes. For five minutes make a concerted effort not to sin in thought, word, or deed. It's a lot harder than you think, but you can do it.

Well, if you can go for five minutes without sinning, then go for ten. If you can succeed for ten minutes, try fifteen, then thirty, then an hour, etc. But make an effort [not to sin!]{.class_s35U}

2\) ["Neither was guile found in his mouth."]{.class_s35V} He didn't twist words or trick anyone into doing anything with His speech. He didn't use ["good words []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_298}and fair speeches"]{.class_s35V} to ["deceive the hearts of the simple"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 16:18).

That is why, earlier, I used examples of the [negative]{.class_s35U} things Christ said to people. That was to show you the difference between the Jesus Christ of [fact]{.class_s35U} and the Jesus Christ of [fiction. ]{.class_s35U}The Lord Jesus Christ would never flatter you or "butter you up" to get anything out of you. He was always straight forward in His speech.

Someone wrote the Bookstore the other day complaining about the way I talked. I get that complaint all the time. "Ruckman is too crude; he's always calling people [names]{.class_s35U}."

Brethren, the speech of the greatest Christian who ever lived was called ["rude"]{.class_s35V} (2 Cor. 11:6) and ["contemptible"]{.class_s35V} (2 Cor. 10:10). The one who told preachers to use ["sound speech, that cannot be condemned"]{.class_s35V} (Titus 2:8), said in the same book, of a certain race of people: ["The Cretians are alway liars, evil beasts, slowbellies. THIS WITNESS IS TRUE. Wherefore rebuke them sharply"]{.class_s35V} (Titus 1:12--13). How is [that]{.class_s35U} for ["sound speech, that cannot be condemned."]{.class_s35V}

Christians, nowadays, have a funny idea about how a Christian is supposed to talk, think, and act. They are that way because they have allowed their thinking to be ["conformed to this world"]{.class_s35V} (Rom. 12:2). This present world system is so concerned about "political correctness" and "hate speech" and "tolerance" that they are all a bunch of thin-skinned sissies who can't tolerate any word or opinion outside of their own designs. Christians have gotten that way too, because they spend more time in front of the "glass toilet" (the TV) and []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_299}listening to the radio than they do reading and studying their Bibles.

3\) ["Who, when he was reviled, reviled not again; when he suffered, he threatened not"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 23). When the guards were smiting Him and reviling Him, He didn't get nasty back with them. If you want to see how Jesus Christ acted as compared with how you are [not]{.class_s35U}[ ]{.class_s36E}supposed to react, get John 18:22--23 in one hand and Acts 23:2--3 in the other.

John 18:22--23. This is Jesus before the high priest. ["And when he had thus spoken, one of the officers which stood by struck Jesus with the palm of his hand, saying, Answerest thou the high priest so? Jesus answered him, ]{.class_s35V}[If I have spoken evil, bear witness of the evil: but if well, why smitest thou me?"]{.class_s363-0}

Now, look at what Paul does in a similar situation. Acts 23:2--3, ["And the high priest Ananias commanded them that stood by him to smite him on the mouth. Then said Paul unto him,]{.class_s35V}[ God shall smite thee, thou whited wall:]{.class_s363-0}[ for sittest thou to judge me after the law, and commandest me to be smitten contrary to the law?"]{.class_s35V}

Paul didn't exactly follow the example of the Lord Jesus Christ there. He kinda "lost his cool." Unlike Christ, he threatened (["God shall smite thee"]{.class_s35V}), and he reviled (["thou whited wall"]{.class_s35V}). That wasn't too "Christlike."

4\) ["But committed himself to him that judgeth righteously."]{.class_s35V} When you are being unjustly persecuted, that is the thing to do. That goes for [any ]{.class_s35U}relationship: family problems, church problems, social problems, or []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_300}any other kinds of problems. When an enemy starts putting the pressure on, you go to [God]{.class_s35U}. You give your problem (in this case, the person persecuting you) to God.

You go to the Lord and say, "Lord, So and so is saying this and believes this and is doing this. I have done everything I possibly can to be right with you and to be right with them. Now, Lord, you heard it, you saw it, and you know what's going on; so Lord, [you ]{.class_s35U}deal with it. I commit my cause to [you]{.class_s35U}. From now on, I will only deal with you about this situation." Then you [back off ]{.class_s35U}and let the Lord deal with the thing Himself. Keep your hands (and your big mouth) off the matter.

One of two things will happen, if you do that. Either the Lord will deal with [you ]{.class_s35U}first, if there is a character flaw He is trying to remove from your life, and then He will deal with [them ]{.class_s35U}(as He did in the case of Job and his friends---see Job 42), or He will deal with them in His own time. And don't you worry; if you let the Lord deal with them, He will be far more effective than ANYTHING [you ]{.class_s35U}could have done.

Now, the four things Peter listed in verses 22--23 are all things[ you can do]{.class_s35U} to follow Christ's example of suffering. That's what Peter means when he says ["ye should follow his steps."]{.class_s35V} But verse 24 is something that Jesus Christ did [for you]{.class_s35U} that you can't do for yourself or anyone else. You can tell whether a man is a born-again Christian or an unsaved Liberal by whether he is following verse 24 or verse 21 to gain merit before God.

Verse 24: ["Who his own self bare our sins."]{.class_s35V} He didn't "share" them like this modern bunch teaches. He took them completely.

["In his own body on the tree."]{.class_s35V} That's a reference to the cross. Paul said, ["Christ hath redeemed us from the curse of the law, being made a curse for us: for it is written, Cursed is every one that hangeth on a tree"]{.class_s35V} (Gal. 3:13). Colossians 2:14, ["Blotting out the handwriting of ordinances that was against us, which was contrary to us, and took it out of the way, nailing it to his cross."]{.class_s35V}

Notice how specific the Holy Spirit gets in regards to the cross. It is not just ["a tree"]{.class_s35V} (Gal. 3:13); it is ["THE tree"]{.class_s35V} (1 Pet. 2:24). It is not just any cross; it is ["HIS cross"]{.class_s35V} (Col. 2:14), which becomes ["THE cross"]{.class_s35V} that creates the Body of Christ (Eph. 2:16).

There is nothing "holy" about a cross. There was certainly nothing holy about Hitler's "iron cross" or the KKK's "burning cross." If you go around wearing a cross, you might as well be wearing an [electric chair. ]{.class_s35U}Roman crosses were instruments of [execution]{.class_s35U}.

What made the cross of Christ special was the [man ]{.class_s35U}who hung on it and what [He accomplished]{.class_s35U} when He hung there. That is what made Christ's physical cross important. [But after Christ was taken down, the cross meant no more than the crosses of the two dying thieves. ]{.class_s35U}You can collect pieces of the "true cross" until you have enough to build a ranch-style house, and the only thing that they will be good for is a [huge bonfire]{.class_s35U} at the Judgment Seat of Christ (or the Great White Throne).

What makes the cross important to us today is its message (1 Cor. 1:18) and its spiritual application to the old nature (Rom. 6:3--13; Gal. 2:20). So Peter says in verse 24, ["that we, being dead to sins, should live unto righteousness."]{.class_s35V}

Observe, again, the Pauline emphasis in 1 Peter. You can't consign the doctrinal application of the whole epistle to the Tribulation. It just won't work. It is [wrongly]{.class_s36G} ["dividing the word of truth."]{.class_s35V}

["By whose stripes ye were healed."]{.class_s35V} That is a quote from Isaiah 53:5. Notice that, here, the healing is a [spiritual]{.class_s35U} healing from the effects of sin on your [spirit. ]{.class_s35U}When the whip was brought down on Christ's back, that was part of God laying your sins on Him. When Christ was being whipped and the blood was coming out, the atonement had already started. [Technically]{.class_s35U}, the atonement began in Gethsemane when ["his sweat was as it were great drops of blood falling down to the ground"]{.class_s35V} (Luke 22:44).

Now, after the crucifixion, and after the Body of Christ began at Pentecost, the healing of Isaiah 53:5 is spiritual. But before the crucifixion, that healing was a physical sign to Israel.

Matthew 8:16--17, ["When the even was come, they brought unto him many that were possessed with devils: and he cast out the spirits with his word, and healed all that were sick: That it might be fulfilled which was spoken by Esaias the prophet, saying, ]{.class_s35V}[Himself took our infirmities, and bare our sicknesses]{.class_s363-0}[."]{.class_s35V} That last verse is a quote from Isaiah 53:4.

The Holiness and Pentecostal folks have developed a theology from Matthew 8:17, which we call "Whipping Post" theology. The idea is that there is [physical healing]{.class_s35U} in the atonement.

But note, carefully, how finely the Holy Spirit divides and applies Isaiah 53:4--5. First, Matthew 8:17 is a free quote of Isaiah 53:4. The original says, ["Surely he []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_303}hath borne our GRIEFS"]{.class_s35V} (not ["sicknesses"]{.class_s35V}) ["and carried our sorrows"]{.class_s35V} (not ["infirmities"]{.class_s35V}). So as the Holy Spirit often does in the New Testament, you have an application made in the translation that is not necessarily found [in the original]{.class_s35U}. (The implication applied to the [King James Bible]{.class_s35U} and the "original manuscripts" is important, but we simply do not have time to go into it here. For further study, I would suggest you get [King James Onlyism vs. Scholarship Onlyism]{.class_s35U} and [How to Teach the "Original" Greek]{.class_s35U} from the Bible Baptist Bookstore.)

Second, in both Isaiah 53 and the New Testament, the healing comes BEFORE the atonement. Christ had not yet been whipped in Matthew 8. Moreover, the healing is not complete until [long after the atonement is made.]{.class_s35U}

Now, instead of trying to wrest the signs given to Israel (1 Cor. 1:22), through Christ and the apostles (Mark 16:17--18 cf. 2 Cor. 12:12), away from them (either one---the givers or the "givees"), let's look at what God does with this thing in the Scriptures.

Before the crucifixion, Jesus Christ and the apostles performed acts of healing, in fulfillment of Isaiah 53:4, so that the Jews would know that the One who made the physical healing possible was the One who was going to die for their sins (Isa. 53:5). Those [signs to Israel ]{.class_s35U}passed on into the book of Acts, but they died out as the Lord stopped dealing with Israel as a nation and turned to the Gentiles.

Today, in the Church Age, when you receive Jesus Christ as your Saviour, your spirit receives [spiritual healing ]{.class_s35U}and is made alive. It will never die again; that spiritual healing is a permanent thing. You no longer have a [spiritual problem]{.class_s35U} with God. You may have a []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_304}spiritual problem with yourself and have to fight the Devil until you die, but as far as God is concerned, everything is fixed spiritually.

But when you got saved, nothing happened to your [body ]{.class_s35U}at all. [It is the same body you had before you were saved.]{.class_s35U}

Now, if you had a diseased liver [before ]{.class_s35U}you were saved and the Lord healed you, thank God, brother. But God didn't give you a [new liver.]{.class_s35U}

I have seen the Lord take one of our students, who damaged his brain on drugs, and give him his memory and mental skills back and make him a missionary in Papua, New Guinea. Praise the Lord! But his brain is the [same brain]{.class_s35U} that got cooked on drugs.

There was a young man who attended PBI who lost a leg before he was saved. He got on drugs or alcohol (I can't recall which) one night and passed out with one of his legs across a railroad track. When he woke up, he didnt' have that leg anymore: a train had come along and taken it off. That young man got saved and is serving the Lord today in the Ukraine as a missionary. He's a tremendous witness for Jesus Christ. [But God didn't grow him a new leg!]{.class_s35U}

Our Holiness, Pentecostal, and Charismatic brethren keep getting the [physical signs to Israel ]{.class_s35U}mixed up with the [spiritual operations on the Church. ]{.class_s35U}When Christ died on the cross, His blood atonement not only paid the price of your sin debt,[ it redeemed the earth from the curse placed on it in Genesis 3. ]{.class_s35U}But that redemption isn't [in force]{.class_s35U} until the One who paid it takes physical possession of it at His [return]{.class_s35U}.

When the Lord Jesus Christ returns for His Church at the Rapture, [that's]{.class_s35U} when the[ physical healing ]{.class_s35U}in the []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_305}atonement is applied to the Christian---and it will be [permanent]{.class_s35U}. For Israel, that physical healing takes place partially in the Millennium, and then permanently in the new earth. Until then, you can count on hospital beds and graves, and ["with his stripes we are healed"]{.class_s35V} won't slow them down one bit.

These Charismatic nuts think that all the benefits of atonement are available NOW. [All the benefits of the atonement are NOT available now]{.class_s35U}. The surest proof of that is when one of these "faith healers" gets sick, he never goes to another faith healer. [He goes to a doctor.]{.class_s35U}

When Katherine Kuhlman got sick (and eventually died), she didn't go to Oral Roberts or T. L. Osborne, although both were in close proximity. [She went to a hospital.]{.class_s35U}

During the Brownsville Revival, John Kilpatrick (pastor of the Brownsville Assembly of God) was working on the roof of the three million dollar home he was building. He fell off and broke his hip or leg; I can't remember which. Do you think he went to the evangelist he had in for the "Revival," Stephen Hill? Of course not. [He went to the hospital too and recovered in the same time and manner it would take anyone else.]{.class_s35U}

When all of the effects of the atonement are complete, you will be able to play with a black mamba (the world's deadliest snake) and not worry. You will be able to use a lion as your pillow, because you won't be his bedtime snack anymore (Isa. 11). If you think that is the case [now]{.class_s35U}, you are nuttier than a pecan pie.

Listen, brother, if [all ]{.class_s35U}of the benefits of the atonement are now, what makes you think that you have enough faith to be saved if you don't have enough faith to be [healed]{.class_s35U}. THEY'RE [BOTH ]{.class_s35U}IN THE ATONEMENT.

That is why all of these poor, sincere, stupid Charismatics are always[ doubting their salvation]{.class_s35U}. They went to some faith healer with a problem, and nothing happened. The healer blames it on their [lack of faith. ]{.class_s35U}So naturally [they question the faith they had to get saved. ]{.class_s35U}And if you can "lose your healing," like all of these Charismatic fakirs teach, then can't you [lose your salvation]{.class_s35U}? After all---[they're both in the atonement.]{.class_s35U}

You may get [some ]{.class_s35U}benefits of the atonement now and be healed, but eventually, you will die. Well, didn't Christ say, ["Whosoever liveth and believeth in me shall never die"]{.class_s35V} (John 11:26)? Yes, He did. But that won't take place until the Rapture.

So although physical healing [is]{.class_s35U} in the atonement, you won't get [complete healing ]{.class_s35U}until the return of Jesus Christ.

["For ye were as sheep going astray"]{.class_s35V} (vs. 25). That's taken from Isaiah 53:6. Doctrinally, it is Israel (Matt. 10:6; Luke 19:10 cf. Matt. 18:11--14). Spiritually, it can be anybody (John 10; Rom. 8:36). That is why Paul uses the term ["pastors"]{.class_s35V} in reference to the elders and bishops in the local churches. A [pastor]{.class_s35U} is another name for a shepherd (Jer. 2:8, 3:15, 10:21, 12:10, 22:22, 23:1--2).

Finally, you should note in verse 25 that Jesus Christ is called ["the Shepherd"]{.class_s35V} (that's a pastor) ["and Bishop"]{.class_s35V} (that's an overseer in Acts 20:28) ["of your souls."]{.class_s35V} Jesus Christ is the [highest rank]{.class_s35U} there is in the church: He is its ["head"]{.class_s35V} (Col. 1:18). That means this: if Jesus Christ is the ["Bishop of your souls"]{.class_s35V} and that is the [highest rank]{.class_s35U} in the church, then any church that claims to have "Archbishops" [is trying to usurp authority over Jesus Christ]{.class_s35U}. An Archbishop is one rank higher than []{#c1MX.xhtml_page_307}a Bishop. [So both Catholics and Episcopalians claim to be higher in authority than Jesus Christ.]{.class_s35U}

And then, for our "Baptist Brider brethren," notice that Jesus Christ is ["the Shepherd\...of your souls."]{.class_s35V} So He's [not ]{.class_s35U}a pastor (shepherd) over a [local church. ]{.class_s35U}That means there is such a thing as the Universal Church made up of [all ]{.class_s35U}saved people.

The standard reply to this is 1) "Who is the pastor?" 2) "Where does it meet?" and 3) "How can I join?"

1\) Its Pastor is the Lord Jesus Christ (1 Pet. 2:25).

2\) It is seated ["together in heavenly places in Christ Jesus"]{.class_s35V} (Eph. 2:6).

3\) You [join ]{.class_s35U}by being baptized by the Holy Spirit of God into that body at salvation (1 Cor. 12:13; Col. 2:10--13).

[]{#c1ZK.xhtml}

## Chapter 3 {.heading_s3A-0}

3:1 Likewise, ye wives, be in subjection to your own husbands; that, if any obey not the word, they also may without the word be won by the conversation of the wives;

2 While they behold your chaste conversation coupled with fear.

3 Whose adorning let it not be that outward adorning of plaiting the hair, and of wearing of gold, or of putting on of apparel;

4 But let it be the hidden man of the heart, in that which is not corruptible, even the ornament of a meek and quiet spirit, which is in the sight of God of great price.

5 For after this manner in the old time the holy women also, who trusted in God, adorned themselves, being in subjection unto their own husbands:

6 Even as Sara obeyed Abraham, calling him lord: whose daughters ye are, as long as ye do well, and are not afraid with any amazement.

This passage is one of the roughest places in the Bible for [women]{.class_s35S}; especially verse 6. Peter commands Christian wives to be ["in subjection unto their own husbands."]{.class_s35R} The Apostle Paul says, ["Wives, submit yourselves unto your own husbands, as unto the Lord"]{.class_s35R} (Eph. 5:22). The command is the same; the words ["subjection"]{.class_s35R} and ["submit"]{.class_s35R} are synonyms that mean the same thing.

When Peter says ["likewise,"]{.class_s35R} he is referring back to what he said in chapter 2, verses 13 and 18. Just as every Christian is to submit himself to the government and just as every slave is to ["be subject"]{.class_s35R} to his master (and just as Christ ["committed []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_309}himself"]{.class_s35R} to the Father back in 1 Pet. 2:23), in the same manner, the wife is to subject herself to her husband.

Now, whenever the Lord addresses the man and the woman together (and He is about to give instruction to the man down in vs. 7), He always speaks to the [woman ]{.class_s35S}first. You'll find this in Genesis. When God speaks to Adam and Eve, the first admonition is to Eve. In Ephesians 5 and Colossians 3, when God speaks to husbands and wives, the [first ]{.class_s35S}admonition is to the wife. And the same is true here in 1 Peter 3.

["That, if any obey not the word."]{.class_s35R} Every major Bible expositor in America will tell you that that is a reference to an unsaved man. Now, I think you can make [application ]{.class_s35S}to that, and I do. But I don't believe that is what Peter is taking about, here.

First, Peter never says the man is [lost]{.class_s35S}. Do you mean to tell me that you have never known a Christian man who did not do what the Scriptures told him to do? Paul did (Gal. 3:1, 5:7; 2 Thess. 3:14--15).

But more than that, the illustration Peter gives to the women to whom he writes is that of [Sarah and Abraham ]{.class_s35S}(vss. 5--6). Abraham was [not ]{.class_s35S}a lost man; he was [saved]{.class_s35S}. But there were at least two times in the book of Genesis (chapters 12 and 20) when Abraham did not [obey ]{.class_s35S}God. He lied about his wife, and yet, both times, Sarah submitted herself to his wishes.

So in verse 1, Peter is writing to Christian women [who are married to Christian men who are not doing right]{.class_s35S}. The problem is not a saved woman trying to win her lost husband to the Lord. The problem is how can a [saved ]{.class_s35S}woman subject herself to a [saved ]{.class_s35S}man and get him right when he's [not]{.class_s35S} doing right and she [knows]{.class_s35S} he's not doing right.

The answer to that problem is this: ["they also may without the word be won by the conversation of the wives."]{.class_s35R} So, ladies, if that fellow won't listen to what the Bible []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_310}says about a matter, God can use something else to reach him. And what the Lord [won't]{.class_s35S} use is a [nagging tongue]{.class_s35S} to win that man.

["The conversation of the wives,"]{.class_s35R} in verse 1, has nothing to do with a woman [saying ]{.class_s35S}anything to her husband. Look at verse 2: ["while they may BEHOLD your chaste conversation."]{.class_s35R} The word ["conversation,"]{.class_s35R} here [in this context]{.class_s35S}, is your[ manner of life]{.class_s35S}, ladies: it's the [way you live.]{.class_s35S}

People always think I'm so "macho" and "male chauvinistic" by the way I talk, but the fact of the matter is, I pity the circumstances of a lot of Christian women, especially those who live down South. The South has, literally, hundreds of thousands of [saved ]{.class_s35S}women in it who are either married to [unsaved ]{.class_s35S}men or who have Christian husbands who have done nothing for the Lord but make a profession of faith and join the church.

When a woman down South really gets hungry for the word of God, nine times out of ten, she has a tremendous drag at home. It's a real pity. The [man ]{.class_s35S}ought to be the leader in spiritual things.

Any man reading this Commentary ought to know more Scripture than his wife. That is the way it [ought]{.class_s35S} to be, but it's not that way down South. The wife of the average man down South will beat him in Scripture knowledge every time.

I have seen this disparity throughout my ministry. The husband will drive his wife to church and drop her off, and then pick her up after the service. He [may]{.class_s35S} actually come with her at Easter and Christmas.

I have talked with a lot of men who are like that. They aren't "bad" men. [They just don't have a spiritual bone in their entire body. ]{.class_s35S}They are just carnal, easygoing, hunting, fishing, time-clock-punching "good ole' boys." They love their wife and kids, and they love "gettin' together" with the kin folk on the weekend.

That must be rough for a woman who is spiritual and loves the Lord and loves the Book and wants to do something for Jesus Christ. I sympathize with you, lady. If I were a woman (and thank God I'm not!), I'd sure get fed up with a man like that. The only remedy is for the wife to win him by the life that she lives in front of him.

You take that case between Abraham and Sarah. Don't you know Sarah questioned the wisdom and spirituality of her husband when he told her [to lie? ]{.class_s35S}But she did what Abraham asked, and God worked the circumstances out so that Abraham was put under conviction. As soon as she obeyed her husband, like she was supposed to do, the Lord showed up and intervened on her behalf. Abraham got put on the spot and rebuked by both Pharaoh and Abimilech. Sarah didn't have to say a word. And what's more, Sarah bore none of the blame for what happened.

Now, ladies, when Paul gives the command to submit to your husbands, he says to do it ["as unto the Lord."]{.class_s35R} I have been in counselling sessions where I have told the woman that, and she [laughed]{.class_s35S}. She said, ["Him?!]{.class_s35S} Like [the Lord?!"]{.class_s35S} And she had good reason to react that way. But that's what you [have]{.class_s35S} to do.

Your attitude should be this: "Lord, I am married to this man, and he's not following you as he ought to do. I am going to let [you ]{.class_s35S}handle him. When he asks me to do something that I don't like I am going to do it [as if you were asking me to do it]{.class_s35S} and not him. I am submitting myself to that man, [as you asked me to do."]{.class_s35S}

That's right, ladies. That's what you have to do: [put the responsibility right back on the Lord]{.class_s35S}. That's not blasphemy or sacrilegious. After all, [God ]{.class_s35S}told you to submit; [He ]{.class_s35S}told you to do it [as unto Him. ]{.class_s35S}Therefore, it is [His responsibility]{.class_s35S} to reign in that husband when he gets out of line. [It isn't yours.]{.class_s35S}

["While they behold your chaste conversation"]{.class_s35R} (vs. 2). That's living a pure life. That's doing right, ladies, as you have []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_312}the opportunity to do right. It is being faithful to your husband and showing him kindness and love even if he doesn't return it.

["Coupled with fear."]{.class_s35R} Now, you have a seeming contradiction here. Look down at verse 6. ["As long as ye do well, and are not afraid with any amazement."]{.class_s35R} So a woman [is ]{.class_s35S}to fear, but at the same time she is [not ]{.class_s35S}to be afraid.

Of course, the answer lies in the [object]{.class_s35S} of her fear. A Christian woman, as every Christian, is to ["fear God"]{.class_s35R} (vs. 2 cf. 1 Pet. 2:17). She is [not]{.class_s35S} to be afraid of her husband.

A husband can upset his wife and keep her in a psychotic fit because she is afraid of what will happen. She can be afraid the family will break up; she can be afraid for her health; she can be afraid something will happen to the children; she can be afraid about the finances; she can be afraid about the behavior or actions of her husband.

Women tend to be ruled by emotions, and that doesn't impress a man. The less that a woman can get rattled emotionally the more the man gets under conviction. Whenever a wife flies off the handle about something, a husband figures she's in the wrong. The woman has to walk a fine line where she is not living in a constant state of fear, and yet, she does not display a cocky indifference.

Verse 3 is a great verse for Holiness women. No make up, no jewelry, straight hair down to your waist, plain clothing: that's the way they interpret it. But Peter is not saying that a woman can [never]{.class_s35S} braid her hair or wear jewelry. If that is what he is saying then every woman should walk around [naked;]{.class_s35S} notice that he says, ["Whose adorning LET IT NOT BE\...of PUTTING ON OF APPAREL."]{.class_s35R}

Obviously, the ["adorning"]{.class_s35R} of verse 3 is [overdressing]{.class_s35S}. You know that because verse 4 describes it as an ["ornament."]{.class_s35R} An ornament is an [embellishment]{.class_s35S}. It is something added on and beyond the necessary things. What Peter is saying is that a []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_313}woman shouldn't always be calling attention to herself by the fancy clothing, fancy jewelry, and elaborate hairstyles. He is not absolutely forbidding a woman from dressing up, though.

There is nothing wrong, ladies, with putting on makeup. The old saying is "if the barn needs painting, paint it." But don't use so much that you give yourself lead poisoning.

After the PTL fiasco (Jim Bakker), the joke down South was that they removed Tammy Bakker's makeup and found Jimmy Hoffa underneath. That's too much makeup.

The rule for ladies' dress is simple: ["In like manner also, that women adorn themselves in modest apparel" ]{.class_s35R}(1 Tim. 2:9). [That takes care of both extremes. ]{.class_s35S}You shouldn't run around half naked or with clothes that leave nothing to the imagination. On the other hand, a woman [can]{.class_s35S} call attention to herself with shabby, unkept clothing or with clothing not appropriate to the situation.

There are times to dress in the nicest clothes that you have and to fix your hair. As long as you are dressing appropriate for the occasion and are not trying to [impress everyone]{.class_s35S} with what you wear, your dress would be modest in those circumstances.

There are times when pants are ["modest apparel"]{.class_s35R} for a woman. One of my youth directors, at one time, insisted that the girls wear knee-length skirts or dresses, no matter what the activity. I warned him that it wouldn't always work, but he didn't listen. We were at camp one summer, and his wife took some girls out on a canoe ride. Well, the canoe tipped over, and those girls were upside down in the water with skirts flapping above their waist. Those skirts weren't too modest on [that ]{.class_s35S}occasion. They weren't too "modest" on the [baseball field]{.class_s35S}, either.

If you dress in such a way as to[ attract undue attention to yourself]{.class_s35S}, [that dress]{.class_s35S} is immodest. And I have seen Holiness women, whose clothing would meet every standard laid down by []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_314}a Fundamentalist, still dress in such a way that it called attention to themselves. [You can't legislate spirituality.]{.class_s35S}

Now, I know you Christian ladies have a hard row to hoe. With all these women walking around dressed like streetwalkers, what are you supposed to do to get, and keep, the attention of a Christian man? After all, you have to have some bait on the hook in order to catch the fish. Well, if he's the right kind of a Christian man, he's going to be looking for more than a clothing store manikin.

The thing that is valuable in a woman is what is [inside ]{.class_s35S}her. That Bible says, ["Favour is deceitful, and beauty is vain: but a woman that feareth the ]{.class_s35R}[Lord]{.class_s35X-0}[, she shall be praised"]{.class_s35R} (Prov. 31:30). A lot of these Hollywood starlets and glamor queens, that are so desired by men because of their beauty, don't make good wives; most of their marriages break up within five years.

If you want a spiritual man, ladies, you have to use [spiritual bait]{.class_s35S} to attract him. If you rely on the flesh to get and keep a man, you will have nothing but a [carnal husband. ]{.class_s35S}But if he is attracted to you by what he sees in your new nature, ["the hidden man of the heart,"]{.class_s35R} then you are getting the right kind of a fellow.

Now, the physical beauty will fade and fashions change. Peter says that the things listed in verse 3 are ["corruptible."]{.class_s35R} But that ["hidden man of the heart"]{.class_s35R} will still be adorning you if you live to be ninety. ["The inward man is renewed day by day,"]{.class_s35R} Paul says (2 Cor. 4:16), so it is just as fresh and young at seventy, eighty, or ninety as it was at twenty-five.

And what is on the inside, shows up on the outside. It is hard to explain, but it shows up on a woman's face and in her demeanor. It has nothing to do with her looks, but you can tell when it's there. And I have known some elderly Christian grandmothers who were more attractive, [spiritually]{.class_s35S}, than women in their teens and twenties.

["Even the ornament of a meek and quiet spirit, which is in the sight of God of great price."]{.class_s35R} That's ["a meek and QUIET spirit,"]{.class_s35R} ladies. The Greek is very strong here. It means "QUIET!!!"

The old saying is "Silence is golden."

Someone said, once, that the perfect marriage would be a [blind]{.class_s35S} wife and a [deaf]{.class_s35S} husband. Of course, the way some men pay attention to what their wives say, the wives would swear that their husbands were deaf anyway.

Now, there are a number of good Proverbs that apply to the text, and lest I say more than some of you women care to hear on the subject, I will simply quote some of them and let those be the comments on the above passage.

Proverbs 21:9 (also 25:24), ["It is better to dwell in a corner of the housetop, than with a ]{.class_s35R}[brawling woman ]{.class_s35W-0}[in a wide house."]{.class_s35R}

Proverbs 21:19, ["It is better to dwell in the wilderness, than with ]{.class_s35R}[a contentious and an angry woman.]{.class_s35W-0}["]{.class_s35R} (Which may explain why some men spend so much time outdoors.)

Proverbs 12:4, ["]{.class_s35R}[A virtuous woman]{.class_s35W-0}[ is a crown to her husband: but she that maketh ashamed is as rottenness in his bones."]{.class_s35R}

Proverbs 31:10--12, ["Who can find a ]{.class_s35R}[virtuous woman]{.class_s35W-0}[? for her price is far above rubies. The heart of her husband doth safely trust in her, so that he shall have no need of spoil. She will do him good and not evil all the days of her life."]{.class_s35R}

Now, men, just because the Bible tells that woman to be ["meek and quiet"]{.class_s35R} doesn't mean that she is a doormat and that she never has an opinion to express. That wife may be one with you physically (Eph. 5:28--31), but from the standpoint of the soul, [the ego]{.class_s35S}, she is still her own person.

There are times when that woman should keep her mouth shut, and there are times when you shouldn't do what she says. Adam shouldn't have listened to [Eve ]{.class_s35S}in Genesis 3:6. Abram shouldn't have listened to [Sarai ]{.class_s35S}in Genesis 16:2.

But there are times when that woman is [right]{.class_s35S}, and you had better listen to her if you want everything to turn out right. You take Sarah and Abraham. Sarah may have been wrong in Genesis 16; but when you get over into Genesis 21:10, Sarah is not only right, God [commands]{.class_s35S} Abraham to do what [she ]{.class_s35S}says (Gen. 21:12). That thing is so strong that the Lord repeats it in the New Testament (Gal. 4:30).

I'll tell you someone else who should have listened to his wife: [Pontius Pilate. ]{.class_s35S}The Lord showed that woman something in a dream, and Pilate should have taken her advice in Matthew 27:19. If he had, things might have turned out differently for him (Acts 4:27).

You say, "How can I tell, then, when my wife is right and when she is wrong." It is simple: when your wife takes [God's side ]{.class_s35S}in a matter, she is right; when she doesn't, she is wrong. [You have to know your Bible, men, to know the difference]{.class_s35S}. You have to be close to the Lord in your prayer life for the Lord to show you the difference.

Now, you ladies, if you want some good examples of how to act as a wife and a mother and a lady, look in the Scriptures. There you will find ["holy women\...who trusted in God."]{.class_s35R} If you want to obey God and be in subjection to your husband as the Lord commanded, don't pick someone like Jean Harlow, Jane Mansfield, Marilyn Monroe, Judy Garland, Katherine Hepburn, Lucille Ball, Madonna, or Britney Spears. And don't watch those soap operas unless you want an education in lying, cheating, deceit, duplicity, adultery, and fornication.

Pick you out someone like Sarah or Rebekah or Esther or Deborah the judge or Ruth or Mary or Elizabeth or one of those []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_317}women. If you go outside the Scriptures, get the biographies of Ann Judson, Catherine Booth, Fanny Crosby, Amy Carmichael, or Madame Guyon. [Don't compare yourself with anyone around you. ]{.class_s35S}Set your sights high.

["Being in subjection unto their own husbands: Even as Sara obeyed Abraham, calling him lord"]{.class_s35R} (vss. 5--6). Now, I am not going to drive this matter of the wife being in subjection to the husband into the ground. I have commented on it sufficiently in verses 1--2.

[Subjection ]{.class_s35S}is the one responsibility the wife has to her husband. Ladies, if you went by the standard wedding vows at your wedding, you promised to love, honor, and [obey ]{.class_s35S}that man. That promise was not conditioned on whether he kept his wedding vows to "cherish" you.

But the fact of human nature is that you [will]{.class_s35S} get into disagreements and fights with your husband, and you will [not ]{.class_s35S}always agree with what he tells you to do. When that happens, the best thing you can do is to [pray]{.class_s35S}. Pray that if he is [wrong ]{.class_s35S}that the Lord will show him and change his mind. But at the same time, pray that if [you]{.class_s35S} are wrong that the Lord will show [you]{.class_s35S} and change [your]{.class_s35S} mind. The husband is [not]{.class_s35S} the one who is always at fault.

["Whose daughters ye are, as long as ye do well"]{.class_s35R} (vs. 6). That, of course, is a spiritual relationship, but it is a spiritual relationship of [works. ]{.class_s35S}It is not like becoming a son of God through faith in the finished work of Jesus Christ. It is following the example of Sarah, and in this case, the example of obeying her husband.

When Paul talks about the Christian being a child of Abraham (Rom. 4; Gal. 3), he is doing what Peter does here. A Christian is a child of Abraham in that he follows [the example]{.class_s35S} of Abraham. But in Abraham's case, the example he sets is one []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_318}of [faith in what God says:]{.class_s35S} imputed righteousness with no works involved.

7 Likewise, ye husbands, dwell with them according to knowledge, giving honour unto the wife, as unto the weaker vessel, and as being heirs together of the grace of life; that your prayers be not hindered.

Now we come to the men after the Lord spends six verses talking to the ladies. I guess your modern feminists and news media would consider that "sexist."

Men, you are commanded to live with your wives ["according to knowledge."]{.class_s35R} That is not just Scriptural knowledge, although [that ]{.class_s35S}is the first kind of knowledge you need to have in a marriage. As I said earlier, a Christian husband should always know more about the Bible than his wife.

But if a husband is not careful, especially one who loves and believes and exalts the Book, he can get to a place where he is going JUST by the Scriptures in dealing with his wife. You have to realize that the Scriptures don't handle [every detail of your life]{.class_s35S}. They give general rules and principles to live by, and then you make decisions according to those general rules and principles as you encounter the varying circumstances of life.

The general principle in a marriage for the man is love. That Bible says, ["Husbands, love your wives, even as Christ also loved the church, and gave himself for it"]{.class_s35R} (Eph. 5:25). Proverbs 10:12 says, ["Love covereth all sins."]{.class_s35R}

If you love your wife the way you should, 90 percent of your problems will be solved. But if you don't love that woman ["according to knowledge,"]{.class_s35R} you are going to make the biggest mess of things you ever saw.

You need to know the traits of the "gender": general characteristics that apply to any woman. You had better know some things about a woman's [chemistry ]{.class_s35S}and [physiology ]{.class_s35S}that []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_319}will affect her [moods]{.class_s35S}. You had better know what women do to get their way. You had better know what women look for in a husband. You had better learn how a woman's mind operates and reasons.

Then you need to know some things about your individual wife. You have to remember that she's a person, and all people are different [in some ways]{.class_s35S}. Some women can have children and some women can't. Some women have no trouble carrying and delivering a child, while others have very difficult times. Some women resent a lack of education, and some [don't. ]{.class_s35S}Some women are quite healthy, and others have physical problems every time you turn around.
