These are things you are going to know about your wife [as a person]{.class_s35S} if you are going to live together for a lifetime.

If you men don't know something you need to know, use some common sense. Look things up; write them down. "Trial and error" is a rough way to go through life with anybody.

I will give some of you young men (and young ladies, for that matter) who are contemplating marriage some good advice from someone who has been "through the mill." Don't make the physical relationship [the reason]{.class_s35S} that you get married. That's a marriage based on [lust]{.class_s35S}, not on [love]{.class_s35S}. A marriage that [starts ]{.class_s35S}out like that, won't [end ]{.class_s35S}right.

You had better know for sure that the one you are marrying is [saved ]{.class_s35S}and loves the Lord---make sure it's both. If you're spiritual and your spouse[ isn't]{.class_s35S}, you will [have ]{.class_s35S}a miserable marriage.

You had better know what your future spouse expects out of married life. If the Lord has called you to preach, men, and that woman doesn't want to be a preacher's wife, you had better hitch your horse to a different wagon. Either you will give up on God's will for your life, or you will live in constant turmoil and strife with that woman if [you do what God called you to do]{.class_s35S}.

You need to know what she is willing to do to follow you, and you need to know what compromises you are willing to make to accommodate her. [Both are involved in a marriage.]{.class_s35S}

[Pray]{.class_s35S} for a long while before you get married. [Love]{.class_s35S} each other when you get married. [Stay]{.class_s35S} in love after you get married. But [know]{.class_s35S} your spouse so that when the problems come that [love won't solve,]{.class_s35S} you can act accordingly.

["Giving honour unto the wife."]{.class_s35R} Husbands, that woman isn't a punching bag or a doormat. She isn't there to have insults heaped on her by you. With all the cooking, cleaning, washing, child-care, and errands she does for you, that woman deserves some respect; she deserves some courtesy; she deserves some kindness; and she deserves [to be treated right]{.class_s35S}.

["As unto the weaker vessel."]{.class_s35R} Now, if we lined all the women in a church up on one side and all the men up on the other and we had a physical "battle of the sexes," there is no doubt that the men would win. As a gender, men are stronger. But women are physically stronger than men in other ways. If you have ever seen a woman have a baby, you know that women have a strength that men don't have. I have seen women overseas in India carry fifty pounds of bricks on their heads. That takes some strength. So ["the weaker vessel"]{.class_s35R} isn't necessarily referring to physical strength.

They're not weaker [mentally]{.class_s35S}. Many women do better in [academics ]{.class_s35S}than men. I don't debate that women can make strong leaders. That's pretty evident, for good and bad, by such women as Catherine de Medici, Catherine the Great of Russia, Queen Victoria, and Margaret Thatcher.

When Peter says the woman is[ "the weaker vessel,"]{.class_s35R} he is speaking [spiritually]{.class_s35S}. The [woman ]{.class_s35S}is more [vulnerable to spiritual attack and spiritual deception than the man is]{.class_s35S}. When Satan went to work on destroying the human couple in the Garden of Eden, [he came to Eve]{.class_s35S}, not Adam.

First Timothy 2:14 says, ["And Adam was not deceived, but the woman being deceived was in the transgression."]{.class_s35R} Paul says that ["the serpent beguiled Eve through his subtilty"]{.class_s35R} (2 Cor. 11:3).

Adam wasn't tricked into eating the forbidden fruit. Adam's problem was that he gave into his wife. He made a conscious decision, [based on his wife's request, to disobey God]{.class_s35S}.

But Eve was tricked by the Devil because she had certain character traits in her makeup to which Satan appealed. She was [curious. ]{.class_s35S}Women have a curiosity about things that are none of their business that men just don't have.

And Eve had a [dissatisfaction ]{.class_s35S}that Adam didn't have because God didn't talk to her personally. Eve wasn't around back in Genesis 2:16--17; she didn't show up until Genesis 2:21--22. Anything that God said, she got [second hand ]{.class_s35S}through her husband. God spoke to Adam before the fall; [He didn't speak to her]{.class_s35S}.

That made Eve dissatisfied and resentful, and that resentment shows up in Genesis 3:2--3 when she subtracts the word ["freely"]{.class_s35R} from God's command in Genesis 2:16 and adds ["neither shall ye touch it"]{.class_s35R} to Genesis 2:17.

Women have a [natural resentment]{.class_s35S} of what God gave to men. They resent the authority and dominion and revelation with which the Lord endowed men. [That is the motivation behind the "women's lib" movement]{.class_s35S}.

The woman is like that because she is a [secondary]{.class_s35S} creation. (See comments on 1 Cor. 11:8--9 in that Commentary.) The woman was not made from the dirt like Adam was; she was made from a rib from Adam. That is why women tend to be more conscious of filth than a man, and why they are more tender than a man.

The woman has no identity outside of the man. Adam was the one who designated the woman [as a woman]{.class_s35S} (Gen. 2:23).

The woman has [no name]{.class_s35S} outside of the man. Eve's name wasn't Eve; her name was ["Adam"]{.class_s35R} (Gen. 5:2). If Adam hadn't called her ["Eve"]{.class_s35R} (Gen. 3:20), the only way that you could have distinguished her would have been to call her "Mrs. Adam." [In the same way, women today have no name of their own]{.class_s35S}. They either bear their [father's]{.class_s35S} name when they're single or their [husband's]{.class_s35S} name when they're married.

The woman is a secondary creation, and she knows it, and she has an [inherent resentment of it]{.class_s35S}. That resentment makes her vulnerable to deception by the Devil, much more so than the [man]{.class_s35S}. No matter how smart a woman thinks she is, SHE CAN BE FOOLED. That susceptibility toward [spiritual temptation ]{.class_s35S}is what makes her ["the weaker vessel."]{.class_s35R}

In your relationship with your wife, men, you have to keep [that ]{.class_s35S}in mind. No matter what airs she puts on, no matter if she is a strong-willed woman, no matter if she thinks (or actually is) more spiritual than you are, she is still ["the weaker vessel."]{.class_s35R} And what's more, SHE KNOWS IT! She knows it whether she will admit it to you or not. So you have to keep that in mind in your dealings with that woman.

["As being heirs together of the grace of life."]{.class_s35R} That is an important thing to remember in a Christian marriage. In a Christian marriage both the man and the woman are saved: they are both members in the Body of Christ. In that sense (and that sense only), the two are equal.

Both of you are saved. Both of you are going to Heaven. Both of you are in the Body of Christ. Both of you possess the indwelling Holy Spirit of God.

If you keep all of that in mind, it will make a difference in the way you act toward each other.

Men, that woman isn't your private property: she [belongs to God]{.class_s35S}. You had better treat her right, or God will require it of [you]{.class_s35S}.

Ladies, you aren't just slaving around the house for some man who doesn't appreciate you. The Lord has made you a steward of one of His children. You aren't serving your husband; [you're serving God. ]{.class_s35S}You will give an account someday.

["That your prayers be not hindered."]{.class_s35R} That's a Christian not getting his prayers answered because of a bad relationship with his spouse---that's the man or the woman. So husbands, if you don't live with your wife knowledgeably and don't honor her and you don't treat her the way a sister in Christ should be treated, you place a block to God answering your prayers. If you are in the ministry, that's real bad because [that ministry is absolutely dependent on prayer.]{.class_s35S}

And ladies, if you don't submit yourself to your husbands, then don't count on getting answers to your prayers. If you have kids to raise and bills to pay, then that can be a desperate situation. You are going to need God [to pay attention to your prayers.]{.class_s35S}

8 Finally, be ye all of one mind, having compassion one of another, love as brethren, be pitiful, be courteous:

9 Not rendering evil for evil, or railing for railing: but contrariwise blessing; knowing that ye are thereunto called, that ye should inherit a blessing.

["Be ye all of one mind" ]{.class_s35R}(vs. 8). That would be a miracle of God if it happened: to have all the Christians think the same way about things. I don't know as it has ever happened in the history of the Church, and I am not sure that it will until the Rapture, but that's the way it should be.

The Christian is to have his mind renewed by the Holy Ghost (Rom. 12:2; Eph. 4:23). And the ["one mind"]{.class_s35R} the Christian is to have is ["the mind of Christ"]{.class_s35R} (1 Cor. 2:16; Phil. 2:5). We are to think about things the way that Jesus Christ thinks about them.

Now, the way the Lord thinks is not dependent on [WWJD]{.class_s35S} (see comments on 1 Pet. 2:21); it is revealed [by God in His Book]{.class_s35S} (1 Cor. 2:13--16). If that is the case (and there's no doubt in my mind about it), then there is no way that modern Christians can ["be\...of one mind."]{.class_s35R} With over 220 different versions of that Book, each one differing with all the others in anywhere from 500 to 64,000 places, there is no way you can get every Christian [thinking ]{.class_s35S}the same way. If you don't believe it, go to the average Southern Baptist Sunday School class (adults) and watch the teacher try to interpret a passage based upon what the eight to ten different versions that are in the class say. All he can say is "And what does [your ]{.class_s35S}version say?" and "What do [you ]{.class_s35S}think the passage means (or is saying to [you]{.class_s35S})?"

There is no way you can get one billion professing Christians to agree together when [225 final authorities ]{.class_s35S}are vying for their allegiance and, in the end, each person's own "noodle" chooses his "preference" as to exactly what God said. It's hard enough to get just a congregation of them to agree when they all follow one Book ([AV]{.class_s35S} 1611).

Now, when it comes to being ["of one mind"]{.class_s35R} with other Christians, here is how it is supposed to work:

1\) ["]{.class_s35R}[Be of the same mind ]{.class_s35W-0}[one toward another. Mind not high things, but condescend to men of low estate. Be not wise in your own conceits"]{.class_s35R} (Rom. 12:16). There should be no "class" distinctions in the church. We should treat the big shots the same way we treat the little shots.

2\) ["]{.class_s35R}[That ye may with one mind]{.class_s35W-0}[ and one mouth glorify God, even the Father of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class_s35R} (Rom. 15:6). We should all praise God together.

3\) ["Now I beseech you, brethren\...]{.class_s35R}[that ye all speak the same thing]{.class_s35W-0}[, and that there be]{.class_s35R}[ no divisions]{.class_s35W-0}[ among you; but that ye be perfectly ]{.class_s35R}[joined together in the same mind]{.class_s35W-0}[ and in the []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_325}same judgment"]{.class_s35R} (1 Cor. 1:10). In the context of the letter to the Corinthians, Paul is saying that the local church shouldn't be divided off according to everyone's favorite preacher and in little cliques and personality cults. He repeats the command again in 2 Corinthians 13:11.

4\) ["Only let your conversation be as it becometh the gospel of Christ\...that ye stand fast in one spirit, ]{.class_s35R}[with one mind]{.class_s35W-0}[ striving together for the faith of the gospel"]{.class_s35R} (Phil. 1:27). Every member of the church should ["contend for the faith which was once delivered unto the saints"]{.class_s35R} (Jude 3).

5\) ["Fulfill ye my joy, ]{.class_s35R}[that ye be like-minded]{.class_s35W-0}[, having the same love, being of one accord, of ]{.class_s35R}[one mind]{.class_s35W-0}["]{.class_s35R} (Phil. 2:2). Every Christian should try to live with his fellow believers in the love of Christ.

6\) ["I beseech Euodias, and beseech Syntyche, that they be of the same mind IN THE LORD"]{.class_s35R} (Phil. 4:2). Those last three words are the catch. Being ["of one mind"]{.class_s35R} and ["of the same mind"]{.class_s35R} does not mean that you fellowship with a believer who is living a life of open, unrepentant sin. Someone like that is to be "churched" (1 Cor. 5:2) until they repent and get right (2 Cor. 2:6--8).

["Love as brethren."]{.class_s35R} I have commented on this at length in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on General Epistles,]{.class_s35S} vol. 2 (specifically 1 John).

["Be pitiful."]{.class_s35R} When a Southerner says, "That's pitiful," he is saying that whatever he is talking about is the object of the pity. Peter isn't using the word that way. He is not telling you to live so that others pity you. He is telling you to be full of pity [for others.]{.class_s35S}

["Be courteous."]{.class_s35R} Now Peter has stopped preachin' and done gone to meddlin'. "That time he hit me."

["Be courteous."]{.class_s35R} Surely there is a modern version somewhere that gives the "true" meaning of the Greek. Doesn't ["courteous"]{.class_s35R} actually mean "to be frank."

["Be courteous."]{.class_s35R} That's one of those "Oh me" verses for me. I have a hard time with that one.

My wife is really good with that; I'm not. I have had people tell me that they liked my tie, and I don't know what to say back to them. I feel like saying, "Well, do you want to buy it?" But my wife says, "That's a compliment, honey. You're supposed to say, 'Thank you.'" Yeah? What for?

["Be courteous."]{.class_s35R} It means what it says and says what it means. You're supposed to shake hands with folks and open the door for them and smile and be nice.

[My problem]{.class_s35S} is that I grew up in a [military family. ]{.class_s35S}My grandfather and my father were artillerymen and infantrymen. When I went into the army I became a platoon leader in a rifle company. I don't see people as "people"; I see them as [targets]{.class_s35S}. That is not too conducive to [courtesy]{.class_s35S}.

The truth is, though, a little courtesy and manners are a good thing. Of course, you should never confuse courtesy and good manners with [spirituality]{.class_s35S}. The Pharisees would never eat unless they washed their hands (Mark 7:3--4), but they would kill Jesus Christ (John 18:28--32). But still, every Christian should learn and practise a little common courtesy and good manners.

The problem is when you go overboard. The Japanese are like that; they can be overly [courteous]{.class_s35S}.

Some Americans boarded a Japanese airliner to go to Tokyo. Before they took off, the captain got on the intercom and said, "So happy to have you flying Japan Airline to day. Hope you enjoy good trip."

Somewhere over the Pacific the captain announced, "So glad to have you aboard Japan Airline today. So sorry to tell you that we have motor trouble. Please do not worry. Have radioed []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_327}Tokyo. Help soon come. May not have to make crash landing. Stand by."

About thirty minutes later he came over the intercom again and said, "So glad to have you aboard Japan Airline. Motors all out. Going to make pancake landing. Please fasten seatbelt. Do not worry. Tokyo is sending out 200 sampans to pick us up."

The plane crashed in the water, and the captain said, "So glad that you fly Japan Airlines. Please listen carefully. All those who can swim stand on right wing. All those who cannot swim, stand on left wing." All the passengers got out of the plane and stood on the wings. The captain comes out of the plane and announces over a bull horn, "Bad news. So sorry. Sampans in hurricane, turn back, and go back to Japan. No worry. Come again soon."

After a while the plane begins to sink beneath the waves, and the captain gets on the bull horn, "Attention please. Plane is sinking. Those of you on right wing who can swim, now is time to swim. Those of you on left wing who cannot swim, thank you for flying Japan Airline."

That's taking "courtesy" too far, brother.

The key, brethren, is balance. In the military it is called being "an officer [and]{.class_s35S} a gentleman." Generals like George Washington, Stonewall Jackson, and Robert E. Lee were good at that sort of thing.

The idea is that there is a time to be rough, crude, and plain-talking; and there is a time to be courteous, polite, kind, and genteel. When you get in the pulpit, that is the time to say what you [mean]{.class_s35S}, to say it with [authority]{.class_s35S}, and to say it in no [uncertain terms]{.class_s35S}. It should be "over the plate, waist high." You should make [direct ]{.class_s35S}application to your congregation and make it personal when necessary. It is not the time to "tone down the message with words polite and snugly keep damnation out of sight."

But in your [personal ]{.class_s35S}contacts and relationships, everyone needs to exercise courtesy and manners. We have students come down to PBI all the time who have no manners whatsoever. I have to teach them to say "Yes, Ma'am," "No, Ma'am, "Yes, Sir," "No, sir," "Please," and "Thank you." Brother, you're in pretty rough shape when [Ruckman ]{.class_s35S}has to teach you [manners]{.class_s35S}!

Verse 9: ["Not rendering evil for evil, or railing for railing: but contrariwise blessing."]{.class_s35R} This hearkens back to the example of Christ in 1 Peter 2:23. If someone does you wrong or ridicules you, you don't do the same thing back at him. Instead of doing or saying something bad to that person, you do something good for them, or you say something good to them.

Christ said, ["Love your enemies, bless them that curse you, do good to them that hate you, and pray for them which despitefully use you, and persecute you"]{.class_s35R} (Matt. 5:44).

Paul said, ["Recompense to no man evil for evil...avenge not yourselves\...if thine enemy hunger, feed him; if he thirst, give him drink\...Be not overcome of evil, but overcome evil with good"]{.class_s35R} (Rom. 12:17--21).

Now, let's take a break for a second. Have you noticed how many times in the last nine verses that we have had direct cross references to [the Pauline epistles]{.class_s35S}? The Hyperdispensationalists will try to tell you that you can't get Christian doctrine from the General Epistles or Simon Peter. They have forgotten that there is more in that Book than [doctrine]{.class_s35S}. There is also ["reproof\...correction\...instruction in righteousness"]{.class_s35R} (2 Tim. 3:16). That's what we have been covering in 1 Peter 3.

Bob Jones Sr. used to say, "The [ethics ]{.class_s35S}of the Bible are just as inspired as its doctrines."

["Knowing that ye are thereunto called, that ye should inherit a blessing."]{.class_s35R} The calling of the Christian is to end up in a perfect body like that of Jesus Christ, in eternity, []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_329}in the New Jerusalem, with God. You talk about a blessing! If you are going to get all of that someday, you can afford to be liberal with your blessings down here on earth, especially with the unsaved.

D. L. Moody said that this earth is all the Hell that a Christian will ever see and it is all the Heaven that a lost person will ever see. There is a lot of truth in that.

A lost man is going to end up with a body just like that of his ["father"]{.class_s35R} (John 8:44). It will be able to feel, in excruciating detail, every agony of the damned in the Lake of Fire forever without being [annihilated]{.class_s35S}. Once there, that lost man will never again know joy, laughter, satisfaction, friendship, ease, comfort, or any pleasure of any kind; just eternal pain and suffering. Given that, don't you think that he deserves some sort of break from you right now?

The most tragic thing that can ever happen to a man is to live a life of poverty, pain, and sorrow down here on earth and then die lost and go to Hell. No comfort from start to finish.

When Sam Jones held his meetings in Atlanta, there was a young fellow who got up and gave this testimony. Before he was saved, he was a gambler and a very wicked young man. He married a Christian woman who witnessed to him and tried to win him to the Lord, but he wouldn't listen. She finally gave up and began praying for him.

One night, he and an old gambler were headed home from a card game that had lasted until about 11 o'clock at night (which was [late ]{.class_s35S}in those days). The guy's buddy said, "Boy, I could sure use a cup of coffee right now, but at this time of night I don't know where I could get one."

The young fellow said, "Well, you come home with me. My wife will get up and fix a cup of coffee for us."

"You must be crazy," the older man replied, "No woman is going to get up at 12 o'clock or 1 o'clock in the morning just to fix us a cup of coffee."

"My wife would," the young guy insisted.

"What kind of wife have you got, anyway"? asked the older fellow.

"Oh, she's a Christian."

The older fellow said, "Well, I've never met one of those before, but it would be worth seeing."

So they went to this younger fellow's apartment. He banged on the bedroom door and shouted, "Wife, get up and make us some hot coffee! [Hurry up and don't take all night about it]{.class_s35S}!"

The two sat down in the living room, and the old man asked, "Is your wife really gonna [do ]{.class_s35S}that?"

"Yeah, she'll do it."

"That's a strange kind of woman you've got there."

"Well," said the younger fellow, "she's a Christian, and that's the kind of stuff she believes, and that's the kind of stuff she does. She's been praying for me and trying to get me to accept her religion for years, but I don't think I could make it."

After a short while, the wife came out and set a couple of cups down and poured them some coffee. But as she went out, her husband winked at his companion and whispered, "[Watch this]{.class_s35S}." With that, he knocked his cup off the table and yelled, "This coffee is cold! [Get some more!"]{.class_s35S}

Calmly, she came back and collected the cups and went back into the kitchen and started to fix another pot.

The old man turned to her husband and said, "I don't see how you live with a woman like that."

"I don't understand how I do either. Sometimes I wonder why I do," replied her husband.

"How can a good woman like [that ]{.class_s35S}live with a devil like [you]{.class_s35S}?"

The young fellow said, "I don't know, but she does. She's always driving me crazy with talk about God and the Bible and prayer and Hell."

"Well, you're going to Hell, all right," his buddy observed, "but I don't understand how a fella like you could wind up with a good Christian woman like that."

When the wife returned with the coffee, that older fellow's curiosity got the better of him. He asked her, "Young woman, can I ask you a question? Why would a good Christian woman, like you, act like you do around this good-for-nothing that you have for a husband?"

"Well," she replied, "[I love him]{.class_s35S}. I have tried to win him to Christ, and [I can't do it]{.class_s35S}. Someday he is going to die and go to Hell, and he is going to burn forever. [He will never be happy again]{.class_s35S}. So I am trying to make him as happy as I can while he's here."

And when her husband heard that, he ended up receiving Christ on the spot. He dropped to his knees and said, "Honey, I want to be saved!"

10 For he that will love life, and see good days, let him refrain his tongue from evil, and his lips that they speak no guile:

11 Let him eschew evil, and do good; let him seek peace, and ensue it.

12 For the eyes of the Lord are over the righteous, and his ears are open unto their prayers: but the face of the Lord is against them that do evil.

This passage is a quote from Psalm 34:12--16. Verses 10 and 11 give two of the rules, laid down in the Scriptures, for living a long life. And when God promises a long life, it is not merely living a long time; it is a good life as well. So if you want a long physical life down here on earth, here are the rules to follow:

1\) ["Let him refrain his tongue from evil, and his lips that they speak no guile"]{.class_s35R} (vs. 10). Proverbs 21:23 says, ["Whoso keepeth his mouth and his tongue keepeth his soul from troubles."]{.class_s35R} Proverbs 18:21 says, ["Death and life are in the power of the tongue: and they that love it shall eat the fruit thereof."]{.class_s35R}

The potential of the tongue toward [life ]{.class_s35S}or toward [death ]{.class_s35S}is so great that God judges the [length of your life]{.class_s35S} by [how you use it]{.class_s35S}. You have to watch your tongue.

Preachers have to be especially careful about speaking ["no guile."]{.class_s35R} They preach their hearts out and don't see the results that they think they should see, so they resort to little [tricks ]{.class_s35S}to get people down the aisle.

I have sat through many an invitation where the pastor said, "If you would like to receive Christ as your Saviour, just lift your hand, and I will pray for you. [Yes]{.class_s35S}, I see that hand and that hand. There are hands going up all over the auditorium," and [not one hand was being raised]{.class_s35S}. That's not the Holy Spirit moving anyone to repent and be saved; it's guile: it's trickery.

When Paul said, ["Nevertheless, being crafty, I caught you with guile"]{.class_s35R} (2 Cor. 12:16), he was being [sarcastic]{.class_s35S}; he wasn't commending guile as an evangelistic tool of the trade.

For further discussion on the tongue, see comments on James 3.

2\) ["Let him eschew evil, and do good; let him seek peace, and ensue it"]{.class_s35R} (vs. 11). The word ["eschew"]{.class_s35R} means to stay away from and avoid. The word is ["depart"]{.class_s35R} in Psalm 34:14. Job ["eschewed evil"]{.class_s35R} (Job 1:1).

The word ["ensue"]{.class_s35R} means to ["pursue"]{.class_s35R} (Psa. 34:14) or to follow after. So to obtain long life, a Christian is to shun evil, ["do good,"]{.class_s35R} and seek and pursue after peace.

Now, [that peace]{.class_s35S} has nothing to do with [world]{.class_s35S} peace. The verse is not talking about some Pope getting up and []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_333}praying, "Lord, make me an instrument of Thy peace," and then preaching the redistribution of wealth by revolution ([liberation theology]{.class_s35S}; i.e., religious Communism), the [unilateral disarmament ]{.class_s35S}of the United States, and Israel giving up its God-given land in Palestine to appease a bunch of murdering, fornicating ragheads who have no more business there (Gal. 4:30) than Hitler had in Poland.

The United Nations has "sought" and "pursued" peace for the world since 1945. Do you know what the results have been? Korea, Vietnam, Kuwait, Afghanistan (twice!), Iraq (twice!), and over eighty-five other wars across the globe. Pretty bum job for a "peacekeeping" organization, don't you think?

World peace might be ["the desire of all nations"]{.class_s35R} (Hag. 2:7), but it is an opium "pipe dream" until the Prince of Peace returns to the City of Peace (Psa. 76:1--3) and sits down on the throne of peace (Isa. 9:7; Zech. 6:12--13).

The ["peace"]{.class_s35R} sought in 1 Peter 3:11 is a [personal peace]{.class_s35S}. It is peace with God that comes to every Christian at salvation (Rom. 5:1). It is the peace of God that the Holy Spirit gives to believers who live in fellowship with God. It is living in peace with other Christians and not fussing and fighting with them (2 Cor. 13:11). And it is our attempt to ["live peaceably with all men"]{.class_s35R} (Rom. 12:18).

3\) Another rule for living a long life is found in Ephesians 6:1--3. ["Children, obey your parents in the Lord: for this is right. Honour thy father and mother; which is the first commandment with promise; That it may be well with thee, and thou mayest live long on the earth."]{.class_s35R}

When God spoke the Ten Commandments in Exodus 20, the first commandment that came with a promise for keeping it was the fifth commandment: ["Honour thy father and thy mother: that thy days may be long upon the land which the ]{.class_s35R}[Lord ]{.class_s35X-0}[thy God giveth thee"]{.class_s35R} (Exod. 20:12).

4\) Proverbs 10:27, ["The fear of the ]{.class_s35R}[Lord ]{.class_s35X-0}[prolongeth days: but the years of the wicked shall be shortened."]{.class_s35R} Of course, there are exceptions to the rule. Stephen and John the Baptist were killed at a young age. A lot of missionaries who went to West Africa (the White Man's Graveyard) in the nineteenth century died at a young age. But these are all exceptions to the rule. Exceptions prove the rule.

The rule is if a man fears God, generally speaking, he will live longer than someone who[ doesn't.]{.class_s35S}

Whenever I preach to young people, I tell them this: If the Lord tarries for ten to twenty years, the young man or the young woman who will come out "on top" will be the one who fears the Lord. The kid who has a guilt complex about sinning against God (i.e., [exactly the opposite of what he is taught in the federal public schools]{.class_s35S}) and fears God's judgment will be ahead of the "pack." The Lord will take care of a young person like that.

5\) Proverbs 3:13, 15--16, ["Happy is the man that findeth wisdom, and the man that getteth understanding\...She is more precious than rubies: and all the things thou canst desire are not to be compared unto her. Length of days is in her right hand; and in her left hand riches and honour."]{.class_s35R} Wisdom and understanding will lengthen a man's life. Amount of knowledge is irrelevant. The Lord [doesn't care]{.class_s35S} how much you know. What the Lord is concerned with is [what you do]{.class_s35S} with what you know and [how you use]{.class_s35S} what you know [for God. ]{.class_s35S}Wisdom is knowing the right way to [apply ]{.class_s35S}your knowledge, and [understanding ]{.class_s35S}is knowing how that knowledge relates to God. If you get wisdom and understanding, [and live by them,]{.class_s35S} you will live longer than a [fool.]{.class_s35S}

6\) Proverbs 28:16, ["He that hateth covetousness shall prolong his days."]{.class_s35R} Any man or woman who avoids those who are greedy or is content with what he has and is not covetous []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_335}himself, that person will have a longer life than someone who "gets all he can and cans all he gets."

Now, [those ]{.class_s35S}are ways God says you can live a long life. Those might seem old fashioned and mid-Victorian, but that is what is [right. ]{.class_s35S}Given those standards, a lot of Americans won't live past their sixties; some won't reach forty or fifty.

Verse 12:[ "For the eyes of the Lord are over the righteous."]{.class_s35R} Well, ["the eyes of the Lord"]{.class_s35R} are everywhere; they see everything. Proverbs 15:3, ["The eyes of the ]{.class_s35R}[Lord ]{.class_s35X-0}[are in very place, beholding the evil and the good."]{.class_s35R} But the Book says, ["the eyes of the Lord are over the righteous"]{.class_s35R} means that the Lord is watching over them with a special care.

The word ["righteous,"]{.class_s35R} here, is used in the same way it is used in the Old Testament. In the New Testament sense, it is not just a saved person with imputed righteousness, but a saved person who is [living right]{.class_s35S}. Peter is speaking [practically]{.class_s35S}, not doctrinally.

["And his ears are open unto their prayers."]{.class_s35R} Notice how the Bible writers ascribe human attributes to God: ["eyes\...ears."]{.class_s35R} Of course, that is true of the Lord Jesus Christ in His human body, but that is not true of God the Father. ["God is a Spirit"]{.class_s35R} (John 4:24). A spirit doesn't have bodily parts. So when the Bible says, ["The eyes of the Lord"]{.class_s35R} and ["his ears,"]{.class_s35R} those are figurative expressions. The idea is that God sees you and takes care of you and hears your prayers.

If you want to see how [figurative ]{.class_s35S}a man can get when describing God, look at Ruth 2:12 and Psalm 17:8, where the Lord is said to have ["wings."]{.class_s35R} Well, the Lord isn't like that [mother ]{.class_s35S}hen which He likened Himself to in Matthew 23:37 and Luke 13:34 in the sense that He has [literal wings]{.class_s35S}. He's not one of the "hawk men" from Flash Gordon. He is like that hen in the sense that He draws you close to Himself and takes care of you. It's another of those figurative expressions.

Now, if you want the Lord to hear your prayers, then live right. The verse says, ["But the face of the Lord is against them that do evil."]{.class_s35R} That goes for a saved person or a lost person. From a practical standpoint, a Christian can be an ["enemy of God"]{.class_s35R} (James 4:4). So don't think that just because you are saved that the Lord [has]{.class_s35S} to listen to your prayers.

Isaiah 59:2, ["But your iniquities have separated between you and your God, and your sins have hid his face from you, that he will not hear."]{.class_s35R}

Psalm 66:18, ["If I regard iniquity in my heart, the Lord will not hear me."]{.class_s35R}

Those verses are as applicable to the personal prayer life of a Christian in A.D. 2005 as they were to Jews in 1000 and 750 B.C.

If you tie verse 12 back in with verse 7, you will see that for a Christian husband not to treat his Christian wife right is counted by God as ["evil,"]{.class_s35R} for it can hinder that man's prayer life. The Lord's ears aren't open to a man who doesn't dwell knowledgeably with his wife and does not honor her as a weaker vessel and does not treat her as his sister in Christ.

13 And who is he that will harm you, if ye be followers of that which is good?

14 But and if ye suffer for righteousness\' sake, happy are ye: and be not afraid of their terror, neither be troubled;

15 But sanctify the Lord God in your hearts: and be ready always to give an answer to every man that asketh you a reason of the hope that is in you with meekness and fear:

16 Having a good conscience; that, whereas they speak evil of you, as of evildoers, they may be ashamed that falsely accuse your good conversation in Christ.

17 For it is better, if the will of God be so, that ye suffer for well doing, than for evil doing.

["And who is he that will harm you, if ye be followers of that which is good?"]{.class_s35R} Well, the [world will ]{.class_s35S}(1 John 3:13). The [Devil ]{.class_s35S}will (1 Pet. 5:8). ["Unreasonable and wicked men"]{.class_s35R} will (2 Thess. 3:2). And Peter makes allowance for those in the next verse.

["But and if ye suffer for righteousness' sake"]{.class_s35R} (vs. 14). The [general rule ]{.class_s35S}is if you do right, people aren't going to hurt you, but the [exceptions to the rule ]{.class_s35S}are many: John the Baptist suffered for righteousness' sake. So did Stephen. So did Paul. The Pope had John Huss burned for proclaiming the truth and being a trusting soul. Nate Saint and Jim Elliott were killed by the Auca Indians after giving gifts to them. They didn't do those Indians any harm.

["But and if ye suffer for righteousness' sake." ]{.class_s35R}The reality is that if you live a good life and treat your wife and kids right and pay your bills on time and are a good neighbor, folks will take a "live and let live" approach to you. But speak up for Jesus Christ, pass out tracts, street preach, tell people that their own righteousness will send them to Hell, and the likelihood of suffering ["for righteousness' sake"]{.class_s35R} jumps up considerably.

Now, if you do ["suffer for righteousness' sake,"]{.class_s35R} then there are three things in verse 14 that you ought to do:

1\) Be happy (["happy are ye"]{.class_s35R}). What could you possibly be happy about in suffering? Well, you can be happy about [why]{.class_s35S} you are suffering: you are suffering for doing [right]{.class_s35S}, not [wrong]{.class_s35S}. That means God isn't against you. That's something to be happy about.

You can be happy about [for whom]{.class_s35S} you are suffering. ["If ye be reproached for the name of Christ, happy are ye"]{.class_s35R} (1 Pet. 4:14). It's not like the old days when you suffered for the Devil or your unsaved friends or your own stupidity.

You can be happy about [what awaits you]{.class_s35S} at the [end ]{.class_s35S}of the suffering. We read back in James 5:11, ["we count them []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_338}happy which endure. Ye have heard of the patience of Job, and have seen the end of the Lord; the Lord is very pitiful, and of tender mercy."]{.class_s35R} You might have sorrow as you go through the suffering but [in the end,]{.class_s35S} just like He did to Job, the Lord will do something to bring you happiness.

2\) ["Be not afraid."]{.class_s35R} That has nothing to do with fearing God. It r[efers to fearing men]{.class_s35S}. If you fear man, you will be likely to "buckle" under persecution, so don't be afraid of men. Memorize Hebrews 13:6. ["So that we may boldly say, The Lord is my helper, and I will not fear what man shall do unto me."]{.class_s35R} Memorize Psalm 56:3, ["What time I am afraid, I will trust in thee."]{.class_s35R}

3\) ["Neither be troubled."]{.class_s35R} There are two types of trouble that you will experience when suffering: trouble on the [outside ]{.class_s35S}and trouble on the [inside]{.class_s35S}. You can't do much about the trouble on the outside. That's up to your persecutors. But you can control how troubled you are on the inside.

Paul said, in 2 Corinthians 4:8, ["We are troubled on every side,"]{.class_s35R} (that's trouble on the outside) ["yet not distressed"]{.class_s35R} (there is the trouble on the inside). Why wasn't Paul troubled on the [inside]{.class_s35S}? Because the ["God, that comforteth those that are cast down, comforted us"]{.class_s35R} (2 Cor. 7:6). In Paul's case it was through a brother in Christ. But you can take comfort also just by resting in the promises of God.

Second Corinthians 1:3--5, ["Blessed be God, even the Father of our Lord Jesus Christ, the Father of mercies, and the God of all comfort; Who comforteth us in all our tribulation, that we may be able to comfort them which are in any trouble, by the comfort wherewith we ourselves are comforted of God. For as the sufferings of Christ abound in us, so our consolation also aboundeth by Christ."]{.class_s35R}

Verse 15:[ "But sanctify the Lord God in your hearts."]{.class_s35R} [Sanctification ]{.class_s35S}is not always a reference to salvation in the New Testament. The verb [sanctify]{.class_s35S} means to set apart for God's use. There is a sense in which you are sanctified at salvation (1 Cor. 1:2, 6:11); i.e., you are set aside by God to be a saint. But sanctification is also a [daily process]{.class_s35S} in which you participate (1 Thess. 4:1--4; 2 Tim. 2:20--22).

Verse 15 has nothing to do with salvation. It is you giving Jesus Christ the proper place in your heart as Lord. The old illustration is that in your heart there is a cross and a throne. When you are on the throne, Christ is on [the cross. ]{.class_s35S}When [you ]{.class_s35S}are on the cross, Christ is on the throne. The trick to the Christian life is to keep Christ on the throne of your heart.

Then you have a great admonition to every Christian in verse 15: ["and be ready always to give an answer to every man that asketh you a reason of the hope that is in you."]{.class_s35R} This verse should be read in conjunction with 1 Peter 4:11. ["If any man speak, let him speak as the oracles of God."]{.class_s35R}

Any Christian, at any time, should be ready to give a Scriptural answer to anybody who asks any question.

That's not "Ruckman" laying some kind of legalistic burden on you; that's a New Testament commandment. It is just as much of a [New Testament commandment ]{.class_s35S}as the previous phrase in verse 15: ["sanctify the Lord God in your hearts."]{.class_s35R}

Now, I know that some of you aren't great intellectuals. You aren't real "bookish" like me. That doesn't matter. That Bible is God Almighty speaking to you, brother, sister. Whether or not you know any other book, you [need]{.class_s35S} to know that Bible. You won't learn it by reading the [newspaper]{.class_s35S}. You won't learn it by watching [television]{.class_s35S}. And these days, you won't learn it by listening to the [radio]{.class_s35S}, even some "Christian" radio.

The only way you will know that Book the way you should is to spend time in it. [Read it, study it, memorize it]{.class_s35S}; then get out in the streets and in neighborhoods and put it to use.

All across this nation, I hold "Open Bible Forums." These are sessions in which any member of the audience can get up and ask me a question, [any question at all]{.class_s35S}, and I will try to give him a Bible answer in five seconds or less. I am not always able to do it. Occasionally I will get a question that stumps me or one that takes me more than five seconds to find the first Scripture. The answer itself may take five to twenty minutes to run all the references, but I can usually hit the first verse in[ five seconds.]{.class_s35S}

[Now, I did not get that way by attending Bob Jones University and getting my doctorate]{.class_s35S}. I will "let the cat out of the bag," so to speak, and tell you how I came to be able to do that.

When I was at Bob Jones University, I met a fellow named Glen Schunk. [He got me out on the streets, witnessing and preaching]{.class_s35S}. Well, I was "hooked." I started witnessing every weekend somewhere on my breaks from school.

At the time I was reading my Bible completely through at least [twice a month]{.class_s35S}. I was familiar with its contents, but I was learning how to use it in dealing with sinners. When someone would ask me a question that I couldn't answer, I would go back to my hotel room or to my trailer or to the farm at which I was staying, and I would look up the answer in my Bible so that I would be able to give it the next time the question came up.

I noticed some questions came up on a fairly consistent basis, so I wrote them down in the front of my Bible along with the [first Scripture reference to answer that question. ]{.class_s35S}From there I made my own system of [chain references ]{.class_s35S}through the Bible on those questions so I could turn from one Scripture to the other without having to recall everything by memory.

Pretty soon I had so many chain references that I had chains crossing chains. But by that time I had gone through some of []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_341}them so often that I could take you through the entire chain of a question by memory. For the lesser asked questions I could usually take you to the first verse by [memory]{.class_s35S}.

Now that is Ruckman's "secret" to those Open Bible Forums. It has nothing to do with my "brilliant intellect" or my "photographic memory" (which I don't have). It is the result of [long hours]{.class_s35S} of reading and [studying on my own ]{.class_s35S}and constant [use ]{.class_s35S}of the Scriptures in one-on-one contacts.

Hebrews 5:12--14 says, ["For when for the time ye ought to be teachers, ye have need that one teach you again which be the first principles of the oracles of God; and are become such as have need of milk, and not of strong meat. For everyone that useth milk is unskilful in the word of righteousness: for he is a babe. But strong meat belongeth to them that are of full age, even those who by reason of use have their senses exercised to discern both good and evil."]{.class_s35R}

No Christian should be saved for ten, fifteen, or twenty years and still be sucking a bottle [spiritually]{.class_s35S}; at least not in America. But the vast majority of churches are filled with baby Christians who have never grown beyond John 3:16 and the Roman's Road. And unfortunately, that number includes many [pastors ]{.class_s35S}who can give their congregations nothing beyond the "fundamentals," church attendance, and giving.

["With meekness and fear."]{.class_s35R} This deals with your [attitude ]{.class_s35S}when giving a Scriptural answer to those who question you. My purpose in Open Bible Forums is [not]{.class_s35S} to show off my Bible knowledge. [I am a Bible teacher;]{.class_s35S} my motive is to tell those people what the Bible [says ]{.class_s35S}about a matter so that they can adjust their thoughts and actions to the [Final Authority.]{.class_s35S}

["Knowledge puffeth up"]{.class_s35R} (1 Cor. 8:1). That is why you have to temper your knowledge of the Scriptures with charity (1 []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_342}Cor. 8:1), humility (["meekness"]{.class_s35R}), and a healthy fear of God (vs. 15).

Now, I have applied verse 14 to any situation that a Christian is in. But the actual [context ]{.class_s35S}of the verse is a Christian[ being put on trial by his persecutors. ]{.class_s35S}The scene is familiar to anyone who has read such works as [Foxe's Book of Martyrs]{.class_s35S} and [Martyr's Mirror. ]{.class_s35S}More modern accounts can be found in the biographies of Watchman Nee, Harlan Popov, and Richard Wurmbrand. When the apostles were hauled before the council and beaten in Acts 5, the Bible says, ["they departed\...rejoicing that they were counted worthy to suffer shame for his name"]{.class_s35R} (Acts 5:41).

The point is when you are arrested and hauled into court and jailed, [make sure it is for the right reason. ]{.class_s35S}You are to have ["a good conscience"]{.class_s35R} in the matter (vs. 16). You are to suffer ["for well doing,"]{.class_s35R} not ["evil doing"]{.class_s35R} (vs. 17). Nobody should be able to legitimately accuse you of breaking the law, unless that law directly contradicts something God told you to do in the Bible.

Brethren, life is filled with enough heartaches, tears, and disappointments without you heaping more on yourself needlessly. If you are going to have to suffer, suffer for the right [Person]{.class_s35S}, suffer for the right [cause]{.class_s35S}, suffer for an [eternal payback]{.class_s35S}.

That's right! If you are going to have to suffer anyway, make sure that you get something [worthwhile ]{.class_s35S}out of it; something more important than money, gold, fame, popularity, cars, or women. Get something that is going to still be around and well in a billion years.

You take someone like JFK, who took a bullet in the head for shacking up with some Mafia boss' girlfriend (or the fiasco at the Bay of Pigs, take your pick. One explanation is just as good as the other). How can that possibly compare to William Tyndale being strangled to death and burnt at the stake for [translating ]{.class_s35S}the [New Testament into English]{.class_s35S}? What Tyndale started has gone []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_343}around the world for 469 years to the tune of over one billion copies ([KJV]{.class_s35S}). That bird is [still]{.class_s35S} reaping dividends for what he did.

Brethren, ["if the will of God be so"]{.class_s35R} (vs. 17) and you have to "get it in the neck," then "get it in the neck" for Jesus Christ.

Some of you military fellows, in the army, navy, air force, and marines: haven't you suffered some to serve Uncle Sam? I personally knew a man who was shipped overseas for [forty-six months]{.class_s35S}. He went for four years without seeing his family. I am sure that family suffered from low pay and not having a husband and daddy around. The fellow not only suffered the normal things one suffers in the military, but I'm sure he missed his family terribly.

Now, if you can suffer like [that ]{.class_s35S}for people like FDR, JFK, Lyndon Baines Johnson, "Tricky Dick" Nixon, Jimmy Carter, and Slick Willie Clinton, can't you volunteer to be a missionary and suffer a little privation for [Jesus Christ]{.class_s35S}?

18 For Christ also hath once suffered for sins, the just for the unjust, that he might bring us to God, being put to death in the flesh, but quickened by the Spirit:

19 By which also he went and preached unto the spirits in prison;

20 Which sometime were disobedient, when once the longsuffering of God waited in the days of Noah, while the ark was a preparing, wherein few, that is, eight souls were saved by water.

21 The like figure whereunto even baptism doth also now save us (not the putting away of the filth of the flesh, but the answer of a good conscience toward God,) by the resurrection of Jesus Christ:

22 Who is gone into heaven, and is on the right hand of God; angels and authorities and powers being made subject unto him.

Now we've reached a passage in chapter 3 that has a lot of [doctrinal content ]{.class_s35S}for the believer. From verses 1--17, Peter has been giving you practical rules for living together as husband and wife, for getting along with other Christians, and for suffering for Christ in this world. But verses 18--22 are purely doctrinal.

The first thing Peter discusses is the blood atonement. If there was any such thing in the New Testament as "the Gospel in a nutshell," verse 18 is it. Of course, I know that is what most people call John 3:16. There is just one problem with that: THERE IS NO [GOSPEL ]{.class_s35S}MENTIONED IN JOHN 3:16.

The Gospel, brethren, is defined in 1 Corinthians 15:3--4. It is ["how that Christ died for our sins according to the scriptures; And that he was buried, and that he rose again the third day according to the scriptures."]{.class_s35R} That's the Gospel.

You don't find any of those things in John 3:16. Christ doesn't [die ]{.class_s35S}in John 3:16, He isn't [buried ]{.class_s35S}in John 3:16, and He doesn't rise from the dead in John 3:16. [There is no mention of sin in John 3:16]{.class_s35S}, and the word [Scriptures]{.class_s35S} isn't in John 3:16 either. The nutshell isn't empty; it just doesn't contain the "nut" most people believe is there.

John 3:16 is a synopsis of the [purpose ]{.class_s35S}and [plan ]{.class_s35S}of the Gospel. Because you are saved, [you read the "Gospel" back into the verse]{.class_s35S}; you know about what it is talking. [But the "Gospel" itself is not there]{.class_s35S}.

Romans 10:9--10 is much better, but still fails to mention the fact that YOU ARE A SINNER. You have to use those verses in conjunction with Romans 3:10, 23 and Romans 5:8.

First Peter 3:18 has all the essential elements in one verse and makes application.

["For Christ also hath once suffered for sins."]{.class_s35R} [There's the atonement for sin]{.class_s35S}.

["Being put to death in the flesh, but quickened by the Spirit."]{.class_s35R} [There's the death and resurrection]{.class_s35S}. (The burial of Christ is expounded upon in vs. 19.)

Then the application:[ "the just for the unjust, that he might bring us to God."]{.class_s35R}

I used to hold meetings for a pastor over in Ft. Walton Beach. His name was Jim Quigley. Jim was a great soulwinner. He would visit all those little trailer courts and housing projects where the military personnel and their families lived. He would make about twenty contacts a day, and I never went on visitation with him where he failed to lead someone to Christ. He won about [one a day]{.class_s35S} the whole time he was pastor of Ocean Springs Baptist Church.

I watched Jim's technique very carefully; he would only use two verses to deal with a person about his soul. He would use Hebrews 9:17 and 1 Peter 3:18. I never saw him turn to any other verse.

Jim would go up to a door, and after the introductions, he would ask, "Has anybody ever showed you out of the Bible what the Bible says about salvation?" If the person said "Yes," he would move on to the next house or trailer. If he said "No," Jim would continue.

"Then do you mind if I showed you a couple of verses?" And out would come his New Testament. Sometimes, he would be cut off right there. If [that ]{.class_s35S}happened, we would leave.

But many times we were invited in. Quigley would sit next to the person and point to Hebrews 9:27 and read it. ["It is appointed unto men once to die."]{.class_s35R} Then he would stop and ask, "You are going to die someday. You do believe that, don't you?" The person would say "Yes," and Quigley would go on.

["But after this the judgment."]{.class_s35R} Then Jim would ask them, "Do you believe that God is going to judge you someday []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_346}for your life?" If the person argued with Jim, he would pray with him and leave. If he said "Yes," Jim would go on.

"Salvation is how to get by that judgement [right now."]{.class_s35S} He would then turn to 1 Peter 3:18 and ask them to read it. ["For Christ also hath once suffered for sins."]{.class_s35R}

"Are you familiar with Christ dying on the cross for sins?" he asked. The person would say "Yes," and Jim would continue. "When Christ died on the cross, He died, the verse says, ['the just for the unjust.']{.class_s35R}"

Then he would turn to the person with whom he was dealing and ask, "Now, who is ['the just']{.class_s35R}?" If he did not give the right answer the first time, Quigley made him read the verse until he realized that ["the just,"]{.class_s35R} there, was [Jesus Christ.]{.class_s35S}

"And who is ['the unjust']{.class_s35R}?" asked Jim. If the person hesitated, he would read the verse again. If it still didn't hit the person, Quigley would say, kindly and politely, "Well, ['the unjust']{.class_s35R} [is us]{.class_s35S}, isn't it?" And when that person got the message, I have seen his eyes light up. Once Jim got people to [that ]{.class_s35S}point, they would nearly always get saved.

Then Quigley would apply the text and "draw the net." "So Christ,[ 'the just,']{.class_s35R} suffered for the sins of ['the unjust']{.class_s35R}; that's [you]{.class_s35S}. Now [why]{.class_s35S} did Christ suffer for us?" Then he would have the prospect read the next part of the verse:[ "that he might bring us to God."]{.class_s35R}

["Do you want to be brought back to God?"]{.class_s35S} Jim would ask. And if he could get a person that far, usually he would say "Yes". So he said, "All right. All you have to do is trust Jesus Christ as your Saviour because He died in your place to bring you back to God. Accept Him as your Saviour. If you will take my hand, I'll show you how to do it."

That was one of the most effective means I have ever seen for leading a soul to Christ. It deals with the atonement in []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_347}[five ]{.class_s35S}words: ["the just for the unjust."]{.class_s35R} That's the heart of the matter.

Before leaving verse 18, there are two more things we should note. First is that Simon Peter, the Roman Catholic's first "Pope," declared by an [actual]{.class_s35S} "excathedra" statement (i.e., an infallible statement made under the direct inspiration of the Holy Spirit) that ["Christ\...hath ONCE suffered for sins."]{.class_s35R} That's ONCE; as in [one time. He does not suffer every Sunday morning at 11 o'clock during the Mass.]{.class_s35S}

Second, is the [extent ]{.class_s35S}of the atonement. Verse 18 says that ["Christ\...suffered for SINS."]{.class_s35R} Those are the individual acts of transgression that we do. But He not only died for [sins,]{.class_s35S} He also died for [sin. ]{.class_s35S}That's the [sin nature. ]{.class_s35S}Isaiah 53:10 says, ["When thou shalt make his soul an offering for SIN, he shall see his seed."]{.class_s35R} That [sin]{.class_s35S} is connected with a man's [seed:]{.class_s35S} it's the Adamic nature.

Second Corinthians 5:21, ["For he hath made him to be SIN for us, who knew no SIN; that we might be made the righteousness of God in him."]{.class_s35R} Christ illustrates that verse Himself in John 3:14. ["And as Moses lifted up the serpent in the wilderness, even so must the Son of man be lifted up."]{.class_s35R} That sin nature is illustrated by that brazen serpent Moses put on the pole in Numbers 21:9. That's what Christ became on the cross.

So Christ died for [sins]{.class_s35S} (the specific acts), He died for [sin]{.class_s35S} (the Adamic nature), and He died for [sinners]{.class_s35S}---individual people. Paul said, ["This is a faithful saying, and worthy of all acceptation, that Christ Jesus came into the world to save sinners; of whom I am chief"]{.class_s35R} (1 Tim. 1:15).

That means when a sinner comes up before the White Throne Judgment, he will have no excuse. The death of Christ covered [everything. ]{.class_s35S}It took care of him as a [sinner]{.class_s35S}, it took care []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_348}of each [act ]{.class_s35S}of iniquity he committed, and it took care of his [Adamic nature]{.class_s35S}.

The [sin]{.class_s35S} question has been settled. It was settled at Calvary. The only question to be settled is the [Son]{.class_s35S} question. The question is "What will you do with Jesus?" I settled [that]{.class_s35S} question on March 14, 1949.

Now, in verses 19--20, we get into some pretty heavy doctrine, and it has to do with the time when Christ was buried. Of course, that is not what a lot of commentators say. The standard interpretation is this: the Spirit of Christ was in Noah while he was preaching to the disobedient of his day. So the ["spirit of Christ"]{.class_s35R} was preaching to them through Noah.

There are several problems with that,  but the two biggest ones are these:

1\) Noah didn't preach to [spirits]{.class_s35S}; he preached to [men]{.class_s35S}. Men aren't spirits; they are [souls]{.class_s35S}.

2\) Noah didn't preach to anyone in [prison]{.class_s35S}. He didn't preach to anyone "in the prison house of sin." That is someone trying to "wax eloquent" because he hasn't a clue as to what the text means. The ["prison"]{.class_s35R} is a literal prison which has bars and gates and chains, as we will see.

Let us go, then, through these verses carefully, paying attention to the wording. We are going to let the Scriptures interpret the Scriptures, instead of assigning some private interpretation of our own to the text.

Verse 19: ["By which."]{.class_s35R} The ["which"]{.class_s35R} refers back to the [Holy Spirit ]{.class_s35S}in verse 18, who raised Jesus Christ from the grave and drove Christ into the wilderness to be tempted in Mark 1:12. He took the Lord to the ["prison"]{.class_s35R} of verse 19 for the specific purpose of preaching to a bunch of spirits.

There is a similar verse in 1 Peter 4:6, but notice that in 1 Peter 4:6, Christ preached ["the gospel."]{.class_s35R} No gospel is preached in 1 Peter 3:19--20. Moreover, in 1 Peter 4:6, Christ []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_349}["preached\...to them that are dead."]{.class_s35R} The ["dead"]{.class_s35R} of 1 Peter 4:6 are going to be ["judged\...in the flesh, but live according to God in the spirit."]{.class_s35R} The ["dead"]{.class_s35R} of 1 Peter 4:6 are not ["spirits in prison; which some time were disobedient."]{.class_s35R} So although 1 Peter 4:6 is a further [explanation ]{.class_s35S}of what Christ accomplished during His burial, it is [not ]{.class_s35S}the interpretation of verses 19 and 20.

Now if these spirits aren't men, then who (or what) are they? Hebrews 1:7 says, ["And of the angels he saith, Who maketh his angels SPIRITS, and his ministers a flame of fire."]{.class_s35R} In Hebrews 1:14, referring back to ["the angels"]{.class_s35R} mentioned in Hebrews 1:13, ["Are they not all ministering SPIRITS, sent forth to minister for them who shall be heirs of salvation?"]{.class_s35R}

When Peter got out of prison in Acts 12, and Rhoda tried to convince those who were praying for him at the house of John Mark that Peter was at the door, they said, ["It is his angel"]{.class_s35R} (Acts 12:15). They were talking about his [spirit]{.class_s35S}, his ghost. They thought Peter was dead, and they called his spirit an ["angel."]{.class_s35R}

Although spirits do not have ["flesh and bones"]{.class_s35R} (Luke 24:39), they can take shape (Job 4:16). In the case of angels, the form is that[ "of a man" ]{.class_s35R}(Rev. 21:17; Gen. 32:24 cf. Hosea 12:4; Judg. 13:3, 6, 8--9).

The question is, then, where were there ever any angels that were put into prison? In 2 Peter 2:4 and Jude 6, there are some ["angels that sinned"]{.class_s35R} and ["kept not their first estate."]{.class_s35R} Those angels were ["cast\...down to hell"]{.class_s35R} and clapped in ["chains of darkness."]{.class_s35R}

First Peter 3:20 says that these angels were ["disobedient\...in the days of Noah."]{.class_s35R} So there is no doubt as to the identity of these ["spirits in prison."]{.class_s35R} They are ["the sons of God"]{.class_s35R} who married ["the daughters of men"]{.class_s35R} in []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_350}Genesis 6:2. In the Old Testament, especially in the book of Genesis, ["the sons of God"]{.class_s35R} refers to a [race ]{.class_s35S}of supernatural beings that were created before the earth (Job 38:4--7). A group of these angels fell with Satan in Isaiah 14:12--15 (cf. Matt. 25:41). They are not in Hell, now, as is evident by the fact that Satan and all kinds of "devils" are running around from Genesis to Revelation 20. Like the old colored woman said, "If de Devil done be chained now, he sho' do have a long chain."

But there is another group that fell in Genesis 6 (see comments in that Commentary). Though they were ["children of the most High,"]{.class_s35R} they died ["like men"]{.class_s35R} in the Flood (Psa. 82:6--7). That's why Job 4:18 says, ["Behold, he put no trust in his servants; and his angels he charged with folly."]{.class_s35R}

When they died in the Flood, [the spirits of these angels ]{.class_s35S}were sent to Hell where they were ["reserved in everlasting chains under darkness unto the judgment of the great day"]{.class_s35R} (Jude 6).

Hell is a prison and is called such in Revelation 20:7. It has [chains ]{.class_s35S}(Jude 6; Rev. 20:1). It has [bars ]{.class_s35S}(Jonah 2:2,6) and [gates ]{.class_s35S}(Matt. 16:18) that require [keys ]{.class_s35S}to open (Rev. 1:18, 20:1).

If you examine the charts in Clarence Larkin's [The Spirit World ]{.class_s35S}(available through the Bible Baptist Bookstore), you will see that Hell is divided into [three compartments ]{.class_s35S}in the Old Testament. In the Old Testament, the whole thing is called [Sheol]{.class_s35S} (Hebrew), the place of departed spirits. One side is called [Hades]{.class_s35S} (Greek) in the New Testament, and that is Hell, the abode of the damned described by Christ in Luke 16, which will someday be cast into the Lake of Fire (Rev. 20:14).

Across from Hell, separated by ["a great gulf"]{.class_s35R} (Luke 16:26), is what Christ called ["Abraham's bosom"]{.class_s35R} and ["paradise"]{.class_s35R} (Luke 23:43). This is where the Old Testament saints went when they died. Since nobody in the Old Testament was born again and nobody had their sins taken away (Heb. []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_351}10:4), the saints could not go to Heaven, so they went to a[ temporary place]{.class_s35S} until Christ died on the cross. After the Church is raptured and the Law is reinstated as a part of salvation (Rev. 12:17, 14:12), the Tribulation saints will once [again ]{.class_s35S}be sent to a temporary place until Christ takes them to Heaven in a post-Tribulation rapture (Rev. 6:9--11; Matt. 24:29--31).

Then below these two is a part of Hell called [Tartarus]{.class_s35S} in Greek (ταρταρωςας) (2 Pet. 2:4). It is equated with ["the bottomless pit"]{.class_s35R} of Revelation 20:1. It is where ["the angels which kept not their first estate"]{.class_s35R} (Jude 6) are chained.

Now, let's put all of this together. I will give you, first, that about which I am [fairly ]{.class_s35S}sure.

When Christ died, His body was put into the tomb of Joseph of Arimathea. His spirit (His human spirit, not the Holy Spirit) returned to God (Eccl. 12:7; Luke 23:46). But the Holy Spirit stayed with His soul and took Him down to Hell (Psa. 139:8; Acts 2:27, 31).

At this point, in my sermon on "[Where Do The Dead Go?]{.class_s35S}" I have Christ enter into Hell itself (what Larkin would call "Hades") and preach condemnation to the unsaved dead of the Old Testament. That is "good preaching," but that is [not]{.class_s35S} what the text says. Christ preached in "Hell" to the angels that sinned in Genesis 6, and from what the Scriptures say in 2 Peter 2:4 and Jude 6, I gather that He preached condemnation to them, probably reaffirming the message of Psalm 82. He may have proclaimed His position as their Lord and Judge that would be accomplished by the resurrection (vs. 22 cf. Phil. 2:10--11; Acts 17:31).

Then He left both Hell and Tartarus, taking the key to Hell with Him (Rev. 1:18) and went to Paradise. There Jesus preached ["the gospel"]{.class_s35R} to the Old Testament saints. The good news of 1 Peter 4:6 was that Jesus Christ's blood could do what []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_352}["the blood of bulls and of goats"]{.class_s35R} could not do: it could [take away sins]{.class_s35S} (Heb. 9:12--14), not merely [forgive ]{.class_s35S}them (Heb. 9:22).

When He arose, He conquered death (Acts 2:24; 2 Tim. 1:10) and took its [key ]{.class_s35S}as well (Rev. 1:18). He then emptied Paradise and took it to Heaven (2 Cor. 12:4) when ["he led captivity captive"]{.class_s35R} (Eph. 4:8).

I am pretty confident of what I have just told you; it is pretty firm ground. What I am about to tell you is not so sure. It is what some would call "speculative" theology, but it has some basis in the Scriptures, so we will examine it.

The giants and ["mighty men"]{.class_s35R} that were born as the result of fornication between ["the sons of God"]{.class_s35R} and ["the daughters of men"]{.class_s35R} were not like [normal men]{.class_s35S}. Their bodies of flesh would have come from their mothers. [But their fathers had no soul to pass on to their children. ]{.class_s35S}Their fathers were [spirits ]{.class_s35S}only, in human form. Their children would have been the same, but with [bodies of real human flesh]{.class_s35S}.

They would be like Hercules in Greek mythology: half human, half gods. Their supernatural nature would make them subject to the punishment of their fathers, but their human nature would be subject to blood redemption. Of course they would have had no say-so in the matter. The sin was the fathers', and the sons of God probably controlled the giants and ["mighty men."]{.class_s35R} So what you have here is a whole race of creatures that don't really "fit in" anywhere. [They aren't angels and they aren't human.]{.class_s35S}

Look at verse 20: ["which SOMETIME WERE disobedient."]{.class_s35R} The verse is worded in such a way that you [could]{.class_s35S} read it: "[At some point]{.class_s35S} in the past these spirits (vs. 19) were disobedient, but they aren't anymore."

[If]{.class_s35S} that's so, and [if]{.class_s35S} 1 Peter 3:19 and 1 Peter 4:6 are referring to the same event (and those are two awfully big IFs), then you are left with the possibility that Christ went down into "Tartarus" to []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_353}preach the gospel to the spirits of the giants and ["mighty men"]{.class_s35R} who died in the Flood. Since they were [born ]{.class_s35S}the way they were through no fault of their own, the Lord [may have given them a chance to be saved right then.]{.class_s35S}

Now, I don't teach that as a [sure]{.class_s35S} thing. People with no more sense than Stewart Custer (head of the Bible Department at BJU) would call that one of Ruckman's "peculiar doctrines." I never said it was a [doctrine]{.class_s35S}. I am just [guessing]{.class_s35S}, based on what the Scriptures say. I know that is a "long shot" and that is "way out in left field," but there are a lot of strange things in that Book.

If you want to find out whether it is so or not, stick around until your friendly neighborhood UFO occupants come down to help the Pope at Rome establish "peace on earth" through one [political system ]{.class_s35S}ruled over by [one dictator ]{.class_s35S}who enforces (by death) a one world economy and [one religion]{.class_s35S}. I won't be around; I'll be "outta here" (1 Thess. 4; 1 Cor. 15)!

Verse 20: ["When once the longsuffering of God waited in the days of Noah."]{.class_s35R} If you go back and study my comments under Genesis 5, you will see that God's "longsuffering" wasn't relegated merely to the 120 years that Noah spent building the ark or even the 600 years that Noah lived before the Flood. The longsuffering of God goes back to the preaching of Enoch [before ]{.class_s35S}his translation (Jude 14).

[God's longsuffering is measured by the life of the longest man that ever lived on this earth]{.class_s35S}, and that man was the son of Enoch. Enoch began to walk with God ["after he begat Methuselah"]{.class_s35R} (Gen. 5:22). He did that because God showed him of the coming judgment of the Flood. This is reflected in the fact that Enoch named his son [Methuselah,]{.class_s35S} which means "when he is dead it shall be sent."

Methuselah lived longer than any man recorded in the Bible: he [lived 969 years]{.class_s35S}. That's a long time for God to put up with folks' foolishness, but He did. That's how patient God is.

Most of the new "Bibles" change that term [longsuffering]{.class_s35S} to "patience". But patience isn't quite as descriptive a word as "longsuffering". As we can see in the example of Methuselah, longsuffering is God suffering (putting up with, allowing---see Mark 9:19, 10:14) something from someone for a LONG time.

[Longsuffering ]{.class_s35S}is one of the greatest attributes of God. It is what theologians call a "communicable" attribute; i.e., an attribute that God can pass on to His creatures. Exodus 34:6 says, ["The ]{.class_s35R}[Lord ]{.class_s35X-0}[God, merciful and gracious, LONGSUFFERING, and abundant in goodness and truth.]{.class_s35R}

It is part of the fruit of the Spirit in Galatians 5:22. It is a quality of the type of love God wants us as Christians to have (1 Cor. 13:4). The Apostle Paul [commands]{.class_s35S} us to be longsuffering (Eph. 4:2; Col. 3:12).

The thing to remember about God's longsuffering is this: it is [long,]{.class_s35S} but it is [not eternal. ]{.class_s35S}God put up with those Ante-diluvians for 969 years, then he made up His mind to judge the world. The day came when His longsuffering ran out, and He drowned everybody except the eight people who did what He told them to do to be saved.

For [2,000 years]{.class_s35S}, now, the Lord has put up with a bunch of Christ-rejecting Gentiles, trying to get to Heaven with their yoga, sacraments, baptisms, masses, prayers, rosaries, Shahadas, etc. The day will come when He won't put up with it any more, and He will call His children home. When that happens, it's ["woe, to the inhabiters of the earth"]{.class_s35R} (Rev. 8:13). The Lord takes ["vengeance on them that know not God, and that obey not the gospel of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class_s35R} (2 Thess. 1:8).

I often read eyewitness accounts of different things. I have read eyewitness accounts of the torture chambers in the death camps during the Holocaust. I read one account by a doctor who []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_355}was there, one by an intern, and another by a prisoner who had endured the whole terrible ordeal.

I don't read those things because I get some morbid fascination from somebody being tortured. I read those things because it helps me see things the way [the Lord ]{.class_s35S}sees them.

For [6,000 years]{.class_s35S} now, the Lord has looked down on mankind and has seen [exactly the kinds of things]{.class_s35S} [that were described in those books. ]{.class_s35S}He has seen that and more, and yet, He has "held back." Oh, He will send individual and even institutional and regional judgment, but He never has let everyone "have it" like He did in the Flood.

The more that you see and know of what God sees and knows about men, the more you will appreciate the [longsuffering ]{.class_s35S}of God. Until you read some of that stuff, your little world is fixated on [you,]{.class_s35S} but the world is about more than [you]{.class_s35S}. What God puts up with from [you ]{.class_s35S}"AIN'T THE HALF OF IT!"

When you learn all of the rest of the mess that the Lord endures, then you can understand why He reacts the way He does. The Flood wasn't God "throwing a fit" or losing His temper. It wasn't [overreacting ]{.class_s35S}or an "overkill." It was mankind getting exactly what it deserved for the atrocities it had committed.

The same thing is true of the coming judgment of the earth in the Tribulation. When the Lord finally "cuts loose," it will be CATASTROPHIC, CATACLYSMIC CARNAGE. And again, men will get exactly what's coming to them.

Brother, I sure am glad that I am on the right side!

Now we come to one of the key verses in the Campbellites "rosary" chain. If you have ever dealt with anyone from the Church of Christ, then you know that they run you in a circle of verses consisting of Acts 2:38; Mark 16:16; Romans 6:1--3; Galatians 3:27; and 1 Peter 3:21. Some of them will also work in Ephesians 4:5; John 3:5; and some verses from James []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_356}2:14--26. But 1 Peter 3:21 is a standard in their "ring around the rosie." Their two favorite parts of verses 20 and 21 are ["saved by water"]{.class_s35R} (vs. 20) and ["baptism doth also now save us"]{.class_s35R} without any reference to the context of either of those statements.

Let's get some things straight first.

1\) Baptism does not save [anyone ]{.class_s35S}in verse 21. It is a ["figure"]{.class_s35R} of your salvation that is ["like"]{.class_s35R} the account of Noah and his family being saved. If they were ["saved by water,"]{.class_s35R} then it certainly wasn't by being [immersed in it. ]{.class_s35S}And if baptism is a ["figure,"]{.class_s35R} then it is not the actual thing itself.

2\) Baptism has nothing to do with washing away [your sins]{.class_s35S} (Acts 22:16). Peter says ["NOT the putting away of the filth of the flesh."]{.class_s35R} That ["filth"]{.class_s35R} is defined in 2 Corinthians 7:1; James 1:21; 2 Peter 2:7; and Revelation 22:11. It is the moral filth of sin. So baptism [does not]{.class_s35S} put away your sin when you go under the water.

3\) Baptism is ["the answer of a good conscience toward God."]{.class_s35R} The conscience has nothing more to do with salvation than the Old Testament Law does. Both are made to show you how sinful you are [before ]{.class_s35S}salvation; that is all (Rom. 2, 3). Moreover, no unsaved man has a [good conscience]{.class_s35S} to which "to answer." The Apostle Paul said, ["Unto the pure all things are pure: but unto them that are defiled and UNBELIEVING is NOTHING pure; but even their mind and CONSCIENCE IS DEFILED"]{.class_s35R} (Titus 1:15).

If Peter ever did teach that baptism was necessary [to be]{.class_s35S}[ ]{.class_s366}saved (and it is mighty questionable that he did---see comments under Acts 2:38 and Rom. 3:25 in those Commentaries), there is no doubt as to what Peter taught by the time he wrote 1 Peter. Acts 15:11, Peter speaking, ["But we believe that through the GRACE of the Lord Jesus Christ we shall be saved, even []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_357}as they"]{.class_s35R} Acts 15:9, ["And put no difference between us and them, PURIFYING THEIR HEARTS BY FAITH."]{.class_s35R}

Peter taught exactly what Paul taught about salvation (Eph. 2:8--9) after Acts 15. [Baptism had nothing to do with it.]{.class_s35S}

Now what does Peter mean when he says, ["eight souls were saved by water. The like figure whereunto even baptism doth also now save us"]{.class_s35R}?[ ]{.class_s35R}Well, baptism "saves us" only inasmuch as it gives a [figure of what happened to us at salvation]{.class_s35S}. That "figure" is likened to what happened to Noah.

Did Noah get baptized? No! Did he get sprinkled? No! Did he get immersed? No!

Noah didn't even get wet.

If that's the case, a Campbellite is a fool to tell you that if a Church of Christ elder puts you underneath the water and brings you back up that you are saved. [If you are going to follow Noah's example, you are going to have to stay dry!]{.class_s35S}

To understand what Peter is saying here, you have to understand what baptism [pictures]{.class_s35S}. Baptism pictures death, burial, and resurrection (Rom. 6:1--4). When the preacher puts you under the water, that is [death]{.class_s35S}. When you are under the water, that is [burial]{.class_s35S}. When he brings you back up, that is [resurrection]{.class_s35S}. Baptism pictures, first of all, what you believed to be saved: you believed ["Christ died for our sins according to the scriptures; and that he was buried, and that he rose again the third day according to the scriptures"]{.class_s35R} (1 Cor. 15:3--4).

But more than that, baptism also pictures [what happened to you]{.class_s35S} when you received Christ, and this is where the similarities to Noah come in. When Noah went into the ark, he cut himself off from the rest of the world. Hebrews 11:7, ["By the which he condemned the world."]{.class_s35R} How did he do that? Because when God shut the door, no one from outside could get in, and the Lord brought the Flood ["upon the world of the ungodly"]{.class_s35R} (2 []{#c1ZK.xhtml_page_358}Pet. 2:5). It was the ones who were immersed in water that were destroyed, not Noah and his family (Luke 17:27).

When you got saved, you were put, by the Holy Spirit, ["into Jesus Christ"]{.class_s35R} (Rom. 6:3 cf. 1 Cor. 12:13). When you entered ["into Jesus Christ,"]{.class_s35R} you became a partaker of His death, burial, and resurrection (Rom. 6:3--4). The part of you that [died ]{.class_s35S}was the old sin nature, and a new nature lives in you now that was made possible by the resurrection of Jesus Christ. Romans 6:6--8, ["Knowing this, ]{.class_s35R}[that our old man is crucified with him, that the body of sin might be destroyed,]{.class_s35W-0}[ that henceforth we should not serve sin. For he that is dead is freed from sin. ]{.class_s35R}[Now if we be dead with Christ, we believe that we shall also live with him]{.class_s35W-0}[."]{.class_s35R}

Colossians 2:12--13, ["Buried with him in baptism,"]{.class_s35R} (Well, not literally, no; but spiritually and figuratively, yes.) ["wherein also ye are risen with him through the faith of the operation of God, who hath raised him from the dead. And you, being dead in your sins and the uncircumcision of your flesh, hath he quickened together with him, having forgiven you all trespasses."]{.class_s35R}

As long as Noah was [outside ]{.class_s35S}of the ark, he was under the judgment and condemnation of God along with the rest of the sinful world. When he got [into ]{.class_s35S}the ark, God's judgment fell on everyone [outside]{.class_s35S}, and Noah was saved [because the water killed all of that which would have condemned him and his family]{.class_s35S}.

A year later, Noah and those with him came out of the ark (which just happened to be shaped like a [coffin]{.class_s35S}, not a [boat]{.class_s35S}) to a new life, both for them and the earth and to new, unconditional promises that God would never judge him as He had done to those who died in the Flood. It was a picture of resurrection.

That is why, if you remove the parenthetical expression in verse 21, Peter says, ["The like figure whereunto even baptism doth also now save us\...BY THE RESURRECTION OF JESUS CHRIST."]{.class_s35R}
